401 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Jurisich v. Jenkins


97 CA 1870


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 1870 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/25/98); 722 So. 2d 1008; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3698



September 25, 1998, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Reported in Table Case Format at: 1998 La.App. LEXIS 3120.

On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 435-965. Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff oyster lease owners sought review of a judgment from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, that denied their request for the issuance of a preliminary injunction against defendant State prohibiting the insertion of certain clauses or stipulations in renewal leases.


OVERVIEW: On appeal the oyster lease owners argued that the trial court erred by denying their petition for preliminary injunction with respect to: (1) the navigation and oil field activity stipulation; (2) the future litigation stipulation; and (3) the wetlands stipulation consisting of the coastal wetlands restoration advisory clause and the allocation of risk, liability, and indemnification clause. The oyster lease owners failed to establish that the State acted in direct violation of the Louisiana constitution or prohibitory law. To the contrary, the Secretary of the Louisiana Department of Wildlife and Fisheries was specifically granted authority to include stipulations in oyster leases. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:425(C). Additionally, the secretary was afforded authority and discretion in determining whether to grant or renew oyster leases. Given the authority and discretion afforded the secretary, coupled with the great discretion afforded the trial judge to grant or deny a preliminary injunction, the appellate court determined the trial judge did not err in denying the preliminary injunction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

402 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Franklin


No. 31,068-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,068 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/23/98); 719 So. 2d 578; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2583



September 23, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 167,028. Honorable Ramona Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and sentenced him to 40 years at hard labor. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress, that the evidence was insufficient, that an excessive sentence was imposed, and that a mistrial should have been ordered.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by police in his vehicle because his rear taillight was not functioning. The police discovered a gun and 31 bags of crack cocaine in the vehicle. Defendant was found guilty of possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute and appealed. Upon review, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court found that defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied by the trial court because the search of defendant's vehicle was lawful. The court determined that the evidence presented at trial was apparently accepted by the jury and was sufficient to support defendant's conviction. Defendant's sentence was not excessive because the trial judge adequately considered the criteria set forth by La. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 and sufficiently examined the circumstances of the case and the background of defendant. The court concluded that the record clearly supported the enhanced sentence of 40 years at hard labor. The court held that there was no error in failing to grant defendant's motion for a mistrial, as the trial court admonished the jury to disregard a witness' comment about prior crimes and the remark did not deny defendant a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and sentence of 40 years at hard labor as a habitual offender.

 

403 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


City of Ruston v. Perritt


No. 30,896-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,896 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/23/98); 718 So. 2d 1044; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2598



September 23, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 43,355. Honorable Cynthia T. Woodard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mayor sought review of a judgment from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln (Louisiana), which denied her petition for attorney fees and costs following the dismissal of a rule for contempt filed against her by appellee city. The city and the city attorney sought damages for a frivolous appeal.


OVERVIEW: The mayor was involved in a dispute with the city board concerning the passage of city ordinances. The mayor filed a suit for a preliminary injunction prohibiting the city board from enforcing one of the ordinances. The trial court upheld the ordinance and ordered the mayor to submit nominations to the city board for a utilities director within 30 days. Thereafter, the city attorney filed a rule of contempt against the mayor for failing to make a timely nomination. The trial court dismissed the rule for contempt, and the mayor sought reimbursement for attorney fees and costs under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42.261(E). The trial court denied the request and the mayor appealed. The court affirmed and held that § 42.261(E), as previously declared unconstitutional, was unconstitutional in its entirety and not in part. The court ruled that La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 863, which granted authority for sanctions when pleadings were note well-grounded, did not apply because the city was not entirely without justification in its claims. Finally, the court held that the city and city attorney were not entitled to damages for a frivolous appeal because the mayor genuinely advocated her claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of trial court denying the mayor's petition for attorney fees and costs. The court also denied the demands of the city and the city attorney for frivolous appeal damages.

 

404 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jordan


No. 97-KA-1756


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1756 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/16/98); 719 So. 2d 556; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2639



September 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 30, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 382-898, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish No. 382-898, Section I (Louisiana), which convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant asserted that the trial court committed numerous errors.


OVERVIEW: Three men were indicted for the first-degree murder of a 12-year-old boy after he was killed in a drive-by shooting. Defendant was tried separately and was convicted. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed. The court found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 (A)(1), (3), relating to drive-by shootings, was not vague or overly broad because a person of ordinary intelligence could easily discern its meaning and its description of those covered. As to the contested statements of the prosecutor, the court stated that the trial judge reprimanded counsel but defendant failed to request an admonition or mistrial. Thus, defendant could not complain of the alleged error on appeal. The court ruled that the trial court did not err in permitting another defendant involved in the murder to take a blanket Fifth Amendment privilege and in refusing defendant's request that the other defendant take the stand in front of the jury to assert the privilege. The other defendant's conviction was not final so that there was exposure to further criminal liability. The court held that the trial court properly charged the jury and that there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for first degree murder.

 

405 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Hoolahan v. Munch


No. 98-CA-199 C/W No. 98-CA-200


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-199 (La.App. 5 Cir. 09/16/98); 719 So. 2d 1094; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2649



September 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 40,702 C/W 41,133 - DIVISION "C". HONORABLE EMILE ST. PIERRE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured person appealed from the judgment of the 29th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant State Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD), dismissing her claims against DOTD for injuries suffered in an accident allegedly caused by a missing stop sign.


OVERVIEW: The injured person contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800, which required actual or constructive knowledge by the State before strict liability could attach to a public body under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2317, was an unconstitutional resurrection of sovereign immunity. However, the court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 was not unconstitutional, because it did not limit a plaintiff's right to sue the state for damages, or limit the amount of damages recoverable against the State. Furthermore, it was in effect at time of the accident, notwithstanding that some courts had declared it unconstitutional, because the Louisiana Supreme Court ultimately determined to it be constitutional. The court then held that summary judgment had been properly granted, because affidavits established that DOTD did not have actual notice of the stop sign's absence at the intersection, and the injured person had not submitted countervailing affidavits regarding the State's notice of the missing stop sign.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted summary judgment to DOTD.

 

406 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Louisiana Seafood Mgmt. Council v. Louisiana Wildlife & Fisheries Comm'n


97 CA 1344


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97-1344 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/01/98): 719 So. 2d 119; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2645



September 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 2, 1998. Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5763.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 419,467), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE JANICE CLARK, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, commercial fishermen and seafood marketers and restaurateurs and consumers, petitioned for class certification and injunctive and declaratory relief from 1995 La. Acts 1316. Conservationists intervened. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana found parts of the act unconstitutional, some of which findings were reversed. Plaintiffs appealed the trial court's findings of constitutionality.


OVERVIEW: Through restrictions on the use of gill nets in the harvesting of saltwater finfish, Act 1316 impacted the availability of such fish for markets both within and outside of Louisiana. Plaintiffs argued that the public trust doctrine of La. Const. art. IX, § 1 required equitable distribution of such fish among fishermen; that commercial fishermen were vested with an incorporeal right to fish using current legal harvesting methods unless biological data supported an alteration of that right; and that the act violated substantive due process, equal protection, and the commerce clause. The appellate court found that Act 1316 was the legislature's exercise of its § 1 mandate. The mandates of La. Rev. Stat. §§ 56:638.3 - .5, part of the amended statute, were directed to the Louisiana Wildlife and Fisheries Commission rather than to the legislature. Plaintiffs failed to show fish caught were inequitably allocated between recreational and commercial fishermen. The latter lacked a property interest in the "right to fish." The incidental burden on interstate commerce of fewer finfish was not greater than the effect within state and did not outweigh the environmental protection interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

407 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. Dixie Elec. Mbrshp. Corp.


No. 30,483-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,483 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/21/98); 717 So. 2d 691; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2458



August 21, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 22, 1998. As Corrected October 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Helena, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 14078. Honorable Bruce C. Bennett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Helena (Louisiana), found that appellee prospective candidate was wrongfully prohibited from seeking candidacy for election to appellant board of directors. It also found the only approved candidate was ineligible to serve as a director. In a judgment upon remand, the trial court also found that the amendment of by-laws did not change those conclusions. The board of directors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prospective candidate sought a nomination for election to the corporate board. She alleged that under the old by-laws, she would not have been prohibited from seeking such election, even though her marriage to a public official would otherwise have prohibited it, because she had a separate membership. However, the by-laws were later amended to provide that a married person had a joint membership and both members had to be eligible to serve. The amended by-laws were in effect when the prospective candidate sought the nomination. The by-laws stated that they could be amended at any time. The trial court ruled that the board of directors wrongfully prohibited her from seeking the nomination, and also found another individual ineligible to serve because his business primarily engaged in selling items to the corporation's members. After judgment was entered, the appellate court found she did not have a vested right to the nomination and was not wrongfully prohibited from seeking it under the amended by-laws. It further found the evidence did not show that the other individual was ineligible to serve, as he was not "primarily engaged" in sales to the corporation's members.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the prospective candidate was reversed, as was that part of the judgment finding that the only approved candidate was ineligible to serve. All of the claims of the prospective candidate were denied and were dismissed with prejudice.

State v. Self


NUMBER CR98-39


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-39 (La.App. 3 Cir. 08/19/98); 719 So. 2d 100; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2454



August 19, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Eleventh Judicial District Court [No. 47,308], for the Parish of Sabine, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Stephen Beasley, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the 11th Judicial Court for the Parish of Sabine, State of Louisiana, which convicted defendant of aggravated rape of a child under 12 years of age, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with one count of aggravated rape of a child under 12 years of age, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42. The trial court convicted defendant. On appeal, defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred when it accepted the jury's non-unanimous verdict of 11 to1. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case. The court held that: (1) evidence was sufficient to support a conviction if, when the evidence was viewed in the light most favorable to the prosecution, any rational trier of fact could conclude that the prosecution proved the essential elements of a crime beyond a reasonable doubt; (2) the prosecution satisfactorily proved the required element of penetration; (3) a criminal case in which the punishment might be capital had to be tried before a jury of 12 people, all of whom had to concur in the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of aggravated rape of a child under 12 years of age, set aside the conviction, and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Cosby


No. 31,073-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


31,073 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/19/98); 717 So. 2d 279; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2428



August 19, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 60,002. Honorable Cecil P. Campbell, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster ( Louisiana), which sentenced him to a term of five years at hard labor and denied a timely motion for reconsideration after he pled guilty to possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a prior conviction for aggravated battery and a lengthy history of misdemeanor offenses, which were thefts or substance abuse-related crimes. Defendant was found in possession of numerous items of drug paraphernalia, which had cocaine residue, and he pled guilty to possession of cocaine in exchange for the State's agreement to dismiss an unrelated charge of middle-grade theft. The trial court sentenced him to a term of five years at hard labor. Defendant filed a timely motion for reconsideration, which was denied, contending that the sentence was excessive. On appeal, the court held that the trial court had duly considered the mitigating and aggravating factors as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 and found that defendant was deserving of the maximum sentence of five years. The court also held that the trial court had not abused its discretion in imposing the sentence, which was not unconstitutionally excessive, because it was not so disproportionate to the severity of the crime as to shock the sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence for his conviction of possession of cocaine.

Bailey v. Parish of Caddo


No. 30,822-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,822 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/19/98); 716 So. 2d 523; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2442



August 19, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 6, 1998. Released for Publication September 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 402,601. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of the decision from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which affirmed the actions of appellees, a planning commission and a parish, in granting appellee adjacent landowners' request to subdivide their lot.


OVERVIEW: The landowners filed a complaint with the planning commission protesting a zoning certificate that gave the adjacent landowners permission to build three houses on their single lot. The adjacent landowners then applied for a formal resubdivision of the lot. The planning commission granted the resubdivision. The landowners appealed the decision to the parish and the parish upheld the planning commission's decision. The trial court affirmed the actions of the planning commission and the parish. In affirming on appeal, the court held that: (1) where the houses built on the adjacent landowners' property were compatible with other houses in the area, the commission and parish did not abuse their discretion in finding that subdividing the lot would not effect a change in the character of the area; (2) the trial court was entitled to find that prior denials of zoning permits did not involve similar situations; (3) because the landowners did not serve the Attorney General as to state constitutional issues raised, they were not entitled to consideration of those issues; and (4) the evidence showed that the final vote on the resubdivision was taken in an open meeting with adequate notice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court, which upheld the actions of the planning commission and parish in granting the adjacent landowners' request to subdivide their lot.

 

411 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


In re Brinkman


No. 98-CA-0159


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-0159 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/05/98); 717 So. 2d 681; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2547



August 5, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 82-16074, DIVISION "J, "DRS2"". HONORABLE NADINE M. RAMSEY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State sought review of a judgment from the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), in the State's rule to make child support arrearages of defendant father executory, which held that the claim for payments more than five years in arrears prescribed. The State claimed that the action was subject to a 10-year liberative prescription and the trial court should have awarded a greater sum.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a rule to make the father's child support arrearages executory. The record was unclear as to the date of the father's last payment. The trial court held that the claim for payments more than five years in arrears prescribed pursuant to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3497.1 (1994). The State sought review and claimed that the action was subject to a 10-year liberative prescription. The appeal record did not contain an exception of prescription, which had to be specially pleaded under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 927(B). The court held that: (1) La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3501.1 (1997) became effective after the arrearages arose; (2) when the claim prescribed, the right to plead the exception of prescription constituted a substantive change in the law; (3) art. 3501.1 did not indicate legislative intent to apply the prescriptive period to revive a cause of action that had already prescribed; and (5) on the record, the court could not determine whether prescription was interrupted for arrearages over five years and whether that claim prescribed before the enactment of art. 3501.1.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment for the State in its action to make the father's child support arrearages executory insofar as it disallowed payments over five years, and remanded the cause for a determination of the date of the father's last payment and whether the claim for arrearages beyond five years prescribed.

 

412 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Pommier v. Savoy Mem'l Hosp.


NUMBER 97-1342


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-1342 (La.App. 3 Cir. 07/15/98); 715 So. 2d 1270; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1743



July 15, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Thirteenth Judicial District Court [No. 51,110-B], for the Parish of Evangeline, State of Louisiana; the Honorable A. Gaynor Soileau, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 51110-B.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Thirteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Evangeline, State of Louisiana, granted plaintiff patient judgment in a medical malpractice case against defendants, hospital, insurance company, and hospital staff. The hospital, insurance company, and hospital staff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient filed a medical malpractice action against defendants, hospital, insurance company, and hospital staff, for a left leg peroneal nerve injury that occurred during her hospitalization for a total right hip replacement surgery. The trial court granted the patient judgment against the hospital staff. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in applying the res ipsa loquitur doctrine. Peroneal nerve injury on a contralateral leg was a recognized complication of hip replacement surgery. As such, this fact could not be discounted by the trial court as a possible cause of the injury. Patient's proof did not rebut this fact, and she could not do so in view of her experts' agreement that it was true. In finding liability, the trial court held the hospital vicariously liable for its employees' conduct. Regardless, the court found the record contained sufficient evidence of fault and affirmed the judgment, but modified and remanded for assignment of fault and determination of the constitutionality of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2323, which allowed non-parties to be held at fault.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as modified and remanded the judgment granting plaintiff patient judgment in a medical malpractice case against defendants, hospital, insurance company, and hospital staff. The trial court erred in applying the res ipsa loquitur doctrine, but the record contained evidence of fault. Remand was necessary to apportion fault and to determine the constitutionality of the statute allowing apportionment of fault to non-parties.

In re Medical Review Panel for Claim of Brown


No. 97-CA-2803


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-2803 (La.App. 4 Cir. 7/1/98); 715 So. 2d 1249; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2523



July 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released For Publication August 13, 1998
Certiorari Denied April 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2360.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 95-13006, DIVISION "G".


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party's parents sought review of a judgment from the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division G (Louisiana), which dismissed their medical malpractice action against defendants, two doctors and a hospital, based on prescription.


OVERVIEW: The doctors removed a mass from the right breast of the parents' child. When the child reached puberty, her left breast developed but her right breast did not. On appeal, the parents argued that (1) prescription was interrupted due to the child's continual treatment by defendants; and (2) they were entitled to an evidentiary ruling from the trial court on whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 was unconstitutional as applied to the child. Upon review, the court found the parents' arguments without merit. The record contained no evidence of a continuous relationship between the child and defendants. Medical records submitted by the parents showed that the child was an inpatient for the 1985 surgery and that she returned to the hospital in 1993 and 1994. The consequence of the surgery did not physically manifest until the child reached puberty more than eight years after removal of the breast tissue. Suit was filed nearly nine years after the alleged malpractice. The parents' complaint required dismissal under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the parents' medical malpractice suit against the doctors and the hospital.

Horseshoe Entertainment v. Bossier Parish Police Jury


No. 30,502-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,502 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/26/98); 714 So. 2d 920; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1665



June 26, 1998, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 92,839. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, two riverboats engaged in gambling, sought review of the order from the 26th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana), which entered judgment in favor of appellee Bossier Parish Police Jury in the riverboats' action for a declaratory judgment that a $ .50 cent boarding fee was invalid.


OVERVIEW: By resolution, the police jury had approved an agreement whereby riverboats paid a fixed amount in lieu of a per person boarding fee and in lieu of any future legislative modifications regarding distribution of riverboat gaming revenue in return for a $ 300,000 annual payment from each boat. Thereafter, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:552 (now § 27:93) was amended to authorize a $ .50 admission fee. This additional $ .50 was allocated to go to the parish road fund. The trial court found that the amendment that authorized the $ .50 boarding fee was not a special or local law and that it would be against public policy to allow the police jury to enter into a binding agreement restricting and preventing the legislature from, in the future, granting them the authority to assess a fee. On appeal, the court affirmed that part of the judgment but disagreed with the finding that the police jury, rather than city, was the "local governing authority" authorized to impose the $ .50 admission fee. The court found that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:552, the legislature authorized the "local governing authority" of the parish or municipality where a riverboat was berthed to charge an admission fee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the police jury and rendered judgment in favor of the riverboats, declaring that the ordinance of the police jury imposing a $ .50 per person admission fee was invalid.

 

415 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Reid v. Commission on Ethics for Pub. Emples.


No. 30,655-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,655 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/26/98); 715 So. 2d 700; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1667



June 26, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 13, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 418,297. Honorable Charles R. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment from the District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), granted the exception filed by appellee, commission on Ethics for Public Employees, and held that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the employee's complaint that challenged the commission's procedural actions against him.


OVERVIEW: The commission conducted an investigation into allegations that the employee had possibly committed violations of the Code of Governmental Ethics. The employee signed a consent agreement and agreed to pay the fine imposed by the commission. The employee filed a petition with the trial court for alleged damages that resulted from the commission's adverse decision. The trial court found that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction to adjudicate the employee's claim. The employee appealed and argued that his original and amended petitions specifically challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1141(C)(2) and not just the procedural actions taken by the commission. The court held that when the commission decided to accept the consent agreement and to dispense with the public hearing, the arguments raised by the employee were no longer at issue and were rendered moot. The court concluded that the employee's complaint was based solely on the administrative and procedural actions taken by the commission and that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1142 provided for the correct forum for the employee's appeal, which was not with the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

416 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr.


No. 30,715-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,715 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/24/98); 714 So. 2d 895; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1634



June 24, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 730 So. 2d 450, 1998 La. LEXIS 3422 (La., Nov. 13, 1998)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Walker v. Bossier Med. Ctr., 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1167 (La.App. 2 Cir., May 12, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 95383. Honorable Ford E. Stinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED, AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a patient and her husband, sought review of a decision by the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana), which sustained appellee medical center's exception of prescription in appellants' medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: In 1981, the patient received a blood transfusion at the medical center. In 1992, the patient learned that she suffered from Hepatitis C, the source of which was the blood transfusion. The patient and her husband brought a medical malpractice action against the medical center. The medical center filed a peremptory exception of prescription on the basis that the medical malpractice prescription statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628, barred the claim. The trial court sustained the exception and appellants sought review. The court affirmed. The court rejected appellants' claim that their action sounded in products liability, rather than medical malpractice, and was not barred by the medical malpractice statute of limitations. The court found that the Medical Malpractice Act was amended in 1976 to include actions for injuries incurred as the result of receiving transfusions of contaminated blood products. Because the patient's transfusion took place after 1976, her claim was one for medical malpractice. As a result of the amendment, the court said, appellants' claims were subject to all of the special provisions of the Act, including the prescriptive period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, as amended, a decision that sustained the medical center's exception of prescription to appellants' medical malpractice claim.

 

417 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Serrano


No. 97-KA-0923


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


715 So. 2d 602; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1736



June 17, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 382-709, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE JAMES F. MCKAY III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish No. 382-709, Division "H" (Louisiana), which convicted him of intentionally knowing and exposing another to the HIV virus in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to quash the bill of information on the ground that § 14:43.5 was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant was convicted of violating the statute. In affirming, the court rejected defendant's argument that § 14:43.5 was unconstitutionally vague on the ground that it penalized the intentional exposure of another to the "AIDS virus" where there was no such thing as an AIDS virus. The court noted that the defense's expert admitted that he had heard the term "AIDS virus" used even though there was a distinction between the HIV virus and AIDS. The court held that the language of the statute was not vague because it communicated that its intent was to criminalize the intentional transmission of the virus that caused AIDS. Moreover, the court held that the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant intentionally exposed the victim to the virus that caused AIDS through sexual contact and without her knowledge or lawful consent. The evidence showed that defendant signed a form acknowledging that he was HIV-positive, but never told the victim about it during their sexual relationship that post-dated the acknowledgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

418 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dixon


No. 98-KA-0090


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-0090 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/03/98); 712 So. 2d 1078; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1594



June 03, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 28, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 385-543, SECTION "G". HONORABLE JULIAN A. PARKER, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE DISTRICT COURT VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with multiple offenses of armed robbery. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) granted defendant's motion to quash information seeking to try defendant as an adult. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: At a hearing, counsel for the juvenile stipulated as to probable cause. At that hearing the assistant district attorney informed the trial court that the matter was being considered for transfer to Criminal District Court where the defendant, a 15 year old juvenile, would be prosecuted as an adult. At his arraignment, defendant pleaded not guilty. Defense counsel filed a motion to quash the bill of information and after a hearing, and the trial court granted the motion to quash, ordering the matter transferred to juvenile court. The state objected and subsequently made unsuccessful applications for writs three times and filed an appeal. Defendant contended that the state failed to give proper notice to defendant and his parents regarding its intent to try defendant as a adult, and had no authority to do so. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the trial court's order quashing the information, finding that pursuant to La. Child Code arts. 305, 857 and 858, the district attorney was "expressly empowered" with "complete discretion" to file a bill of information in criminal court or a petition in juvenile court.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment granting defendant's motion to quash the information was vacated and the matter remanded.

 

419 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Bishop v. Lakeland Med. Ctr.


No. 97-CA-2849


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-2849 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/03/98); 715 So. 2d 541; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1600



June 3, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 28, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION. NO. 96-00960, DISTRICT 8. HON. GWENDOLYN R. THOMPSON, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged an order of the Office of Workers' Compensation (Louisiana), which dismissed her claim against defendant employer for workers' compensation benefits pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 (E) upon finding that she willfully made a false statement or representation during the hearing on her claims.


OVERVIEW: The employee injured her wrist while in the course of her employment. She filed a claim for workers' compensation benefits contending that she was temporarily totally disabled. At trial, she testified that she had not worked since she left the employer. The worker's compensation judge dismissed the employee's claim because she failed to disclose that she was working as a sitter. The court affirmed and held that the judge did not err in ordering forfeiture of the employee's benefits pursuant to § 23:1208(E). Although the employee testified that she did not work for anyone, her own rebuttal witness testified that she was paying the employee to care for her children everyday. That had been going on for the entire year before the trial. The employee's testimony demonstrated that she had no difficulty understanding the questions put to her. The judge had the opportunity to observe her at close hand and was in a unique position to conclude that she was intentionally concealing the fact that she had the ability to do some work and was in fact gainfully employed. The employee's false statements were not inadvertent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the employee's claim for workers' compensation benefits.

 

420 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


No. 97-KA-269


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-269 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/27/98); 713 So. 2d 828; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1372



May 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, NO. 97-6087, DIVISION "P, HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED, REMANDED FOR RE-SENTENCING. CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED, REMANDED FOR RE-SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) convicted defendant of simple robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:65, adjudicated defendant to be a third felony offender, and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction stemmed his snatching money from the hand of a cashier at a restaurant's drive-up window. On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, arguing that the state failed to show that he used force or intimidation. Defendant also complained that the trial court erred in refusing his requested jury charge regarding simple robbery and improperly instructed the jury as to the elements of simple robbery. Finally, defendant complained that his life sentence was constitutionally excessive. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, but vacated his sentenced and remanded for resentencing. The state proved the essential elements of the offense because the victim testified that he was intimidated by defendant. The trial court properly instructed the jury on the elements of simple robbery and defendant's requested charge was sufficiently included in the general charge. The trial judge imposed an illegal sentence on defendant, in violation of the Ex Post Facto clause, by sentencing defendant under a version of the multiple offender statute that did not become effective until after defendant committed the simple robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for simple robbery, but vacated his multiple offender sentence and remanded for resentencing under the version of the multiple offender statute in effect at the time defendant convicted the underlying offense.

 

421 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bowers


No. 97-KA-1029


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-1029 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/27/98); 712 So. 2d 302; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1368



May 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 96-4157, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO II, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana in favor of the State of Louisiana, after a jury verdict, which convicted him of armed robbery, under La. Rev. Stat. § 14:64, and sentenced him to 17 years at hard labor with 7 years to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The district court denied defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a juvenile, had been tried as an adult. Defendant's trial counsel had not appeared at the hearing on his motion to reconsider the sentence. On appeal, the court held that since the record did not show that defendant's mother had prevented him from entering into a plea bargain that he had wanted, it could not consider that issue on appeal. The court found that defendant's excessive sentence claim had been preserved by filing the motion to reconsider the sentence, pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1(D). Thus, the court held that there had been no prejudice from his counsel's failure to appear and his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was without merit. The court found that it was error, under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 873, for the trial judge to impose the sentence less than 24 hours after denying the motion for a new trial, since defendant had not waived the statutory delay period. Even though the conviction for armed robbery carried a mandatory prison sentence, the court noted that the trial judge still had to determine the number of years to be imposed. Thus, the court held defendant had been prejudiced by the early imposition of the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment in favor of the State, which had convicted defendant of armed robbery, but reversed defendant's sentence and remanded for re-sentencing.

Hall v. House, Golden, Kingsmill & Riess


No. 97-CA-988


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-988 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/27/98); 717 So. 2d 250; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1387



May 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 8, 1998.
Rehearing Denied July 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM DISTRICT O7 OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION ADMINISTRATION. STATE OF LOUISIANA, NO. 93-00272. HONORABLE ANNE MARIE VANDENWEGHE, HEARING OFFICER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the employer and insurance companies, challenged the judgment of the District 07 Office of Workers' Compensation Administration, State of Louisiana, which held in favor of plaintiff individual and found that the deceased employee was abducted while in the course and scope of his employment.


OVERVIEW: The employee was abducted in a parking lot and later murdered. The trial judge found that the employee was in the course and scope of his employment when abducted. The court affirmed and amended the judgment. Close calls in workers' compensation cases were usually made in favor of the employee. The court could not say that the judgment was manifestly wrong in finding that the employee's work place, considering all relevant aspects and particulars, extended to the parking lot. The threshold doctrine was an exception to the general rule that when an employee was traveling to and from work he was not covered by workers' compensation. The threshold doctrine was properly applied when an accident occurred at a place with an unusually hazardous travel risk which was immediately adjacent to, but not on, the employer's premises. The court amended the judgment to include an award for burial expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, as amended, in favor of the individual in the workers' compensation action against the employer and insurance companies.

 

423 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Louisiana Dep't of Agric. & Forestry v. Sumrall


NUMBER 97 CA 0288


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


712 So. 2d 678; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1790



May 15, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 423, 082. Honorable A. Foster Sanders, III, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Agriculture sought review of the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana which granted the summary judgment motion filed by defendant Civil Service Commission in a declaratory judgment action to decree certain Civil Service Rules unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The department sought a declaratory judgment that Civil Service Rules 1.14.1, 13.10(c), 13.10(e), 13.10(h), 13.10(k), 13.10(1), and 14.1(a) were unconstitutional insofar as they purported to authorize a right of appeal from discrimination other than discrimination based upon a classified employee's political or religious beliefs, sex or race, as provided in La. Const. art. X. The commission asserted that it was given broad authority for the administration and regulation of the state classified service under art. X, and the district court granted the commission's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the summary dismissal of the petition. The court held that La. Const. art. X, § 8(B) did not provide an exclusive listing of bases for civil service appeals based on discrimination because district courts would be precluded from entertaining discrimination claims under La. Const. art. X, which would thwart the entire civil service scheme. At most, La. Const. art. X, § 8(B) guaranteed a constitutional right to appeal in its listed discriminations. The commission had the power to expand prohibited discrimination under the broad and general rule-making power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the commission, dismissing the department's declaratory judgment action to declare certain civil service rules unconstitutional.

In re Succession of Jones


No. 97 CA 1428


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


712 So. 2d 640; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1768



May 15, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 9330143. Honorable M. Douglas Hughes, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandson sought review of the decision of the Twenty-first Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, State of Louisiana, which found that he was not a forced heir to the succession of his grandfather and dismissed the grandson's petition of intervention in the succession proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The grandson filed a petition of intervention seeking to be recognized as a forced heir and declaratory judgment in the succession proceedings of his grandfather. In response, appellee surviving wife filed a peremptory exception raising the objection of no cause of action. The trial court granted the peremptory exception and dismissed the grandson's intervention. The grandson asserted that because his mother had been disinherited and he was the only grandchild, he was entitled to inherit in his own right as the nearest heir in the direct line of descendants. The court found that the trial court was correct when it determined that the grandson was not a forced heir. The court found that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493 imposed a requirement that descendants beyond the first degree only became forced heirs through their representation of a predeceased child of a decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding that the grandson was not a forced heir to the succession of his grandfather.

Fields v. Lofton


NUMBER 97 CA 0884


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


712 So. 2d 268; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1775



May 15, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge State of Louisiana. Suit No. 417,424. Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third party plaintiff sellers challenged a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, which granted a summary judgment in favor of third party defendant City of Zachary and dismissed the City. The sellers urged that the immunity granted in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4771 was barred by the Louisiana Constitution as it existed prior to 1995.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff buyers filed an action against the sellers, seeking damages on the basis that water leakage from the attic of their home rendered it materially defective and substandard. The sellers filed a third party demand against the City alleging that any liability owed to the buyers arose out of the City's failure to perform its regular duty to inspect and grant a building permit in accordance with 1992 proper standards. The City filed a motion for summary judgment. It asserted that pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 33:4771, 33:4773, it was immune from liability. It relied on the theory that the 1995 amendment to the Louisiana Constitutional provision regarding sovereign immunity was curative of any constitutional infirmity in § 33:4771 et seq and the statute referred to therein. The district court granted the motion and dismissed the City. On appeal, the court found it unnecessary and improper to address the constitutional issue and affirmed. The plain wording of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. tit. 33 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4773(D) made it clear that the sellers did not and could not state a cause of action against the City for any act of the building inspector.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and assessed the costs of the appeal.

Revere v. Canulette


NUMBER 97 CA 0552


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


715 So. 2d 47; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1791



May 15, 1998, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From The 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany State of Louisiana. Suit Numbers 94-13866-E c/w 95-13040-D and 95-14940-C. Honorable A. Clayton James, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner appealed the judgment from the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which, in three consolidated cases, dismissed his petitions for writs of mandamus and civil penalties against defendant sheriff in the prisoner's actions, which sought radio logs, photographs, and employment records of former employees.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner filed the petitions to obtain the radio logs, the photographs, and the termination or retirement records of the department's former employees. After the trial court dismissed the petitions, the prisoner appealed. The court reversed the dismissal for the records and reinstated a judgment that granted access to the records. The prisoner sufficiently raised the exception of res judicata in his objection to the consolidation. The consolidation was improper. The matter became final when no appeal was taken from the judgment that granted access to the records. The court affirmed the dismissal for the radio logs and the photographs. The denial of the claim for the radio logs under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:31.1 did not violate either the equal protection clause or due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. The prisoner did prove that the state had no appropriate governmental interest in the photographs. The trial court was correct in determining that § 44:31.1, as applied to the photographs, was not an unconstitutional violation of Article I, Section 3 of the Louisiana Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the prisoner's petitions for the writs of mandamus and civil penalties against the sheriff for the radio logs and the photographs. The court reversed the dismissal of the prisoner's petitions for the employment records and reinstated a judgment that granted the prisoner access to the records.

Catanese v. Louisiana Gaming Control Bd.


97 CA 1426


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


712 So. 2d 666; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1752



May 15, 1998, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 437,557, Division "A". Honorable Robert D. Downing, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Louisiana Gaming Control Board and Louisiana State Police, Riverboat Gaming Enforcement Division, sought review of a decision of the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, that reversed decisions of the Division and Board not to renew appellant applicant's permit to work as a non-key gaming employee with a riverboat casino pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 27:76(3).


OVERVIEW: The renewal application was denied because the applicant had pleaded guilty to an offense punishable by imprisonment for a period of more than one year and was a person whose prior activities and criminal record posed a threat to the effective regulation and control of gaming. On appeal from the Board's decision, the trial court concluded that as a result of a first offender pardon, the applicant's first offense felony conviction ceased to exist and that he was therefore, not rendered ineligible for a permit by § 27:76(3). On appeal from that decision, the court found that § 27:76(3) provided that the Division could not award a permit to any person disqualified on the basis of a prior felony conviction. The applicant argued that pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 20, his citizenship rights were restored after he was automatically pardoned for his first offense pursuant to La. Const. art. IV, § 5(E)(1). In reversing the trial court, the court held that despite his first offender pardon, the historical fact of the applicant's felony conviction was extant and that the legislature's clear intent was to deny a permit to anyone convicted of even one felony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and reinstated the Board's decision not to renew the applicant's gaming permit.

State v. Hardy


No. 98-KA-25


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


98-25 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/13/98); 715 So. 2d 466; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1161



May 13, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 17, 1998, Reported at: 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1745.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 96-7131, DIVISION "I". THE HONORABLE JO ELLEN GRANT, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED; MOTION TO STRIKE DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which entered judgment of her conviction for distribution of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A, and which sentenced her as a second offender to 25 years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant also filed a motion to strike portions of the record.


OVERVIEW: After a sanity hearing, defendant was found competent to stand trial on a charge of distribution of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A. Defendant's motion to quash the information, based upon alleged government misconduct, and her motion to suppress, were denied. Defendant was found guilty as charged and sentenced as a second offender to 25 years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. In affirming the judgment, the court held that defendant's motion to quash was properly denied because the evidence demonstrated the she was an active participant in the criminal activity, and thus could not avail herself to the defense of government misconduct. The court held that defendant could not have proven an entrapment defense because a rational trier of fact could have found that defendant was not sufficiently induced to buy cocaine and that she was predisposed to commit the offense. The court amended defendant's sentence to conform with the statute under which she was convicted, which specified at La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(B)(4)(b) that only the first five years of the sentence was to be served without parole eligibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court amended defendant's sentence to reflect that only the first five years of her sentence were to be served without parole eligibility, and then affirmed the sentence as amended. The court denied defendant's motion to strike.

Doe v. Southern Baptist Hosp.


No. 98-C-0063


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


98-0063 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/06/98); 717 So. 2d 654; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1215



May 6, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON SUPERVISORY WRITS DIRECTED TO CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 93-1328, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff relators sought review of a decision of the Civil District Court, for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which ruled that that La. Rev. Stat. § 9:5628 applied to the relators' medical malpractice action against defendant hospital, but pretermitted entering judgment pending the relators' challenge to the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The relators asserted a medical malpractice action against the hospital alleging that their daughter was transfused with HIV-infected blood while a patient. The hospital filed an exception of prescription pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. § 9:5628. The trial court ruled that the statute applied but pretermitted entering judgment pending the relators' challenge to the constitutionality of the statute. On appeal, the relators complained that the trial court erred in concluding that § 9:5628 did not discriminate on the basis of physical condition and in placing the burden of proving the statute's unconstitutionality on them. The court articulated the presumption that statutes were constitutional and the rule that the burden of proving unconstitutionality rested upon the party challenging the validity of the statute. The court found that § 9:5628 did not classify individuals according to physical condition and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that the medical malpractice statute of limitations did not discriminate on the basis of physical condition and correctly placed the burden of proving the statute's unconstitutionality on the realtors. The court denied the relief sought by the relators.

 

430 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Leger v. Coccaro


No. 98-202


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-202 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/29/98); 714 So. 2d 770; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1105



April 29, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT [No. 1048], PARISH OF ACADIA, STATE OF LOUISIANA, THE HONORABLE RONALD D. COX, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father sought review of a decision of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Acadia, State of Louisiana, which granted an intrafamily adoption of his minor son to plaintiff stepfather. The stepfather and the child's mother had filed a petition for intrafamily adoption with the trial court.


OVERVIEW: In connection with the divorce of the father and the mother, the mother was awarded custody of their child. Thereafter, the stepfather and the mother filed a petition for intrafamily adoption of the minor son with the trial court. The trial court granted the intrafamily adoption, holding that the father had failed to pay child support for one year, the father had lost the right to object to the adoption, and that the adoption was in the child's best interest. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and denied the stepfather's petition for intrafamily adoption. The court held (1) that the trial court did not err in finding that the father had lost the right to object to an intrafamily adoption due to his failure to support the child, as the record reflected that the father had adequate income to pay child support and did not and that the father knew where the mother was and still did not send support; and (2) that the trial court erred in finding that an intrafamily adoption by the stepfather was in the child's best interest, as it was clear that a natural parent relationship existed and the father's failure to visit the child was justified due to the resistance of the mother.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of the stepfather's petition for an intrafamily adoption of the minor child. The court also denied the petition for intrafamily adoption of the child by the stepfather.

State v. Delcambre


NUMBER Cr97-1447


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-1447 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/29/98); 710 So. 2d 846; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1104



April 29, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, No. 8374-97/8375- 97, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, Honorable Alcide Gray, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash indictments that charged him with unauthorized use of a movable valued in excess of $ 1000 and with malfeasance in office.


OVERVIEW: The offenses were allegedly committed during defendant's tenure as a state trooper. The State claimed that the trial court erred in disregarding the mandatory language of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 442 and in quashing the indictments because the prosecution used defendant's statements before the grand jury that had been given to State Police Internal Affairs investigators. The court found that the grant of use plus derivative use immunity by the investigators to defendant was binding on the prosecutor, but that quashing the indictments was not the appropriate mechanism for enforcing the immunity agreement. The court reversed the trial court's order because art. 442 prohibited dismissing the indictments on the grounds that they were based in whole or in part on illegal evidence. The court ruled that the statements likely would have been considered illegal evidence at trial because defendant had been compelled to give them by threat of termination and they had been given in exchange for a promise of use plus derivative use immunity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted defendant's motion to quash and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

432 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Cooks v. Rodenbeck


NUMBER 97-1389


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-1389 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/29/98); 711 So. 2d 444; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1112



April 29, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides. (Docket No. 182,300), State of Louisiana, the Honorable B. C. Bennett, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff material witness sought review of a decision of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, which dismissed his action against defendants, a city and certain officers. Defendants sought review of the trial court's rejection of their motions for sanctions. Defendants also had sought damages for frivolous appeal. The material witness had filed an action against defendants for false arrest and imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: In connection with the material witness's imprisonment under an arrest warrant for 56 days, the material witness filed an action against defendants. The material witness asserted claims of false arrest and imprisonment. Defendants filed motions for summary judgment. The material witness also filed motions for partial summary judgment. The trial court granted defendants' motions for summary judgment and implicitly rejected defendants' motions for sanctions against the material witness. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held (1) that as a matter of law defendants could not have been liable for damages for false arrest and imprisonment because the officers had acted pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:257 in arresting and incarcerating the material witness; and (2) that while the record as a whole reflected that the material witness's counsel had filed pleadings that clearly raised sanction questions under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 863, the court was bound by the manifest error and abuse of discretion inquiries and the court found no manifest error or abuse of discretion in the trial court's rejection of the motions for sanctions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of defendants' motions for summary judgment and the trial court's implicit denial of defendants' motions for sanctions. The court also denied defendants' request for damages for frivolous appeal.

State v. Francis


No. 96-KA-2389


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-2389 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/15/98); 715 So. 2d 457; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 810



April 15, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 383-170, SECTION "I", HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court for the Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted and sentenced him for aggravated burglary. The State filed a multiple bill, and defendant was found to be a third offender. The trial court sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The trial court denied his motion to reconsider the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant complained that the State failed to prove his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt because there was insufficient evidence of unauthorized entry and no evidence of intent to commit a felony or theft within the victim's home. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held as follows: 1) there was sufficient physical evidence that defendant was not authorized to enter the house because the door lock was broken and the victim made an incriminating statement to the police on the night of the incident; 2) the circumstantial evidence that defendant had beaten the victim in the head was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to find that defendant intended to inflict greater harm on the victim, harm sufficient to constitute a felony, once inside her home; and 3) under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii), defendant was subject to a mandatory life sentence as a third offender convicted of aggravated burglary and the trial court did not err in imposing the mandatory life sentence because defendant failed to present substantial evidence to rebut the presumption of constitutionality of the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

434 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Splond


No. 30,433-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,433 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/08/98); 712 So. 2d 182; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 725



April 8, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 95-F0344. Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, upon a guilty plea, for driving while under the influence of alcohol (DWI), third offense, for which he was sentenced to three years hard labor and fined.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was originally charged with DWI, fourth offense, to which he pled not guilty and sought to quash the predicate offenses. The trial court quashed only one, and defendant pled guilty to DWI, third offense, reserving his right to appeal. The court affirmed, finding first, that the motion to quash the other two predicate offenses was properly denied because they were properly filed, and the affidavits were legally sufficient and not defective. Although the court clerks who received the filings were improperly sworn in, they were nonetheless de facto public officers. Thus, their acts had the same validity as de jure officers and could not be collaterally attacked by third persons. Second, defendant's allegation that Monroe, La., City Code § 33-10, under which defendant was charged, was invalid because it was inconsistent with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98, which required that third and subsequent DWI offenses had to be charged under state law, was without merit because the DWI ordinance was valid and substantially consistent with § 14:98. Third, defendant's sentence was not excessive under La. Const. art. 1, § 20 because it was not grossly disproportionate to the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentencing of defendant for DWI, third offense.

 

435 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Overby


No. 30,589-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,589 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/08/98); 714 So. 2d 28; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 736



April 8, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Richland, Louisiana. Trial Court No. F-96-169. Honorable Glynn D. Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Richland (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of second degree kidnapping, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1 following defendant's plea of guilty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offered the victim a ride and when she accepted, he held her in the back of his truck and raped her, until she managed to break free and run to safety. Defendant was charged with aggravated kidnapping, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44. In return for a guilty plea, defendant was convicted of second degree kidnapping, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1. Defendant received the maximum sentence for second degree kidnapping. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that venue was proper under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 611, 612 because at least one element of the crime was committed within the jurisdiction. The court further found that defendant intended to force the victim to acquiesce in exchange for safety where defendant conveyed to the victim that she would be killed if she tried to get away, manifesting defendant's intent to force her to give in to his demands with the hope of securing her safe release. The court concluded that defendant's sentence did not shock the sense of justice in view of the benefit the defendant received by pleading guilty to a lesser charge and thus avoiding a longer sentence and defendant's prior criminal history.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.
