State ex rel. A.A.S.


No. 30,775-JAC


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,775 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/08/98); 711 So. 2d 319; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 741



April 8, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 51367. Honorable David Matlock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the judgment of the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which held that La. Child Code art. 897.1, which imposed mandatory "juvenile life" sentence for juveniles adjudicated delinquent for aggravated rape, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42, was unconstitutional as applied to defendant, a juvenile.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and adjudicated a delinquent for aggravated rape. The juvenile court held that as applied to defendant La. Child Code art. 897.1 violated U.S. Const. amends. VIII, XIV, and fundamental notions of fairness by mandating a secure placement of defendant until age 21. On appeal, the court reversed the juvenile court's judgment and remanded. The court held that the mandatory sentence was not grossly out of proportion to the gravity of the conduct and that the juvenile court failed to articulate sufficient rationale that defendant's case was a truly "rare case" that warranted the exceptional declaration of unconstitutionality. The court noted that while the victim may have "initiated" the encounter, she was not capable of consent. Although defendant had no juvenile felony record, he did have a prior adjudication for simple battery that involved an element of sexual battery, and he had extensive behavioral problems at school. Overall the court did not find that the imposition of juvenile life would have made no measurable contribution to defendant's rehabilitation or that it would have been a needless and purposeless infliction of pain and suffering.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the juvenile court's judgment and remanded with instructions for the entry of a judgment of disposition consistent the "juvenile life" sentence mandated by statute.

 

437 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Devers v. Southern Univ.


No. 97 CA 0259 CONSOLIDATED WITH 97 CA 0260


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 0259 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/08/98); 712 So. 2d 199; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 787



April 8, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 415,413 and 416,026. Honorable Bob Downing, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant university sought review of an order from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which entered a judgment declaring defendant's dormitory sweep policy prima facie unconstitutional. Plaintiff student also challenged the trial court's dismissal of a number of defendants and denial of his discovery motions and request for sanctions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff student was arrested following the discovery of marijuana in his dormitory room. The discovery was made pursuant to defendant university's random dormitory search policy. Plaintiff subsequently filed an action seeking damages and an injunction against defendant. The trial court declared defendant's search policy was prima facie unconstitutional and also dismissed a number of defendants and denied plaintiff's discovery motions and request for sanctions. Upon appeal by both parties, the court affirmed. The court held that the dormitory search policy was prima facie unconstitutional where defendant failed to show that the policy furthered its functioning as an educational institution. The court noted that checks of dormitory rooms for health hazards were permissible as were searches in emergencies. However, defendant did not specify such a purpose; rather it allowed entry of dormitory rooms accompanied by police without any stated purpose. The court found defendant's attorney was properly dismissed as a party because the attorney had no involvement in the actions of which plaintiff complained and his only connection with the case was his representation of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that declared defendant university's dormitory search policy prima facie unconstitutional. The court also affirmed the dismissal of a number of defendants and the denial of plaintiff student's motions and request for sanctions. The court held defendant's random dormitory search policy was prima facie unconstitutional because defendant failed to show the policy furthered its function as an educational institution.

Johnson v. Aymond


NUMBER 97-1466


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-1466 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/01/98); 709 So. 2d 1072; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 657



April 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Docket Number 96-3590-B; Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana; the Honorable William J. Bennett, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs filed a petition for damages against defendants, a newspaper and others, for damages allegedly sustained by the publication and/or dissemination of the contents of and allegedly illegally intercepted communication between them. The Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana granted the newspaper's exception of no cause of action. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The newspaper's exception of no cause of action contended that the Electronic Surveillance Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1301 et seq., did not bar the publication or broadcast of an allegedly illegally intercepted telephone conversation that had already been disclosed. On appeal, plaintiffs argued that: (1) trial court erred in dismissing their claims against the newspaper after finding that the literal interpretation of the Act supported a cause of action; and (2) the trial court erred in finding that to apply the Act in the case would have been unconstitutional. Upon review, the court held that the consideration of the constitutionality of the Act by the trial court was erroneous and that plaintiffs' petitions stated a cause of action. Because none of the procedures for considering the constitutionality of the Act were observed, and the Act did not interfere with or curtail the plenary powers vested in the trial court by the Louisiana Constitution, the issue of constitutionality was not in proper posture for consideration.In addition, the allegations of plaintiffs' petitions, when accepted as true, supported a cause of action under the literal language of the Act.


OUTCOME: The decision sustaining the newspaper's exception of no cause of action is reversed and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. All costs associated with the appeal were assessed to the newspaper.

Latter v. ABC Ins. Co.


No. 97-CA-1968


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1968 (La. App. 4 Cir. 03/18/98); 708 So. 2d 536; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 573



March 18, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 93-14637, DIVISION "B-6". HONORABLE MAX N. TOBIAS, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney sought review of a judgment of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff clients and held that if the attorney had timely filed a suit on behalf of the clients, they would have been successful in their claim against the state for arrearages. Therefore, the trial court ordered the attorney to pay the arrearages.


OVERVIEW: The clients filed an action against the attorney because the attorney failed to timely file suit against the state for arrearages. The attorney filed an exception of prescription/peremption. The trial court found in favor of the clients and ordered the attorney to pay the arrearages. The attorney appealed. While the matter was pending on appeal, the state supreme court handed down a decision, which was dispositive of the prescriptive/peremptive defense issue raised by the attorney, but not addressed by the trial court. Thereafter, the clients filed a motion with the court seeking a remand so that they could challenge the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605. The attorney opposed, arguing that the clients never asserted any constitutional arguments at the trial level and, therefore, those issues could not be raised for the first time on appeal. However, the court determined that in the light of the law's liberal approach toward allowing amended pleadings in order to promote the interests of justice, remand was proper in order to allow the clients to amend their pleadings to assert that their claim was not perempted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was remanded to allow the clients to amend their pleadings to assert that their claim was not perempted.

March 18, 1998, Decided

Rehearing overruled by, 04/30/1998
Writ denied by Davis v. Board of Supervisors of 719 So. 2d 1288, 1998 La. LEXIS 2157 (La., June 26, 1998)
Subsequent appeal at Davis v. Bd. of Supervisors, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2827 (La.App. 4 Cir., Nov. 17, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 94-16678, DIVISION "J", HONORABLE GEORGE C. CONNOLLY, JR., JUDGE.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed the order from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which granted defendant doctors and Board of Supervisors of state university summary judgment in the parents' "wrongful life" action on behalf of their minor child, who was born with a birth defect.


OVERVIEW: During the mother's pregnancy, she requested amniocentesis to screen for possible birth defects. The doctor originally said the test was normal but later said it was not and requested blood tests from both parents. The parents were advised during the 23rd week of gestation that there was a significant risk that the child would be born with a birth defect. The baby was later born with a chromosomal abnormality. The parents filed a wrongful birth action against defendants, claiming that if they had been advised earlier, they would have aborted the baby. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment. The court held that defendants had met their burden of offering uncontroverted evidence that no genuine issue of fact material to the question of whether their alleged delay in notifying the parents of the risk of a birth defect caused the parents to choose to continue the pregnancy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting defendants summary judgment in the parents' "wrongful birth" action.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION NOS. 94-02528 c/w 96-03265 c/w 96-03247, DISTRICT EIGHT. HONORABLE GWENDOLYN F. THOMPSON, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a judgment from the Office of Worker's Compensation (Louisiana), which awarded temporary total disability benefits in the amount of $ 243 per month to appellee grandchild of worker's compensation recipient on the ground that appellee was a partial dependent.


OVERVIEW: The worker's compensation recipient was receiving benefits for a knee injury, but the benefits were discontinued when he became incarcerated. The grandchild of the worker's compensation recipient had filed an action to continue the payment of the benefits to him because he was his dependent, as provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201.4. The worker's compensation office awarded temporary total disability benefits in the amount of $ 243 per month to the grandchild based on a finding that he was a dependent, and the employer appealed. However, the court did not find anything in the record that supported the calculations of the judge concerning the amount of support that the grandchild was entitled to. The court remanded to the judge for a more accurate determination on this issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the worker's compensation office insofar as it found the grandchild of the worker's compensation recipient was a partial dependent. The court remanded the case for a more accurate determination of the actual amount of benefits that should be provided to the grandchild.

City of New Orleans v. Board of Dirs. of the La. State Museum


No. 97-CA-1574


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1574 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/11/98); 709 So. 2d 1008; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 553



March 11, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 31, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 97-9958, DIVISION "H-12". HONORABLE LOUIS DIROSA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant historical preservation commission sought review of a decision from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, No. 97-9958 Division H (Louisiana), which granted a peremptory exception of no cause of action filed by appellee state museum on the commission's petition for injunctive relief and application for restraining order to prevent the museum from constructing a fence around its building.


OVERVIEW: A historical preservation commission filed a petition for injunctive relief and an application for a temporary restraining order seeking to prevent a state museum from constructing a proposed fence to keep the undesirables from entering that museum at night. The State and museum filed an exception of no cause of action, claiming that the museum, as a state-owned building, was not subject to the jurisdiction of the commission. The court reversed the district court's judgment upholding the State and museum's exception of no cause of action and the court concluded that the commission had jurisdiction over state-owned buildings within the historical section of New Orleans. The court found that La. Const. art. 14, § 22A applied to any building in the historical section due to the need for uniformity to retain the beauty of the section as a whole. The court held that requiring the State to comply with the commission's permit procedure did not abridge the State's police power. The court found that the commission and the State museum had distinct powers and the commission ordinance and that State museum statute were not incompatible and could be effectuated in harmony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment maintaining the museum's peremptory exception of no cause of action and the court concluded that the commission could seek any and all remedies that arose out of its inability to secure a preliminary injunction which sought to prevent the museum from constructing a fence around the building.

Smith v. Willard


No. 97-CA-1772


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1772 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/11/98); 711 So. 2d 723; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 751



March 11, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS NO. 95-1604, DIVISION "K" HONORABLE RICHARD J. GANUCHEAU, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bankruptcy trustee sought review of a judgment from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment to defendants, attorney and his professional liability insurer, and dismissed plaintiff's lawsuit that was filed against defendants based on the failure to settle.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was hired by the insurer to defend against a claim. The opposing counsel had made a demand on the insurance policy limits, and the attorney refused to settle. The case went to trial, and resulted in a $ 403,200 judgment against the insured. The insured had filed for bankruptcy, and the bankruptcy trustee was appointed to represent her. The bankruptcy trustee then filed a lawsuit against the attorney and his professional liability insurer based on the failure to settle. The trial court had granted summary judgment to the attorney and the professional liability insurer, and dismissed the bankruptcy trustee's lawsuit. On appeal, the court did not find an issue of fact concerning whether the attorney had the opportunity to settle the claim, and had the duty to protect the insured from the excess settlement. The attorney was hired by the insurer, and he did not represent the insured in the litigation. The affidavit of the opposing counsel also supported the fact that the attorney was engaged by the insurer, and not by the insured. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the attorney and his professional liability insurer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted summary judgment to the attorney and his professional liability insurer. The court affirmed the dismissal of the bankruptcy trustee's lawsuit that was filed against the attorney and the professional liability insurer based on the failure to settle.

Ieyoub ex rel. State v. W. R. Grace & Co.-Conn.


NUMBER 97-728


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-0728 (La. App. 3 Cir. 03/06/98); 708 So. 2d 1227; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 400



March 6, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Docket No. 95-3722, Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, Honorable Patricia Minaldi, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, asbestos manufacturers and their insurers, sought review of a judgment from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff attorney general on plaintiff's action for declaratory judgment. The issue involved was the constitutional validity of plaintiff's contract with outside counsel to pursue a civil claim for the state.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general had a contract with outside counsel for the outside counsel to pursue a civil claim for the state against the asbestos manufacturers and their insurers. The attorney general then file an action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutional validity of the contract that he entered with the outside counsel. The trial court had granted summary judgment in favor of the attorney general, and the asbestos manufacturers and their insurers had appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the grant of summary judgment in the attorney general's favor. The court held that the contract in question was an unconstitutional infringement by the attorney general upon the legislature's power to control the financial affairs of the state. The court found the contract was unenforceable, and had violated the separation of powers doctrine under La. Const. art. II, § 1, because neither the state constitution nor the legislature had authorized the attorney general to enter into the contract at issue with the outside counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that granted summary judgment to the attorney general on the attorney general's action for declaratory judgment. The court found the attorney general's contract with outside counsel to pursue a civil claim for the state was constitutionally unenforceable.

Herpin v. Boudreaux


NUMBER 98-306


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


98-306 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/05/98); 709 So. 2d 269; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 281



March 5, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District. Court for the Parish of Vermilion, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Edward Rubin, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District, Court for the Parish of Vermilion (Louisiana), which ruled that defendant did not meet the qualifications of actual residence and domicile as required by law, and was therefore disqualified as a candidate in the primary election for the office of Mayor for the City of Kaplan.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an action objecting to defendant's candidacy for mayor. The trial court held that defendant was disqualified as a candidate for the office of mayor. Defendant appealed and the court found defendant did not meet the qualifications for the office of the mayor of a certain city and that he did not actually reside at the home at issue. The court found it difficult to believe that a family of four could spend the majority of their time, including most nights in a home, and use very limited utilities although the home contained an electric stove, electric refrigerator, freezer, television, and other electrical items. The court concluded that the utility bills easily inferred that defendant's family was not actually residing at the residence at issue the majority of the time. The testimony of defendant and a certain letter showed that defendant's main intent was to qualify the residence as his political domicile. Proof of defendant's intention to change domicile depended upon the circumstances because there was no declaration to change domicile. The trial court was not clearly wrong in finding that defendant's domicile had not changed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that held defendant was disqualified as a candidate in the primary election for mayor.

 

447 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Romaguera v. Overby


No. 97-CA-1654


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1654 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/04/98); 709 So. 2d 266; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 337



March 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 96-6138, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE YADA T. MAGEE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed a judgment from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which dismissed her medical malpractice claim against defendant doctor on an exception of prescription, in the patient's lawsuit against the doctor and defendant medical corporation.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed the lawsuit against the doctor for damages resulting from his failure to remove a catheter following chemotherapy treatment. The doctor filed an exception of prescription claiming that the patient's action had prescribed on its face. The issues on appeal were whether the doctor's conduct constituted a continuing tort so that the three year prescriptive period established by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 did not begin to run until long after the initial tort and whether the statute was unconstitutional. In an effort to overcome the three year prescription the patient argued that the doctor's continuing failure to discover that a part of the catheter was left in her body constituted a continuing tort until January 1995 when she last saw the doctor. The court found that the record did not support the application of the continuing tort doctrine to the patient's case. The patient presented no evidence that the doctor knew about the faulty removal of the catheter in June 1991, or that he should have known about it. The patient did not properly raise the issue of the constitutionality of § 9:5628.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the patient's medical malpractice case against the doctor.

Johnson v. Carter


No. 97-CA-1800


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1800 (La. App. 4 Cir. 03/04/98); 707 So. 2d 1366; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 341



March 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 97-8378 - DIVISION "L". HONORABLE MAX N. TOBIAS, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters appealed an order of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which dismissed their petition for a writ of mandamus against defendant city council members to compel them to call an election on a Home Rule Charter of the city to provide for a local minimum wage.


OVERVIEW: The voters filed a petition for a writ of mandamus against the city council members to compel them to call an election on a proposed amendment to the Home Rule Charter of the city to provide for a local minimum wage. The state legislature passed La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:642, which prohibited a local government from establishing a minimum wage, during the pendency of the voters' suit. The trial court then dismissed the voters' suit because the proposed election was to have been held after the effective date of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:642, and thus the issue of whether to provide for a local minimum wage was moot. The voters appealed, arguing that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:642 was patently unconstitutional. The court held that the constitutionality of a statute must have been questioned first in the trial court, and the constitutionality of statute must have been specially pleaded and grounds for the claim particularized. In proceedings in which the constitutionality of a statute was questioned the attorney general should have been served with notice. The constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:642 was not presented to or considered by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court denying the voters' application for a writ of mandamus. However, this portion of the judgment was vacated and the case remanded to the trial court to allow the voters to specifically plead the unconstitutionality of a statute prohibiting a local government from establishing a minimum wage, to notify the state attorney general, and to allow for the issue of constitutionality to be fully litigated.

State v. Barney


No. 97-KA-777


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-777 (La. App. 5 Cir. 02/25/98); 708 So. 2d 1205; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 228



February 25, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 97-0037, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE ROBERT A. CHAISSON, JUDGE. THOMAS F. DALEY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 29th Judicial District Court of the Parish of St. Charles (Louisiana), which convicted him of possession of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967. He was sentenced to two years in prison, sentence suspended, and two years active probation.


OVERVIEW: Officers observed defendant standing next to a vehicle in the middle of the street. Defendant fled and was eventually apprehended. The officers testified that they observed defendant attempting to reach in his pocket. During a pat down, the officer felt an object he thought was a matchbox in defendant's right rear jeans pocket. He retrieved the matchbox, opened it, and discovered an off-white material, which field-tested positive for cocaine. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. Specifically, he argued that the officers did not have a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity to justify the initial stop, nor did the officer have an articulable belief that he was in danger so as to justify the subsequent pat down. The court found that the investigatory stop and initial frisk were legal, but held that the opening of the matchbox by the officer exceeded the permissible bounds of a reasonable search. The officer was only permitted to pat down defendant's clothing to detect hidden weapons to protect himself and others from a potentially armed and dangerous suspect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine. The trial court erred in denying the motion to suppress evidence.

 

450 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lisotta


No. 97-KA-406


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-406 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/25/98); 712 So. 2d 527; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 226



February 25, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 95-4171, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING. H. CHARLES GAUDIN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE SET ASIDE; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentencing for indecent behavior with a juvenile in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court Parish Of Jefferson (Louisiana). On appeal, defendant argued (1) that the trial judge erred in permitting a witness to testify about earlier incidents involving her and defendant; (2) that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 32 and the victim was 16 when defendant attempted have sex with the victim. Defendant was convicted of indecent behavior with a juvenile and sentenced to seven years at hard labor, the maximum penalty. On appeal, defendant argued that admission of evidence of his attempt to have sex with a minor when he was 21 was error. The court disagreed and affirmed. The court was unaware of any reported Louisiana opinions saying that events occurring 14 or 15 years before a trial could not be acceptable evidence against a charged defendant only because of the time element. Accordingly, there was no error. The court, however, agreed that defendant's sentence was excessive. The court held that maximum sentences were appropriate only in cases involving the most serious violations of the statute and the worse type of offender. The facts and circumstances did not justify a maximum seven-year sentence. The maximum was disproportionate to the realities of the crime and was an abuse of discretion. A lesser sentence would not deprecate the seriousness of defendant's behavior. The court remanded for sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for indecent behavior with a juvenile but vacated the maximum penalty and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Diaz


97-KA-1003


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-1003 (La. App. 5 Cir. 02/25/98); 708 So. 2d 1192; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 230



February 25, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NUMBER 96-5588, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE, PRESIDING. THOMAS C. WICKER, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted defendant for knowingly causing or participating in a vehicular collision for the purpose of presenting a false or fraudulent claim with the intent to injure, defraud, or deceive an insurance company under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1244(A)(1). He was sentenced to three years at hard labor with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to quash pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 531, alleging that all of the evidence against him was illegally seized from his attorney's office in violation of his attorney-client privilege. The trial judge denied the motion to quash. The court held that there was no showing by defendant of a privileged communication between defendant and his attorney that was used at trial. Defendant also contended that his insurance claims for property damage and personal injury were legitimate and as such showed that he lacked the requisite intent to defraud. The court disagreed based on a clear reading of the statute. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1244(1) required that defendant knowingly caused or participated in a vehicular collision for the purpose of presenting any false or fraudulent claim. Finally, defendant complained that his sentence of three years imprisonment at hard labor was excessive. In imposing the sentence, the trial court considered the provisions of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 and aggravating and mitigating factors. The court found no abuse of the trial court's wide discretion to sentence within statutory limits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for knowingly causing or participating in a vehicular collision for the purpose of presenting a false or fraudulent claim with the intent to injure, defraud, or deceive an insurance company.

 

452 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lisotta


No. 97-KA-407


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-407 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/25/98); 712 So. 2d 525; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 232



February 25, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 95-4172, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING. H. CHARLES GAUDIN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, which convicted him of exhibiting a pornographic tape to a minor pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:91.11.


OVERVIEW: The state proved through the testimony of three teenaged girls that defendant showed them pornographic video tapes, called porno movies, in his home. The court affirmed the convictions. The court rejected defendant's argument that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:91.11 pertained only to activity at a newsstand or other commercial establishment, not to videos shown in residences. The clear legislative intent was to make it a crime for anyone over 17 to sell, exhibit or distribute obscene material to persons under 17 at a commercial establishment and everywhere else. Statutes were presumed valid and their constitutionality was to be upheld whenever possible. The court found that § 14: 91.11 gave adequate notice of what was prohibited and which standards were to be used in determining guilt or innocence. The court held that if the defense had prior notice of the State's intent to introduce a statement and the statement was properly admitted later, the prosecutor's premature mention of the statement in its opening statement to the jury caused no prejudice. The court held that a deputy's statement to which defendant assigned error was admitted during the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of exhibiting a pornographic tape to a minor.

State v. Dunn


No. 30,269-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,269 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/25/98); 713 So. 2d 479; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 251



February 25, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Rehearing May 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1466; Released for Publication June 19, 1998. Rehearing of May 15, 1998, Reported at: 713 So. 2d 479 at 489.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 18232. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana, convicted defendant of simple escape, adjudicated defendant a fourth felony offender, and sentenced defendant to the minimum term of 20 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant escaped from a holding area in the courthouse by climbing out of a window. After serving time in another state, defendant was extradited back to Louisiana. A charge of simple escape was added to other charges already pending against defendant. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in finding that he had waived his right to counsel, failing to advise him of the dangers of self-representation, and failing to provide him with stand-by counsel. Defendant also challenged the sufficiency of the evidence for his simple escape conviction and habitual offender adjudication. Finally, defendant argued that his sentence should not have been enlarged by application of the habitual offender law, and that his sentence was excessive. The court rejected these contentions and affirmed. Defendant understood his right to counsel and consciously chose not to accept court-appointed counsel. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's simple escape conviction. The trial court did not err in adjudicating defendant a habitual offender and accordingly enlarging defendant's original sentence. Based on his criminal record, defendant's sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for simple escape and his sentence to 20 years at hard labor.

Jones v. Board of Ethics for Elected Officials


No. 97 CW 2686 CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 97 CA 2854


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 2686 (La. App. 1 Cir. 02/20/98); 709 So. 2d 841; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 307



February 20, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On application for writs to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 429,619.

On appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 429,619. Honorable Janice G. Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED. WRIT RECALLED, VACATED, AND SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Ethics challenged the decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found pursuant to an action filed by appellee senator that the makeup of the Board did not comply with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1132 to reflect the state's population and granted a preliminary injunction restraining the Board from taking any action against the senator.


OVERVIEW: The Board of Ethics appealed a preliminary injunction granted in favor of the senator restraining it from taking any action against the senator. The senator alleged in an action against the Board that it had no authority to proceed against him. In a supplemental petition, the senator alleged that the Board's makeup violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1132 because it was not "representative of the state's population as near as practicable." The court disagreed and reversed. The court held that it was unable to discern what the legislature intended with the questioned phraseology. It was unclear what the makeup of the Board was supposed to be. The legislature did not definitively proscribe the membership of the Board. The court therefore refused to intervene between the two political branches of government to determine that the legislature intended the membership of the Board to correspond numerically to the population makeup of the state along racial and gender lines. The senator's action was an impermissible collateral attack on the right to office of the Board members under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 42:76-77.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding of the trial court and the injunction granted in favor of the senator restraining the Board of Ethics from taking any action against the senator.

Lewis v. Day


NUMBER 97 CA 0111


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 0111 (La. App. 1 Cir. 02/20/98); 708 So. 2d 1152; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 319



February 20, 1998, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Suit Number 409,227, Section "F". Honorable A. Foster Sanders, III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which held that defendant was not eligible for good time credits he had earned prior to resentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was adjudicated a habitual offender. After serving some time on his sentence, defendant filed a motion to correct an allegedly illegal sentence and was resentenced to the same term, but this time it was clarified that he was sentenced to serve without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence and with credit for time served. In recomputing his sentence, defendant was not credited for good time credit he had earned prior to resentencing. He filed suit to receive his good time credit and the trial court found that he was ineligible for the good time credits. On appeal, the court affirmed because under the clear language of § 15:571.3, which was in effect when defendant committed the instant offence, defendant was not eligible to earn diminution of his sentence through good time credit. The Louisiana Department of Public Safety and Corrections had no discretion in the matter to allow defendant to earn the good time credits and it had the right to correct the error it made in application of the statutory law governing good time eligibility to take away good time credits which it had no statutory authority to award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held that defendant was not eligible for good time credits he had earned prior to resentencing.

Martin v. Elmwood Med. Ctr.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed from a judgment of the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration, District 07 (Louisiana), which found that the employer failed to pay a workers' compensation judgment to plaintiff employee within 30 days as mandated by statute and assessed a penalty and attorney fees pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. § 23:1201(F).

State v. Williams


No. 97-KA-970


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-970 (La. App. 5 Cir. 01/27/98); 708 So. 2d 1086; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 96



January 27, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 95,6761, DIVISION "D". THE HONORABLE ROBERT M. MURPHY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of conviction of distribution of heroin in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 40:966(A) entered by the Twenty Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) upon a jury verdict, challenging the trial court's imposition of a sentence of life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold $ 30 of heroin to an undercover police officer. Defendant was found guilty by a jury of distribution of heroin in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 40:966(A). The trial court entered a judgment of conviction and imposed a mandatory life imprisonment sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed. First, the court held that defendant was procedurally barred from challenging his sentence pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1. The court also held that defendant's sentence was not constitutionally excessive. Next, the court rejected defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. Because the sentence was reviewed and not found to be excessive, defendant was not prejudiced by counsel's failure to object to the sentence or his failure to file a motion to reconsider the sentence. Finally, defendant did not show that he was prejudiced by the trial court's failure to observe a 24-hour delay in sentencing required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 873. Because the life sentence was mandatory, no prejudice could possibly have resulted from the failure of the trial court to comply with the delay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction of defendant of distribution of heroin entered by the trial court upon a jury verdict and also affirmed the mandatory sentence of life imprisonment imposed by the trial court.

 

459 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Salavarria v. National Car Rental Sys.


No. 97-C-2090


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-2090 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/21/98); 705 So. 2d 809; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 54



January 21, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON SUPERVISORY WRITS FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NOS. 95-14334 c/w 95-14335, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE ETHEL S. JULIEN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant relator appealed a judgment of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans, Division N (Louisiana), which denied its motion for summary judgment against plaintiff injured parties in a negligence action between residents of different states. The relator claimed that the trial court erred in ruling that because the rental agreement was entered into in Florida, Florida law applied to the Louisiana accident.


OVERVIEW: The injured parties, Louisiana residents, had an accident in Louisiana with a car that was owned by the relator, a Florida car rental company, and driven by a Florida resident. In the injured parties' negligence action, the trial court denied the relator's motion for summary judgment on the ground that Florida law applied, which was more advantageous to the injured parties. The court reversed the judgment and dismissed the complaint against the relator, ruling that the because the accident occurred in Louisiana, Louisiana's standard of care applied. Under both La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3515, the general conflict of law statute, and La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3542, Louisiana had the greatest relationship to the action, and its policies would have been most seriously impaired if its law were not applied. In Louisiana a self-insured rental car company had the right to limit operation of its vehicles to only those individuals to whom it gave express permission, those who were listed as authorized drivers in the rental agreement. The driver of the vehicle was not a party to the contract but was an unauthorized operator, and the contract absolved the relator from liability for such operation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had denied the relator's motion for summary judgment in the action against it by the injured parties. The court also rendered judgment in favor of the relator, dismissing the injured parties' complaint against the relator with prejudice, and it remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Descant v. Administrators of the Tulane Educ. Fund


No. 95-CA-2127


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-2127 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/21/98); 706 So. 2d 618; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 70



January 21, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Descant v. Administrators of the Tulane Educ. Fund, 717 So. 2d 1131, 1998 La. LEXIS 1776 (La., Apr. 3, 1998)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Descant v. Herrera, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3236 (La.App. 4 Cir., Dec. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 91-22670, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE YADA T. MAGEE, JUDGE.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of December 23, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2944.
Descant v. Administrators of the Tulane Educ. Fund, 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2944 (La.App. 4 Cir., Dec. 23, 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents appealed the judgment of the Civil District Court, for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which entered a directed verdict in favor of defendant hospital and entered a jury verdict in favor of defendant doctor, in the parents' medical malpractice action for injuries sustained by their baby at birth.


OVERVIEW: Complications in the birth of the parents' baby left her profoundly brain damaged. The parents filed a medical malpractice suit against the hospital and the doctor. The father's employer intervened to obtain reimbursement for funds it paid on behalf of the baby. The trial court held that the employer had no cause of action and dismissed it from the case. The trial court directed a verdict in favor of the hospital, and the jury found in favor of the doctor. On appeal, the court reversed in part and affirmed in part. The court held that neither it nor the trial court had jurisdiction to decide the employer's subrogation rights because that issue fell under the auspices of the federal court. It was error for the trial court to grant a directed verdict in favor of the hospital because reasonable and fair-minded people could have found the hospital was negligent. There was no error in finding the parents' expert did not establish the standard of care applicable to the doctor. The jury instructions accurately reflected the applicable malpractice law. The jury instructions on informed consent were proper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part and affirmed in part the judgment of the trial court. The case was remanded.

State ex rel. D.L.S.


No. 30,322-JAC


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,322 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/21/98); 706 So. 2d 187; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 26



January 21, 1998, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 56154. Honorable David Matlock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant 14 year-old juvenile appealed his adjudication of delinquency by the Juvenile Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, of aggravated rape of an 11 year-old girl, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42, and resulting custodial commitment until his 21st birthday.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 14 year-old juvenile, was arrested for the alleged aggravated rape of an 11 year-old girl, a violation of § 14:42. After both he and his mother were advised that he had the right to remain silent and that anything he said could and would be used against him in court, he gave an inculpatory tape-recorded statement to police. The trial court denied his motion to suppress the statement, admitted the statement into evidence, adjudicated him delinquent as charged, and imposed a disposition of custodial commitment until his 21st birthday. On appeal, the court affirmed each of the trial court's rulings, holding that defendant's statement was fully voluntary and was preceded by all proper warnings to him and his mother regarding his right to remain silent; and the disposition was not unlawfully excessive, in light of the totality of the evidence at the disposition hearing, which the trial court was in the best position to evaluate as it was offered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decisions denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence, and held that the disposition of commitment until defendant's 21st birthday was not excessive.

 

462 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Terrytown Fifth Dist. Volunteer Fire Dep't v. Wilcox


No. 97-CA-322


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-322 (La. App. 5 Cir. 01/14/98); 707 So. 2d 449; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 75



January 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 10, 1998. Released for Publication March 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 424-877, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE ROBERT J. BURNS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fire department sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of defendant State and declared constitutional 1991 La. Acts 1000, which authorized supplementary payments by the State to employees of nonprofit, volunteer fire companies.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court declared the Act to be constitutional, the department appealed. The department claimed that the Act's body was broader than its title, that contracts between the department and the parish were impaired by the Act, and that the Act deprived the department of equal protection under the state and federal constitutions. On appeal the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the title of the Act was plainly clear and did not suggest that the body there of would or should have been limited to state supplemental salary payments. The court stated that the department failed to show specifically how the Act impaired contracts between itself and the parish. The court found no showing that the Act caused an oppressive impairment as suggested by the department. The court noted that the Act sought to further a fairly apparent general state interest of providing better fire protection. The court held that the act did not deprive the department of equal protection and was neither arbitrary nor capricious but was a legislative response to the attorney general's previous opinion saying that supplemental pay to volunteer firemen was illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

463 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Oliver


NUMBER W97-721 AND NUMBER 97-1102


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-721 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/07/98); 705 So. 2d 301; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1



January 7, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On application for supervisory writs to the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, and on Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Acadia (Docket No. 69,412), State of Louisiana, the Honorable John D. Trahan, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 69412 - 1A.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant filed an action against defendants, tortfeasor, liability insurer, and uninsured motorist insurer, for injuries sustained in a highway accident. The Fifteenth Judicial District Court applied Louisiana law in determining the uninsured motorist coverage and rendered partial summary judgment against the uninsured motorist insurer. The uninsured motorist insurer appealed and applied for supervisory writs.


OVERVIEW: Although the accident occurred in Louisiana and the tortfeasor was a Louisiana resident, the claimant and the uninsured motorist insurer were from out of state. The trial court applied Louisiana on the basis of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1406(D)(1)(a)(iii). The court found that Georgia law should have been applied to the uninsured motorist policy. The court utilized a conflict of law analysis and determined that where the uninsured motorist policy complied with Georgia law, the negotiation, selection of benefits, issuance, and delivery of the policy occurred entirely outside the State of Louisiana, and neither the insured nor the uninsured motorist insurer maintained any offices, terminals, or employees in Louisiana, the trial court should have applied Georgia law. The fact that the accident occurred in Louisiana and that the tortfeasor was a Louisiana resident was not enough to warrant application of Louisiana law. Georgia had a compelling interest in regulating insurance policies issued to its residents and in seeing that the expectations of the parties to the policies issued were upheld. Louisiana had no compelling interest in overriding Georgia law in this case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of partial summary judgment against the uninsured motorist insurer and remanded for further proceedings.

 

464 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hammond


NUMBER 97-712


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-712 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/07/98); 704 So. 2d 1281; 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3



January 7, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Lower Court: Rapides. Lower Court Judge: W. ROSS FOOTE. Lower Court Number: 242,576.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Rapides Court (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of the State and sentenced defendant to 25 years at hard labor for the conviction of aggravated burglary and 40 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence for the conviction of attempted armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of aggravated burglary and attempted armed robbery he was sentenced. Defendant appealed from the sentences imposed, claiming that they were excessive and placed him in double jeopardy. On appeal the court amended and affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that defendant was not placed in double jeopardy when he was sentenced for both crimes. The court found that the two criminal acts did not contain identical elements and that neither offense was a lesser-included offense of the other. The court stated that double jeopardy did not attach because the two offenses each required proof of an additional element that the other did not. The court noted that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in the imposition of defendant's sentence. The court found that the sentence was based upon defendant's prior criminal record and the fact that he had been offered probation previously for those other crimes. The court held that the trial court failed to give defendant credit for time already served and that his sentence had to be amended to award credit for time actually spent in custody prior to the execution of his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment of the trial court to award defendant credit for time spent in custody prior to the execution of his sentence and, as amended, affirmed the judgment.

 

465 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hammond


No. 97-K-1677


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1677 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/30/97); 706 So. 2d 530; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2954



December 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON CERTIORARI TO THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 389-819, SECTION "D". HONORABLE FRANK A. MARULLO, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On Certiorari to the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted defendants' motion to suppress statements made to state legislative auditors in an action charging defendants with theft of $ 500 dollars or more belonging to the State of Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were toll collectors and were charged with theft after an investigation uncovered a scheme whereby defendants would deliberately misclassify revenue vehicles as non-revenue vehicles and then pocket the money they collected. Defendants were interviewed concerning the investigation by a state auditor. The trial court determined that state auditors were state actors and that because the auditors failed to give defendants their Miranda warnings prior to the interviews the statements were inadmissible. The court concluded that the trial court erred. Defendants were not in custody for purposes of the Miranda warnings because they were not under arrest and were free to leave at any time. Further, Miranda warnings were necessary only when a confession was made to a state actor. The court concluded that state auditors were not actors. Auditors were not law enforcement officers and did not function as such. The court remanded for a determination of voluntariness of defendants' statements under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:451, a statute that required confessions to be given voluntarily, regardless of who they were given to, before they could be submitted into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court erred in granting defendants' motions to suppress statements made to state legislative auditors in an action charging defendants with theft of five hundred dollars or more belonging to the State of Louisiana, but remanded the action to consider the voluntariness of the statements.

Lambert v. Riverboat Gaming Enforcement Div.


NUMBER 96 CW 1856


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 1856 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/29/97); 706 So. 2d 172; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2960



December 29, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari, Review and Mandamus to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, Trial Court Number: 409,582, Division "D", Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: WRIT OF CERTIORARI RECALLED; JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a state police division and its supervisor, appealed the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which had overruled their exception to plaintiff applicant's allegations of violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315 and its challenge to the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:525(A), following the denial of its gambling license application.


OVERVIEW: The applicants' application for a gambling license was denied by the state. The applicant alleged that the state's denial violated the applicants' rights. The applicants alleged that the state departed from its uniform evaluation process and utilized a ranking scheme. The trial court found that one of the state's agents was entitled to qualified immunity, but overruled the exception of no cause of action. The court affirmed. The court rejected the applicants' contention that the question of qualified immunity could only be resolved in the context of review of summary judgments. The applicants' complaint alleged sufficient facts to assert that the state violated a clearly established right of which a reasonable person would have known and, therefore stated a cause of action. Thus, the pleading set forth sufficient facts to survive the exception of no cause of action based on qualified immunity as claimed by one of the state's agents. The state's discretionary acts defense was inapplicable to conduct that involved violation of the Louisiana Riverboat Economic Development and Gaming Control Act, LSA-R.S. 27:41 et seq., because that Act did not provide for discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to overrule the state's exception of no cause of action to the applicant's action alleging violation of state and federal statutes after its application for a gambling license was denied.

Pierce v. Lafourche Parish Council


NUMBER 96 CA 1603


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 1603 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/29/97); 706 So. 2d 178; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2981



December 29, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 17th Judicial District Court in and for Lafourche Parish, Louisiana, Trial Court No. 78875, Honorable John L. Weimer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sought review of the decision of the 17th Judicial District Court in and for Lafourche Parish (Louisiana), which found in favor of defendant employer in an action seeking to have La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(iii) declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while in the course and scope of his employment with the employer. He was 73 years old at the time of his accident. Section 23:1221(3)(d)(iii) limited persons over 70 from receiving more than 104 weeks in workers' compensation benefits, while workers younger than seventy could receive 520 weeks of benefits. The employee filed an action seeking a judgment declaring that statute unconstitutional. The employer filed an exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction, contending the Office of Workers' Compensation hearing officers were vested with original exclusive jurisdiction over all claims or disputes arising out of workers' compensation matters. The trial court agreed, granted the employer's exception, and dismissed the employee's action. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the trial court, and not a workers' compensation hearing officer, had subject matter jurisdiction in the matter pursuant to a recently decided case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court in favor of the employer in the employee's workers' compensation action.

469 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Legros v. Westlake Polymers Corp.


No. W97-579


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-579 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/10/97); 704 So. 2d 876; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2823



December 10, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court [# 96-1160], Parish of Calcasieu, Honorable Wilford Carter, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicants, an employer and an insurer, filed a petition with the court for a writ to determine the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1101(D), which dealt with employee and employer suits against third persons in a workers' compensation setting. The employer and insurer argued that they should have been permitted to participate in the liability phase of a tort action filed by respondent employee against a third-party.


OVERVIEW: The employer and insurer filed a petition of intervention in the employee's tort action against a third-party tortfeasor in order to recover the amounts they paid to the employee for his injuries. The employer and insurer wanted to participate in the presentation of the evidence to jury on the issue of liability, but the district court denied their request. The court held that the district court's decision precluding the employer and insurer from participating in the trial on the merits was not an unconstitutional application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1101(D) because the employer and insurer only had a vested property right once the third-party tortfeasor was found liable to the employee. Where the third-party tortfeasor's liability to the employee had not yet been found, the employer and insurer were not denied any due process of law by not being able to participate in the liability phase of the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the district court's ruling that it was constitutional to deny the employer and insurer the ability to participate in depositions and the liability phase of employee's tort action against a third-party.

State v. Washington


No. 30,108-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


30,108 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/10/97); 705 So. 2d 254; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2844



December 10, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Trial Court No. 177,183B. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a jury verdict convicting him of possession of firearm by a person convicted of a felony and the sentence imposed in the trial court (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of a firearm by a person convicted of a felony. He was found guilty and sentenced. He appealed, arguing that the verdict was contrary to law and evidence, the evidence was insufficient, and his motion for post verdict judgment of acquittal should have been granted. The court held that the State presented sufficient evidence to convict defendant of the charged offense. It also presented evidence and defendant admitted that he had been convicted previously of possession with intent to distribute within the 10 year statutory limit. The jury chose to believe the testimony of the State's witnesses as opposed to the testimony of defendant. As such, the testimony of the witnesses presented sufficient evidence to convict, and the trial judge correctly denied defendant's motion for post judgment verdict of acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant.

 

471 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Delaughter


No. 29,974-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,974 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/10/97); 703 So. 2d 1364; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2863



December 10, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Franklin, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 95-047F. Honorable E. Rudolph McIntyre, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of indecent behavior with a juvenile and attempted indecent behavior with a juvenile, appealed the sentences rendered by the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Franklin (Louisiana). He argued that his sentences were excessive and denial of good time violated the ex post facto provisions of the United States and Louisiana Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to aggravated oral sexual battery and sexual battery of an eight year old victim. Pursuant to a plea bargain, he pled guilty to indecent behavior with a juvenile and attempted indecent behavior with a juvenile. He was sentenced to serve seven years at hard labor on the consummated offense and three years on the inchoate offense with two years to run concurrently without eligibility for diminution of his sentence for good behavior. He filed a motion to reconsider the sentence, which was denied, and he appealed. On review, the court held that prior to imposing the sentence, the trial court reviewed a presentence investigation report and set forth extensive reasons for the sentences imposed. Thus, it adequately followed the statutory guidelines. The trial court's articulation of reasons were adequate and did not constitute an abuse of discretion. The sentence was tailored to the offender and the offense and was not unconstitutionally excessive. Yet the application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:537 to deny diminution of the sentence for good behavior violated the ex post facto prohibition of both the federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences, but amended the judgment to delete denial of eligibility for diminution of sentence for good behavior.

 

472 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. CR97-700


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-700 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/10/97); 704 So. 2d 376; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2868



December 10, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction proceeding at State v. White, 2010 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 776 (La.App. 3 Cir., Dec. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWELFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. [Nos. 83,210-A & 83,211-A], PARISH OF AVOYELLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA, THE HONORABLE MICHAEL J. JOHNSON, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCES REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana), which convicted him on two counts of simple burglary in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62, adjudicated him a second felony offender under the habitual offender law, and sentenced him to 24 years on each count, to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in ordering his sentences to be served consecutively because the two burglaries showed a common scheme or plan. The court rejected this contention and affirmed defendant's conviction, finding that the two offenses were not part of the same transaction or part of a common scheme or plan. The court found the offenses involved different victims and occurred almost a month apart and appeared sufficiently separate and distinct to justify consecutive sentences. However, despite the fact that defendant's individual sentences appeared to be legally sound, the court found that their combined effect might make them disproportionate to the crimes committed because the 48-year combined sentence would effectively span the remainder of defendant's life. The court concluded that the 48-year combined sentence was not proportionate to the crimes committed and that it constituted a manifest abuse of discretion on the part of the trial court. Therefore, the court reversed defendant's sentences and remanded to the trial court for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of two counts of simple burglary and adjudicated him a second felony offender under the habitual offender law. The court remanded the action to the trial court for resentencing.

First Commun. Co. v. Jefferson Parish


No. 97-CA-608

State v. Robertson


No. 97-KA-1040


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1040 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/19/97); 702 So. 2d 1207; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2757



November 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 382-810, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of attempted possession of a firearm by a convicted felon.


OVERVIEW: An officer testified that defendant, who had walked quickly away from the direction of a police car, dropped a gun that discharged. The officer retrieved the gun, a semi-assault weapon, and his partners apprehended defendant. Defendant, who was charged with possession of a firearm by a convicted felon in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1, was convicted of attempted possession and sentenced to seven and one-half years without parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's argument that because the sentence was the maximum penalty allowed by law, the sentence was excessive. The trial court had complied with the applicable sentencing statutes. The sentencing range for § 14:95.1 was 10 to 15 years without parole or probation; because defendant was convicted of attempted possession, his sentence could be up to one-half of the longest sentence prescribed for the offense attempted. The sentence was not excessive in light of defendant's extensive history, which included eight prior arrests and seven prior convictions; defendant also had four prior convictions for possession of a firearm by a convicted felon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for the attempted possession of a firearm by a convicted felon.

RCS Gaming v. State ex rel. Louisiana Gaming Control Bd.


97 CW 2317


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


97 2317 (La.App 1 Cir. 11/19/97); 705 So. 2d 1124; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2889



November 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON SUPERVISORY WRITS FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, (DOCKET NUMBER 443,018), STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE ROBERT D. DOWNING, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED IN PART; DENIED IN PART; STAY RECALLED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator state filed supervisory writs to review the decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, which overruled its exception of prematurity to respondent gaming company's challenges to an administrative rule adopted by the gaming control board.


OVERVIEW: The company challenged the validity of a rule adopted by the gaming control board on constitutional, procedural, and statutory grounds. The trial court overruled the state's exception of prematurity. On the state's petition for a supervisory writ, the court granted the writ, in part, and denied it, in part. The court determined that to the extent that the company raised constitutional challenges to the rule, the board was not authorized to decide those issues. Accordingly, the court found that the trial court correctly denied the state's exception of prematurity as to those claims. The court further observed that the legislative delegation of power in the Louisiana Gaming Control Law did not violate the separation of powers. The court concluded that the Louisiana Gaming Control Board Haring Office was the proper forum to raise issues regarding the procedural and statutory challenges to the rule. The court found that because the company was entitled to a hearing pursuant to La Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:955-956 that the trial court erred in not granting the state's exception of prematurity as to the non-constitutional challenges to the rule.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's writ, in part, and denied it, in part. The court granted the state's exception of prematurity to the extent that it related to the company's non-constitutional challenges to the administrative rule.
