State v. LeBlanc


No. 96-KA-0296


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0296 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/12/97); 702 So. 2d 377; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2694



November 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 370-222, SECTION "H". HONORABLE JAMES F. MCKAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, which convicted him of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64 and sentenced him as a triple offender.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 648A was unconstitutional because it required clear and convincing proof of mental competency and that the trial court applied the incorrect standard. The court held that defendant was only required to prove his incompetency to stand trial by a clear preponderance of the evidence. The court noted that the supreme court had previously determined that art. 648A violated the Due Process Clause to the extent that it required a defendant to prove his incompetency by clear and convincing evidence. Although the court presumed that the trial court applied the clear and convincing standard, the court concluded that defendant may not have met the preponderance of the evidence standard. Accordingly, the court remanded the case for a determination as to whether defendant proved by a preponderance of the evidence that he was not competent to stand trial.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for a determination of whether defendant proved by a preponderance of the evidence that he was not competent to proceed to trial.

 

477 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Labostrie


No. 96-KA-2003


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-2003 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/19/97); 702 So. 2d 1194; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2770



November 11, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 378-050, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES FOR ARMED ROBBERY AND ATTEMPT FIRST DEGREE ROBBERY AFFIRMED; SENTENCE FOR ATTEMPT ARMED ROBBERY AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of four counts of armed robbery, one attempted armed robbery, attempted first-degree robbery and sentenced defendant to 99 years of hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went into two banks in which he demanded and took money at gunpoint. On each occasion, a bank employee was able to identify defendant in a photographic lineup. As a result of the witness identifications, the police obtained an arrest warrant for defendant and a search warrant for his residence. They seized clothes similar to those used by defendant in one of the bank robberies. Defendant was eventually arrested. Upon his arrest, he gave a statement inculpating himself and several other individuals. Defendant was found guilty of four counts of armed robbery, one attempt armed robbery, and attempt first-degree robbery. Defendant was then sentenced to 99 years of hard labor. Defendant's major contention on appeal was that the lower court erred when it denied his motion to suppress his confessions. The court affirmed and amended. The court held that defendant's statements should not have been suppressed because there were no allegations by defendant of any force threat, coercion, or promises that caused defendant to give the confessions. Therefore, defendant had failed to rebut that his statements were freely and voluntarily made.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and amended the decision, which convicted defendant of four counts of armed robbery, attempted armed robbery, attempted first-degree robbery and sentenced defendant to 99 years of hard labor.

State v. Wilkerson


NUMBER 96 KA 1965


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 1965 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/07/97); 704 So. 2d 1; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2716



November 7, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, Trial Court No. 9-91-2161, Honorable Michael R. Erwin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile challenged the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which, after a jury trial, found him guilty of murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment without benefit of parol, probation, or suspension of sentence, but further provided that in accordance with La. Child. Code art. 857(B) that his confinement would not extend beyond his 31st birthday.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by grand jury indictment with second-degree murder pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1. After a jury trial, he was found guilty as charged. The trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence, but because defendant was 14 years old at the time of the murder, the trial court further provided in accordance with La. Child. Code art. 857(B) that defendant should not be confined beyond his 31st birthday. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court held that La. Child. Code art. 857(B) did not replace the ordinary sentencing provisions as set forth in the Louisiana Criminal Code; it provided that a child tried as an adult for specific enumerated offenses would not be confined for that offense beyond his 31st birthday. Further, the court found that the trial court did not err in transferring the case from juvenile court to a district court and that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to exclude evidence of other crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder in the second-degree.

State v. Moses


NUMBER 96 KA 2739


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 2739 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/07/97); 701 So. 2d 1382; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2749



November 7, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From The Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, Suit Number 4-96-324, Division "V", Honorable Linda Holliday, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, that departed from the minimum sentence provided by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 for habitual offenders after defendant was convicted of simple burglary, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62. The trial court denied the State's motion to reconsider the sentence, which was allegedly illegally lenient.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found stealing items from a school cafeteria and was convicted of simple burglary. Although defendant was a habitual offender, the trial court deviated from the minimum sentence proscribed by § 15:529.1 and sentenced defendant to three-years hard labor. The court affirmed the conviction and vacated the sentence, holding that the trial court failed to provide adequate justification for the departure by showing that the minimum sentence would have resulted in the needless infliction of pain and suffering. The court found no basis for the trial court's comments concerning the facts of the case. The trial court erred and failed to make a proper determination on the record to support its declaration that imposition of the statutorily mandated minimum sentence would be constitutionally excessive. Even assuming the sentence was excessive; the trial court failed to justify its deviation from the statutorily mandated minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for simple burglary and vacated the sentence imposed.

 

480 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Kroger Co.


No. 29,915-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,915 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/29/97); 702 So. 2d 347; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2450



October 29, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 397,446. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and injured wife, appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which sustained defendant supermarket's exception of prescription. Plaintiffs argued that the running of the prescriptive period provided by La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3492 was delayed and that the facsimile filing of their suit interrupted the running, and, if not, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:850 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that, until they could determine whether the wife's back pain was due to a fall at the supermarket or to the delivery of a baby a few days later, they were unable to file suit, so the suit was within an exception to art. 3492 under which prescription was suspended. On appeal, the court could not conclude that the trial court was clearly wrong in finding that the prescriptive period began to run on the date of her fall. Further, although § 13:850 allowed litigants to transmit a facsimile of a pleading to the court clerk, the statute made the effectiveness of such a filing conditional upon the delivery of the original to a clerk within five days of the transmission. Plaintiffs failed to perform that statutory condition and the court held that the facsimile filing had no force or effect. With respect to plaintiffs' constitutional challenge to § 13:850, the court held that due process did not prohibit the abolition of existing causes of action in order to attain permissible legislative objectives. Because plaintiffs failed to file suit within period required by art. 3492, they did not have a cause of action, and they had no vested property right in bringing suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining the supermarket's exception of prescription and dismissing the claims of the husband and his injured wife.

 

481 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Backest v. Louisiana Workers' Compensation


No. 29,924-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,924 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/29/97); 702 So. 2d 14; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2452



October 29, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 412,054. Honorable Charles R. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commission salesman appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by defendant Louisiana Workers' Compensation Corporation and dismissed his declaratory action seeking a determination that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(10)(d) was unconstitutionally discriminatory to private employees paid on the basis of unit, piecework, or commission.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the salesman had the burden of proving that the classification in § 23:1021(10)(d) delineating the wage calculation for differing methods of compensation was not rationally related to a legitimate state objective or did not further any appropriate state interest. The court held that the federal and state constitutions did not empower the court to second-guess legislators who were charged with the heavy responsibility of regulating the social obligations that existed between the employee, the employer, and the public. The formula in § 23:1021(10)(d) provided a reasonable and rational method for meeting the goals of the Louisiana workers' compensation statute. The fact that the classification and the formula applied to the class might result in some inequality to some members of the class did not offend the equal protection provision of the constitution because there was some reasonable basis for the classification. The court held that the trial court's conclusion that the salesman failed to show that the classification and formula provided by § 23:1021(10)(d) did not further any legitimate state interest was not clearly or legally wrong.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment and the dismissal of the salesman's declaratory action.

State v. Rachal


No. 97-642


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-642 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/29/97); 703 So. 2d 678; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2612



October 29, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court [# 233,307], Parish of Rapides, Honorable Donald Johnson, Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 233,307.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Ninth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which sentenced him to the maximum of five years at hard labor following his conviction for negligent homicide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.


OVERVIEW: During an altercation, defendant pulled a gun from his glove box. The gun discharged, killing the victim. Following defendant's conviction for negligent homicide in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32, the trial court imposed the maximum sentence of five years at hard labor. On appeal of his sentence, defendant argued that the trial court erred by failing to sufficiently set forth its reasons for imposition of sentence and by imposing an unconstitutionally excessive sentence. In affirming, the court ruled that there was an adequate factual basis for the sentence contained in the record and the trial court was not required to articulate every circumstance listed in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1. The court held that maximum sentences were reserved for the most egregious and blameworthy of offenders and that, even though defendant was a first-time offender, negligent homicide with a firearm was distinctive because guns were designed to kill. The court also noted that the district attorney did not seek a firearms enhancement under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 893.1 through 893.3 and found that this was an additional factor that the trial court may have considered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of sentence.

State v. Taylor


No. 96-KA-1843


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-1843 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/29/97); 701 So. 2d 766; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2661

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 382-744, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and the State appealed a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which found defendant guilty of attempted possession of cocaine. Based upon the State's multiple bill, defendant was also found to be a fourth offender and was sentenced to eight years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of attempted possession of cocaine. The trial court sentenced him to 30 months at hard labor. Defendant failed to prove that the State was at fault in failing to produce evidence for his review; therefore, he was not denied his right to a fair trial due to any failure to disclose by the State. The court upheld defendant's sentence, holding that the trial court properly considered defendant's age, criminal history, and that fact that none of his offenses were violent.

485 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Koeppen v. Raz


No. 29,880-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,880 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/29/97); 702 So. 2d 337; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2456



October 29, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 91,625. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED at appellants' costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the former property owner and a mortgagee, complained of a grant, by the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, of summary judgment in favor of defendant tax sale purchaser, which dismissed their petition to annul the previous tax sale on grounds that they had received notice of neither the tax delinquency nor the pending sale.


OVERVIEW: The post office returned the tax collector's notice as undeliverable. After the initial mailing was returned, the sheriff, complying with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180(B), twice published notice of the impending sale in the local newspaper to apprise the former property owner and the mortgagee of both the tax delinquency and the tax sale. Consequently, in this respect, summary judgment in favor of the tax sale purchaser properly issued. Neither the record nor the posture of the case refuted the applicability of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180.1, which required that a mortgagee specifically apprise the tax collector of its mortgage in order to be sent notice of the tax delinquency. The former property owner and the mortgagee do not dispute the fact that they did not comply with this provision and, thus, they cannot sustain the burden of proving the invalidity of the tax sale for lack of statutory notice. They also failed to plead the issue of unconstitutionality in a pleading before the trial court, did not particularize the grounds of their claim, and neglected to serve the attorney general. Under these circumstances, the issue was not properly before the court for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment below which dismissed the petition to annul the previous tax sale.

State v. Ledet


No. 97-KA-363


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


97-363 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/28/97); 701 So. 2d 1067; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2630



October 28, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 9601561, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE SUSAN CHEHARDY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Criminal District Court, Jefferson Parish (Louisiana), which sentenced him in conformity with a plea agreement for conspiracy to commit first degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:26 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his guilty plea was not knowing and voluntary because it was induced by the trial court's inaccurate representation of his sentence exposure. The record revealed that during the plea, the trial judge informed him that the maximum penalty for the charged offense was 50 years. The Waiver of Rights form also indicated that the maximum penalty was 50 years. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:26(B) actually provided for a maximum sentence of 30 years. The record showed that defendant agreed to a sentence of 20 years as part of the plea agreement. Defendant argued that he thought he was receiving a sentence that was less than half of the maximum and that he would not have agreed to the 20 years if he had known it was only ten years less than the maximum penalty. The court held that it appeared that the trial court mistakenly referred to the statute dealing with attempted murder, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27, in determining defendant's sentence exposure instead of the statute outlining the sentence for criminal conspiracy, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:26. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27 provided for a maximum sentence of 50 years.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction and sentence entered by the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court.

Tomas v. Conco Food Distribs.


NUMBER 97-426


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-426 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/22/97); 702 So. 2d 944; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2443



October 22, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, [No. 96-1535], Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana; Honorable Hugh E. Brunson, District Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 961535.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged the judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which held in his worker's compensation action against defendant employee that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(7)(e) was constitutional, denying the employee worker's compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employee sought workers' compensation benefits after suffering a stroke while attending a meeting at work. The Office of Workers' Compensation Administration denied benefits and found that it lacked jurisdiction to determine the employee's constitutional challenge to La. Rev. Stat. Subsequently, the court agreed that hearing officers were not vested with authority to rule on the constitutionality of workers' compensation statutes. Accordingly, the court remanded the case to the hearing officer, instructing her to transfer the case to the appropriate trial court for proceedings on the constitutional issue. The employee appealed the trial court's finding that § 23:1021(7)(e) did not violate the Louisiana State Constitution. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court found that the legislature had a legitimate purpose in limiting recovery for heart-related conditions caused by mental stress and that the employee was not foreclosed from bringing a tort action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the employee worker's compensation benefits.

State v. Cormier


No. CR97-382


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-382 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/15/97); 702 So. 2d 929; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2433



October 15, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Aaron Frank McGee, District Court Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 94-K-4037-B.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED AND SENTENCE VACATED ON THE POSSESSION OF OVER 400 GRAMS OF COCAINE. CASE REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT FOR RESENTENCING. CONVICTION REVERSED FOR POSSESSION WITH INTENT TO DISTRIBUTE COCAINE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Twenty- Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), which pursuant to a jury trial found him guilty of possession of 400 grams or more of cocaine as well as possession with intent to distribute cocaine. Defendant was sentenced to 45 years on his conviction for possession and 10 years on the charge of possession with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of 400 grams or more of cocaine as well as possession with intent to distribute cocaine, violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F)(1)(c) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1), respectively. He was sentenced to 45 years on the first conviction and 10 years on the second, with sentences to run concurrently. The State conceded the defendant's double jeopardy claim. Thus, the court vacated the conviction of possession with intent to distribute cocaine, the lesser offense. The court held that the trial court properly amended defendant's sentence. The court upheld defendant's conviction for possession of 400 grams or more of cocaine, but vacated his 45-year sentence as excessive and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Washington


No. 29,784-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,784 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/26/97); 700 So. 2d 1068; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2279



September 26, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 95-F0642. Honorable Michael S. Ingram, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of her conviction from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), in a bench trial, for issuing a worthless check in an amount greater than $ 500. She was sentenced to six years at hard labor and ordered to make restitution. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to convict and the excessiveness of the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant bought a car from a dealer. She gave the dealer a check for the downpayment. The check was deposited but was returned to the dealer. After she failed to honor verbal demands to make the check good, the dealer sent a registered letter demanding payment, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:71A(2). Defendant did not respond. The dealer's owner then contacted her, demanding that she either pay the check or return the car. She did neither and was arrested. She admitted at trial that she knew she did not have sufficient funds in her account to satisfy the check when she wrote it. Nor had she made restitution in any amount. She urged that the evidence was insufficient to convict. In affirming the judgment of her conviction, the court found that the statutory presumption of intent to defraud under § 14:71A(2) applied where she had refused to timely honor the check after the demand. Also, she knew she had not paid for the car and failed to timely return it to the dealer. Such conduct fell within the accepted meaning of the term "defraud." However, the court vacated the sentence, as it was the unconstitutionally excessive given her circumstances as a first-felony offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of defendant's conviction for issuing a worthless check in an amount greater than $ 500, but vacated the sentence of six years hard labor and remanded the case for resentencing.

New Hampshire Ins. Co. v. Gowen


No. 29,842-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,842 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/24/97); 699 So. 2d 1169; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2305



September 24, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 376,905. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employees challenged an order of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which limited the uninsured/underinsured motorist coverage available from plaintiff insurer on their employer's policy to $ 20,000, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1406, in the insurer's concursus proceeding. The trial court also directed that the full amount belonged to the workmen's compensation insurer under § 23:1103(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: The employees were injured in an automobile accident, in a vehicle owned by their employer, while in the course and scope of their employment. The accident was in Alabama and the other vehicle was underinsured. The court found that the employer clearly contemplated the addition and deletion of vehicles during the policy term. Thus, the addition or deletion of a vehicle did not constitute a new insurance contract that required the execution of a separate rejection or selection of uninsured/underinsured motorist (UM) coverage. Further, the selection of lower UM limits did not have to be signed at the time of the application or the issuance of the insurance policy, as long as the selection was made prior to the accident. The insurer provided sufficient testimony and documentary evidence that the rejection/selection form signed by the employer complied with statutory requirements, and that the employer understood the coverage options and intentionally and unambiguously selected lower limits of UM coverage. Finally, the trial court did not err in awarding the entire amount of the recovery to the workmen's compensation carrier, whose payments far exceeded the recovery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Costs of the appeal were assessed to the employees.

 

494 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ignot


No. 29,745-KA, No. 29,746-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,745 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/24/97); 701 So. 2d 1001; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2292



September 24, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Franklin, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 96-243F & 96-243F(A). Honorable Glynn D. Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from the Fifth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Franklin (Louisiana), where he was convicted of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:68.4. Defendant was sentenced to the mandatory term of life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence after the court applied La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was using a farmer's vehicle without permission. While police gave chase, he wrecked the car, attempted to shift blame to his passenger, and fled the scene. Defendant was convicted of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle. Following defendant's conviction for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle, the state filed a habitual offender bill against him. Defendant was found to be a third felony offender with a prior crime of violence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 and was sentenced to the mandatory term of life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant sought review. On appeal, the court found that the mandatory life sentence stipulated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 was not cruel, unusual, and excessive. The court further determined that the multiple offender bill applied because defendant did not have 10 felony-free years before committing the present offense. The court found no fault in the prior convictions or release dates submitted below. The court also concluded that the amendment of the charges that occurred prior to the trial was not error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and his sentence of a mandatory term of life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence was affirmed.

Smith v. Ouachita Parish Sch. Bd.


No. 29,873-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,873 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/24/97); 702 So. 2d 727; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2282



September 24, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 91-3035. Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school board (board) sought review from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), where judgment was rendered in favor of plaintiff tenured teacher (teacher) in the form of money damages, plus lost wages, medical specials, and attorney's fees. The case concerned the teacher's alleged demotion and her claims under the Teacher Tenure Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:444, and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was employed by the board for many years and was in a tenured position. The board assigned the teacher to the position of guidance counselor where she was negatively evaluated. She was thereafter given mundane duties and became depressed. She filed an action against the board and obtained a judgment in the form of money damages, lost wages, medical specials, and attorney's fees. The board sought review. The issues presented concerned the application of the Teacher Tenure Law, the damages awarded, and whether the teacher had a property right entitling her to due process. On review, the court determined that the teacher's statutory rights were violated under the statute. The court determined that the board failed to contract with the teacher and to set forth performance standards as required under the statute. The court observed that the teacher had a protected property right to her position. Further, the actions of the board caused the teacher much distress. The court concluded that the damages awarded were called for due to the teacher's emotional distress, whether intentionally or unintentionally inflicted, and the amount awarded was fair and was not overturned.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the teacher and against the board concerning the teacher's claims resulting from her alleged demotion was affirmed.

State v. Barnett


NO: 96 KA 2050


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 2050 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/23/97); 700 So. 2d 1005; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2276



September 23, 1997, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARY, STATE OF LOUISIANA, DOCKET NO. 142,245. HONORABLE GERARD B. WATTIGNY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana), where he was convicted of attempted second-degree murder and unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27 & 14:30.1 and 14:62.3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was furious with his wife and forcibly kicked in the door and entered the residence. He then ripped the phone from the wall and began repeatedly beating her head against a bed headboard while stating he was going to kill her. Defendant was apprehended by police while the beating was in progress. Defendant was charged with attempted second-degree murder and unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling. Defendant entered pleas of not guilty and not guilty by reason of insanity. Defendant waived his right to a jury trial; and, after a bench trial, he was found guilty as charged on both counts and thereafter sought review. On appeal, the court rejected the insufficiency of the evidence argument and found that the state proved the requisite specific intent for the offense. The trial judge was within his discretion when he rejected the contention that defendant was so drugged and/or intoxicated that he could not form the specific intent required for attempted second-degree murder. As to the sentences, the court rejected the argument that the sentences were unconstitutionally excessive. Rather, the court found the sentences were reasonable in light of the offenses.


OUTCOME: The convictions of attempted second-degree murder and unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling, as well as the sentences against defendant, were affirmed.

Standard Materials v. City of Slidell


96 CA 0684


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0684 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/23/97); 700 So. 2d 975; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2346



September 23, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 9110004), PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE STEPHEN A. DUCZER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review from the 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which rendered judgment and awarded damages to plaintiff corporation for the city's alleged denial of the corporation's substantive due process rights via a deprivation of its property.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was a concrete business and had taken substantial steps towards the construction of a plant when the city amended its zoning ordinances. This had an adverse affect on the corporation, which filed an action against the city for injunctive relief and damages due to a constitutional taking. The trial court awarded the corporation damages for the city's denial of the corporation's substantive due process rights via a deprivation of its property. The city sought review asserting an error in this determination, and the corporation answered the appeal and sought additional relief. On appeal, the court observed that there was no evidence that the city's zoning board ever denied a request for the plant. The court concluded that the corporation's claim was not ripe because the final decision of the zoning board was not adverse to the corporation which was the complaining party. The court, in addressing the merits of the action, found that the inability to operate the plant did not destroy a major portion of the property's value and therefore, there was no taking. Also, the trial court committed legal error in finding that the city acted arbitrarily and capriciously.


OUTCOME: The judgment which required the city to pay damages to the corporation for the alleged denial of the corporation's substantive due process rights via a deprivation of its property was reversed.

Livingston Downs Racing Ass'n v. State ex rel. Edwards


No. 96 CA 1988


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 1988 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/23/97); 700 So. 2d 1021; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2371



September 23, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Denied November 12, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 413,022. Honorable A. Foster Sanders, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Racing association sought review of an order of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, that denied its petition to intervene in plaintiff claimant's actions attacking the constitutionality of a provision of the Video Poker law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4862.4 and seeking injunctive relief and a judgment declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 4:211(5) and (7) and § 4:214(a)(1) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The claimant obtained a license to operate a racetrack. The legislature enacted the Offtrack Wagering Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:211 et seq., which allowed certain live horse racing associations to operate offtrack wagering facilities. The claimant filed a suit seeking injunctive relief and a judgment declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4:211(5) and (7) and 4:214(a)(1) unconstitutional. It also attacked the constitutionality of a provision of the Video Poker law, § 33:4862.4, which established the maximum jackpots that could be offered on video poker devices. Intervenor racing association filed a petition to intervene. The trial judge denied its request. The intervenor appealed and the court reversed. The intervenor satisfied the two-fold test of La. Code Civ. Pro. Ann. art. 1091. The intervenor had a justiciable interest in, and a connexity to, the principle action. The intervenor sought to join the state in defending the constitutionality of the very provision which gave it the statutory authority to offer larger video poker jackpots than other businesses. It had an economic interest in preserving its right to conduct business pursuant to the statute attacked by the claimant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that denied the racing association's petition to intervene in the claimant's actions attacking the constitutionality of a provision of the Video Poker law and a judgment declaring the other statutes in question unconstitutional.

96 1510 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/19/97); 701 So. 2d 457; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2356



September 19, 1997, Rendered

He appeared before the paroled board, but parole was denied based on the serious nature of the offense, police and/or juvenile records, prior felony conviction(s), and law enforcement and/or judicial objection. He then sought a petition for a writ of habeas corpus stating that, although his original conviction and sentence were lawful, his continuation in custody was unlawful because the parole board violated his constitutional rights to due process. The lower court denied habeas corpus and he sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment on the grounds that the Louisiana parole statutes had not created an expectancy of release or liberty interest in general, or for those with life terms in particular.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed petitioner's writ of habeas corpus.

State v. Silva


No. 96-KA-0407


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0407 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/03/97); 699 So. 2d 487; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2161



September 3, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused September 30, 1997. Released for Publication September 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 371-003, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans, Section "B" (Louisiana) of first degree murder, on the grounds that the trial court improperly refused access to sources of the state's psychiatrist and applied the wrong standard with regard to whether he was competent to proceed with trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first degree robbery, and was found guilty. His expert testified that defendant was insane at the time of the offense, and did not know right from wrong. The state's expert testified that defendant was sane at the time of the offense. Defendant requested through discovery procedures all the sources from which the state's expert drew to form his opinion and make his report, pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 719, but the trial court refused. Defendant argued that the trial court improperly applied the clear and convincing evidence standard of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 648(A) in the determination of whether he was competent to proceed with trial. The court held that the state was required to produce to defendant the report of its expert, which it did, but not the sources relied upon by the expert in forming the report. The court held that the trial court should have used the preponderance of the evidence standard regarding defendant's capacity, but that even under that standard defendant failed to demonstrate his incapacity. The court affirmed defendant's conviction of first degree murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

City of Kenner v. Jumonville

Writ denied by City of Kenner v. Jumonville, 709 So. 2d 718, 1998 La. LEXIS 465 (La., Jan. 30, 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Jumonville v. City of Kenner, 524 U.S. 953, 118 S. Ct. 2371, 141 L. Ed. 2d 739, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4309 (1998)
Writ denied by City of Kenner v. Jumonville, 721 So. 2d 477, 1998 La. LEXIS 2700 (La., Sept. 16, 1998)
Related proceeding at City of Kenner v. Jumonville, 793 So. 2d 574, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1348 (La.App. 5 Cir., Apr. 11, 2001)
Related proceeding at City of Kenner v. Jumonville, 927 So. 2d 574, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 651 (La.App. 5 Cir., Mar. 28, 2006)
Related proceeding at Jumonville v. City of Kenner, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 816 (La.App. 5 Cir., Mar. 26, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 481-536, DIVISION "I". HONORABLE JO ELLEN GRANT, JUDGE.
City of Kenner v. Jumonville, 694 So. 2d 221, 1997 La. LEXIS 1775 (La., May 22, 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED; WRIT APPLICATIONS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which held them in contempt of court for failing to abide by a consent agreement with plaintiff city government over the renovation of their house, claiming that finding of contempt was erroneous, and that they should not have to pay a fine.


OVERVIEW: Property owners failed to renovate their house and the city sued them for creating a nuisance. Eventually the owners and the city entered into a consent agreement, whereby the owners would complete the repairs on the house. After the owners failed to renovate, the city brought suit, seeking a finding of contempt. The trial court found the owners in contempt and ordered them to pay damages to the city. The owners appealed the ruling, claiming that it was erroneous. The court held that the consent agreement was a bilateral contract which was binding, and could not be directly appealed to the court. The court stated that it could not invalidate the agreement on the grounds that it was a bad deal or more expensive than anticipated. The court determined that the consent agreement was valid and enforceable, and therefore the trial court correctly found the owners in contempt for failing to live up to their agreement. However, the court concluded that the amount of the fine was excessive, and should be reduced. Finally, the court ordered that the fine was payable to the court and not to the city, because it was remedial in nature.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the lower court, and affirmed as modified.

McChesney v. Penn


No. 29,776-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,776 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/20/97); 698 So. 2d 705; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2084



August 20, 1997, Judgment rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 387,343. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagee appealed the judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which found that defendant purchaser was the owner of a tract of immovable property acquired pursuant to a tax sale from the city.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of the mortgagee's action to quiet title the mortgagee argued that as mortgagee of the property, he did not get notice of the impending city tax sale, rendering that sale a nullity; and that La. Rev. Stat. Ann § 47:2180.1, which required the mortgagee to notify the tax collector of any recorded mortgage, was unconstitutional because it shifted the burden from the tax collector to the mortgagee of ensuring adequate notice. The tax sale purchaser of the property argued that the mortgagee had failed to establish that he was entitled to notice under La. Rev. Stat. Ann § 47:2180.1. The court held that that the mortgagee was not reasonably identifiable and therefore constructive notice of the tax sale satisfied due process requirements as to him. Further, under the facts presented in this case, the mortgagee's Fourteenth Amendment Due Process rights were not violated, and § 47:2180.1 had no bearing on the court's decision; thus the constitutionality of the statute was not addressed.


OUTCOME: Th court affirmed the judgment of the trial court quieting and confirming title and ownership of the disputed property in the tax sale purchaser.

Boudoin v. Nicholson, Baehr, Calhoun & Lanasa


No. 96-CA-0363


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0363 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/30/97); 698 So. 2d 469; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 2005



July 30, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 92-18776, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a radiologist and the state patient's compensation fund, sought review of an order of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which awarded damages to plaintiffs, a widow and the adult children of the deceased, based upon a finding that the radiologist had breached the applicable standard of care.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the radiologist's improper reading of deceased's x-ray resulted in a loss of chance to survive a chest wall cancer. The radiologist argued peremption and that the jury was manifestly erroneous in finding that the deceased might have survived if his cancer had been diagnosed eleven months earlier because the testimony did not reasonably support that conclusion. The family contended that the facts and circumstances were insufficient to infer that the widow's discussion with the pulmonologist put them on notice that malpractice had occurred or that any harm had thereby resulted, and that their claims were timely filed within one year of deceased's death. The court held that the family's claims to recover for injuries suffered by the deceased were perempted by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628; only compensation for their own losses arising from his death may be recovered. The court held that in view of the diagnosis and the general agreement on the favorable outlook if a sarcoma were promptly detected and treated while small, the jury could reasonably conclude that the eleven month delay contributed to the deceased's failure to survive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court as to liability but amended the damages awarded in the family's claim for the deceased's lost chance to survive.

Liberty Mut. Ins. Co. v. Louisiana Ins. Rating Comm'n


96 CA 0793


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0793 (La.App. 1 Cir. 07/02/97); 696 So. 2d 1021; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1772



July 2, 1997, Decided  
July 2, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 2, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Parish of East Baton Rouge.

Original Opinion of February 14, 1997, Reported at: 1997 La. App. LEXIS 392.



DISPOSITION: The application for rehearing filed by LIRC and by Liberty Mutual are DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance company and defendants, the Louisiana Insurance Rating Commission, its chairman, and its members, filed applications for rehearing of the court's decision to reverse a trial court judgment that declared a commission bulletin to be a rule and that declared the rule null and void. The court reversed the judgment because it was not rendered in conformity with the procedural requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:963.


OVERVIEW: The commission asserted that the court's decision went too far in finding its rule invalid. The court, however, noted that its decision made no substantive finding that the rule was invalid. Therefore, the court found the commission's complaint on rehearing to be without merit. The company's basic complaint on rehearing was that it did not like the stringent requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:963(D), which was part of the Louisiana Administrative Procedures Act. Although the court agreed with the company that there were some serious problems with § 49:963(D), the court concluded that if any reform or modification to § 49:963(D) was to be made, it would have to be done by the legislature or by the Louisiana Supreme Court when faced with a constitutional issue. The court rejected the company's assertion that the court's opinion was in conflict with an earlier decision. The court also rejected the company's argument that the trial court was the proper forum to address the alleged unconstitutionality of the commission's bulletin, finding that the case could be disposed of on the basis of nonconstitutional issues.


OUTCOME: The court denied the applications for rehearing that were filed by the company and by the commission.

State v. Banks


No. CR95-1210


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-1210 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/25/97); 699 So. 2d 418; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1698



June 25, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, STATE OF LOUISIANA; THE HON. GEORGE METOYER, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING. Lower Court Number: 239,445.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which upheld a jury verdict that found defendant guilty of an aggravated crime against nature in soliciting a teenage boy to perform oral sex and sentenced defendant to 12 years.


OVERVIEW: A teenage male was solicited by defendant, who was a coach at a YMCA, to engage in an act of oral sex. The teenager told the sports director at the YMCA about the incident. Defendant was charged with an aggravated crime against nature in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89.1. The sports director testified about her conversation with the teenager. A jury convicted defendant as charged. The trial court sentenced defendant to 12 years in prison at hard labor without benefit of parole or suspension of sentence. Defendant sought review, contending that his sentence was excessive. On appeal the court held that an excessive sentence was nothing more than the needless imposition of pain and suffering, however, the legislature was authorized to punish a more offensive type of conduct more severely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the aggravated crime against nature in soliciting a teenage boy to perform oral sex, but reduced defendant's twelve year in prison sentence to seven and one-half years.

Ready v. HHS


NUMBER 95-1564


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-1564 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/25/97); 707 So. 2d 1250; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1696



June 25, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] On Rehearing March 25, 1998, Reported: 1998 La. App. LEXIS 572. Released for Publication November 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Seventh Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Catahoula, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Leo Boothe, Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 18,272.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state department of health and human services, sought review of a decision of the Seventh Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Catahoula (Louisiana), which granted appellee parents damages in a tort alleging the wrongful removal of their son.


OVERVIEW: The parents had an ongoing tumultuous relationship over number of years. The parents' two oldest children were taken from them and the State assumed custody after juvenile proceedings. The parents' son was taken, with the father's sister being temporary custody for six months. The son's aunt had the boy for over five years, during which time it was alleged that the boy, when he was four, molested his younger sister after witnessing sexual acts performed by his aunt. The parents filed a tort suit alleging wrongful removal of their son. The trial court granted the parents and their daughter substantial damages. On appeal the court held that the State's involvement with the son ceased after the six months and a one-year liberative prescription period began to run after that point. In any event, the State could not be liable because the boy was not in the State's custody.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered the damage award to the parents in the tort action against the State alleging the wrongful removal of the their son.

State v. Mitchell


NUMBER 96 KA 1896


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 1896 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/20/97); 697 So. 2d 22; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1690



June 20, 1997, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Mary. State of Louisiana. Suit No. 142,493. Honorable John E. Conery, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AFFIRMED, AS AMENDED; AND, CASE REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree robbery and simple escape. He was subsequently billed a habitual offender on the robbery conviction in the 16th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana). The district court sentenced him on the conviction as a third felony offender to life imprisonment without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant alleged that the life sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was billed as a habitual offender after his conviction for first degree robbery and escape. Thereafter, the district court sentenced him on the robbery conviction as a third felony offender to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed. He urged that the life sentence imposed by the district court was excessive. The court found that the life sentence imposed was not grossly disproportionate to defendant's crimes. First degree robbery was a serious offense that involved force or intimidation, when the offender lead the victim to reasonably believe he was armed with a dangerous weapon, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.1. The robbery and use of force or intimidation by defendant was not an isolated incident. Defendant was a third felony offender. Thus, no proportionality review was necessary. However, if the court conducted such a review, based upon the facts in the record, the court would have found that the sentence imposed by the district court was tailored to both the offender and the offense, and was not excessive. Accordingly, the court found no merit in defendant's assignment of error.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed. The sentences were affirmed, as amended, and the case was remanded with order.

 

508 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


City of Baton Rouge v. DiVincenti


NUMBER 96 CA 2662


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 2662 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/20/97); 697 So. 2d 1; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1717



June 20, 1997, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 425,632. Honorable A. Foster Sanders, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner in an action under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4712 for the abatement of a public nuisance complained of an adverse judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, contending that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and, alternatively, that plaintiff city failed to adequately comply with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4713.


OVERVIEW: The city asserted that the property owner's residences supported the maintenance of a nuisance as defined in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4711 et seq. The property owner contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4711(A)(2) failed to explain what was required of a person to avoid an injunction or contempt citation, or how an owner can avoid "permitting" the nuisance to exist. The court held that, to avoid the issuance of a permanent injunction, the property owner must maintain nuisance-free premises. The statute simply forbade the act of maintaining a nuisance; it did not place any affirmative duty on the property owner. The language was sufficient to give persons of ordinary intelligence fair notice of what conduct is prohibited. Therefore, that language did not render the statute void for vagueness. The court held, however, that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4713B set forth the procedure to be followed by the city in obtaining an injunction or order of abatement, and that the trial court erred in granting a permanent injunction without first conducting a preliminary hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the property owner's exception of no cause of action. The court vacated the judgment issuing the injunction, and remanded this case for further proceedings.

 

509 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


MRT Exploration Co. v. McNamara


NUMBER 94 CA 0063R CONSOLIDATED WITH NUMBER 94 CA 0064R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 0063 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/20/97); 703 So. 2d 40; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1705



June 20, 1997, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended on Grant of Rehearing January 8, 1998, Reported at: 1998 La. App. LEXIS 25.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. SUIT NUMBERS 262,928 AND 323,597. HONORABLE WILLIAM BROWN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Secretary of Revenue and Taxation challenged a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, and on remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court, the court held that plaintiff taxpayers owed severance taxes for the period of December, 1979, through September, 1982.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought to recover severance taxes paid under protest. On a prior remand, the court had determined that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 52:1, prior to its amendment, exempted land acquired by the United States from all taxation, including severance taxes, and that the 1982 amendment to § 52:1 was intended to specifically authorize the imposition of severance taxes upon natural resources severed from within the confines of land acquired by the United States. The secretary appealed and the Louisiana Supreme Court remanded the case for reconsideration, that court having held that the state could lawfully impose severance taxes on fugitive oil and gas captured from beneath a portion of the lands within the confines of a federal enclave for the taxable period of January 1, 1980 through September 10, 1982. The court noted that the legislature, in amending § 52:1, intended to make clear its authorization for the imposition of severance taxes on mineral lessees of federal lands, and also noted that this authorization had always existed under state law. The court held, therefore, that the taxpayers owed severance taxes for the period of December, 1979, through September, 1982.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the State of Louisiana, plaintiff in reconvention, awarding taxes, together with interest.

State v. Galliano


NUMBER 96 KA 1736


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT

State v. Moore


96 KA 1835


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 1835 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/20/97); 696 So. 2d 657; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1729



June 20, 1997, DATE OF JUDGMENT


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 1-96-469-V), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE LINDA HOLLIDAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRM CONVICTION AND SENTENCE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, which sentenced her to imprisonment at hard labor for five years without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence after she pleaded guilty to conspiracy to commit first degree robbery.


OVERVIEW: Police received information that a grocery store would be robbed. Defendant was arrested along with two others before the crime could be committed. Defendant admitted that she participated in planning the robbery and was to share in its proceeds. Defendant was charged with conspiracy to commit first degree robbery. After defendant withdrew her initial plea of not guilty and pled guilty, the trial court sentenced her to imprisonment at hard labor for five years without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Her motion to reconsider sentence was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:26(C), defendant was to be sentenced in the same manner as the offense contemplated by the conspirators. First degree robbery required that the entire sentence be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The trial court did not misunderstand the applicable penalty and did not apply the incorrect law in sentencing defendant. The trial court considered the mitigating factors urged by defendant, but noted the seriousness of the crime and defendant's "blase" attitude toward it. Defendant's sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for conspiracy to commit first degree armed robbery.

Related proceeding at Gay v. Leblanc, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 156496 (M.D. La., Oct. 30, 2015)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at State ex rel. Gay v. State, 186 So. 3d 651, 2016 La. LEXIS 586 (La., 2016)
Writ dismissed by State ex rel. Gay v. State, 2016 La. LEXIS 1397 (La., June 3, 2016)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed the victim and shot him while the victim's wife and child watched. Defendant, who had a prior felony drug conviction, admitted that he was at the scene of the crime and struggled with the victim, but said that the gun went off during a struggle. He was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced. He sought review arguing that the trial court erred in failing to grant a mistrial under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 770. The court held that defendant was not erroneously prohibited from presenting evidence about his criminal intent because although relevant, the evidence's probative value was substantially outweighed by other factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of first-degree murder.

Priola v. Calcasieu Parish Police Jury


NUMBER 97-161


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-161 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/04/97); 696 So. 2d 183; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1532



June 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 1, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Arthur J. Planchard, Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 95-3182.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parish ward residents appealed a judgment from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) which denied their demand for a declaratory judgment concerning the interpretation of changes to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:281(I) enacted by 1989 La. Acts 585 concerning the sale of beer and the effect given those changes by defendant Calcasieu Parish Police Jury.


OVERVIEW: The sale of three and two-tenths percent by weight alcohol beer had never been prohibited by a referendum of the residents of the parish. When La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:281(I) was amended to allow the sale of alcohol up to six percent by volume in any political subdivision which had approved the sale of three and two-tenths percent alcohol beer, the Police Jury enacted an ordinance making it legal to sell six percent beer, unless and until this was disapproved by referendum. In affirming the judgment, the court held that this was the correct interpretation of the effect of the amendment to § 26:281(I). The court held that by failing to ban three and two-tenths beer, the parish residents had in fact approved its sale. Three and two-tenths beer having been approved, albeit tacitly, by the parish residents, the Police Jury was within its lawful authority in enacting an ordinance that permitted the sale of six percent beer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in the residents' declaratory judgment action against the Police Jury.

 

514 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kittlin


No. CR97-92


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-92 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/04/97); 695 So. 2d 1137; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1538



June 4, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-EIGHTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LASALLE, STATE OF LOUISIANA; THE HON. J.P. MAUFFRAY, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING. Lower Court Number: 55573.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Twenty-Eighth Judicial District Court, Parish of LaSalle, State of Louisiana, which adjudicated defendant a third felony offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, which vacated his prior, plea bargained sentence upon his plea of guilty to attempted possession of cocaine, and which imposed a habitual offender sentence on him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to attempted possession of cocaine and the trial court sentenced defendant pursuant to the terms of his plea bargain. The State subsequently filed a habitual offender bill against defendant. The trial court adjudicated defendant a third felony offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15: 529.1, vacated the plea bargain sentence, and imposed a habitual offender sentence on defendant. On appeal, the court reviewed the case for errors patent on the face of the record pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 920, and remanded the case for further consideration. The trial court committed plain error by not giving defendant credit for time served as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 880. If the State agreed not to enhance defendant's sentence as a habitual offender, the plea bargain had to be upheld. If defendant reasonably believed that the State would not seek to enhance his sentence, his guilty plea had to be set aside as being involuntary. If the State promised not to use the current conviction as an enhancement for any future convictions, the plea bargain was void as against public policy, and defendant was entitled to withdraw his plea.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to determine the State's agreement for defendant's plea of guilty to attempted cocaine possession. Defendant could not be sentenced as a third felony offender if the State agreed not to enhance his sentence. Defendant's plea had to be set aside if he reasonably but inaccurately believed the State made that promise, or if the State improperly agreed not to use the current conviction to enhance any future convictions.

 

515 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. Roemer


No. 96-CA-2133


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-2133 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/04/97); 696 So. 2d 252; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1551



June 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 17, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 89-24694, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE MAX N. TOBIAS, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, former nonteaching employees of a parish school board, appealed the judgment from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which found that the amendments to La. Rev. Stat. § 17:524 in 1988 La. Acts 79 did not violate their equal protection rights under La. Const. art. I, § 3 (1974), and which entered judgment for defendant parish school board on the employees' suit for wrongful termination.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:524 as amended by 1988 La. Acts 79, a parish school board eliminated the positions of two nonteaching employees due to lack of funds. The employees sued the board for wrongful termination, and alleged that the amendment violated their equal protection rights under La. Const. art. I, § 3 (1974) because teachers were not subject to the amendment. The trial court found that the amendment was constitutional and entered judgment for the board. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that because the classifications in the amendment were not specifically enumerated in La. Const. art. I, § 3 (1974), the employees had the burden of proving that the classification were not rationally related to a legitimate government purpose. Because the paramount purpose of the school board was to educate children, and because teachers were essential to that purpose, the employees did not meet their burden. The board properly eliminated the positions by the adoption of a budget, and the evidence showed that the board had limited funds. Therefore, the judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which found that a law that allowed a school board to reduce the number of its nonteaching employees, but not its teachers, for budgetary reasons did not violate the nonteaching employees' equal protection rights under the Louisiana Constitution, and which entered judgment for a parish school board on the employees' suit for wrongful discharge.

Crown Bev. Co. v. Dixie Brewing Co.


No. 96-CA-2103


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-2103 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/28/97); 695 So. 2d 1090; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1484



May 28, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 96-12968, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE MICHAEL G. BAGNERIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant-appellant beer supplier sought review of the judgment of the Civil District Court, Parish of New Orleans (Louisiana), granting the motion of plaintiff-appellee, a beer wholesaler, for a preliminary injunction that prevented the beer supplier from violating La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 26:801-812 by terminating a contract entered into with the beer wholesaler.


OVERVIEW: A beer supplier and a beer wholesaler had a wholesale sales agreement obligating the wholesaler to maximize the sales of the supplier's beer in a geographical area. Concerned about dropping beer sales, the supplier gave notice of its intent to terminate pursuant to a contractual provision entitling it to terminate the agreement according to its sole discretion. The wholesaler filed suit against the supplier, contending that the termination would violate La. Rev. Stat. It held that the statute expressed a legislative intent that the 1993 statute not be retroactive, and thus that the statute did not regulate the 1990 contract between the parties. The court specifically held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:803 did not apply to the termination provision in the parties' contract.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the preliminary injunction and remanded the case.

State v. Lacoste


No. 97-K-1113


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


97-1113 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/28/97); 695 So. 2d 1121; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1493



May 28, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF CERTIORARI AND PROHIBITION FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 384-606 and 384-6152, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; SENTENCE VACATED; AND CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State applied for a writ of certiorari and prohibition from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which, under a plea bargain, sentenced defendant to 10 years imprisonment upon his plea of guilty to possession of cocaine and battery of a police officer under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967(C) and 14:34.2, rather than to life imprisonment as mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii) for a third felony offender.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea bargain, defendant pled guilty to possession of cocaine and battery of a police officer under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967(C) and 14:34.2, and the trial court sentenced defendant to 10 years imprisonment. The State applied for a writ of certiorari and prohibition challenging the sentence, and the court granted the writ, vacated the sentence and remanded the case for reconsideration. Because defendant was a third felony offender, his minimum mandatory sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii) was life imprisonment. The trial court failed to justify its deviation from the mandatory minimum sentence by stating the facts that made the minimum sentence so grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offense so as to shock the sense of justice. Therefore, the sentence was improper and the trial court had to resentence defendant to the maximum sentence that was not constitutionally excessive, and to justify any deviation from the mandated minimum. If the new sentence was greater than 10 years, defendant was entitled to an opportunity to withdraw his guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's application for a writ of certiorari and prohibition, vacated defendant's sentence, and remanded the case for the trial court to impose the maximum constitutional sentence, to justify any change from the statutory minimum for a third felony offender, and to allow defendant to withdraw his pleas of guilty to cocaine possession and battery of a police officer if the new sentence was more than the plea bargain sentence.

State v. Neville


No. 96-KA-0137


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0137 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/21/97); 695 So. 2d 534; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1467



May 21, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT FOR ORLEANS. PARISH NO. 371-790, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED. REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Criminal District Court for Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of purse snatching under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65.1, and which sentenced him as a multiple offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took a wallet from his victim's purse as the victim was boarding a bus. As a result, defendant was convicted of purse snatching under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:65.1 and was sentenced as a multiple offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's pro se request to change his appointed counsel. The bystanders' cries were admissible under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 801D(4) to show why the victim chased defendant rather than hearsay under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 801C, and were also admissible excited utterances under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 803(1)(2). The conviction was proper even if defendant only picked up the wallet if the victim dropped it. Because all of defendant's convictions were for nonviolent felonies, the sentence was excessive and violated La. Const. art. I, § 20, although it was the minimum sentence for a multiple offender. Therefore, although the conviction was proper, the sentence was not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of purse snatching. The court vacated defendant's sentence as a multiple offender and remanded the case for resentencing.

Damone v. Whitley


96 CA 0635


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0635 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/09/97); 694 So. 2d 1205; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1473



May 9, 1997, Judgment rendered
