DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, which dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus and mandamus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pled guilty to murder and was sentenced to serve the balance of his natural life at hard labor. While serving his life sentence, petitioner asked to have his master prison record changed to reflect that he was parole eligible, thus, enabling him to apply for parole consideration. His request was denied and he filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus and mandamus. In his pleadings, he requested the issuance of an order stating that he was to be considered immediately eligible for parole consideration. The commissioner found petitioner had failed to prove that the law in effect on the date of his offense allowed for parole eligibility on his life sentence. Based on that finding and the commissioner's adjudication, the district court's judgment dismissed his claim, with prejudice. From that judgment, he sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment on the grounds that due to the requirements of the current and former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(B), parole consideration would have been withheld from petitioner, by operation of law, despite the fact that the applicable penalty provision had not or could not include the words "without benefit of parole."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed petitioner's writ of habeas corpus and mandamus.

Batiste v. Capitol Home Health


No. 96-799


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-799 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/07/97); 699 So. 2d 395; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1296



May 7, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT 02, PARISH OF AVOYELLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA; KATHRYN VAN HOOF, ADMINISTRATIVE HEARING OFFICER, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed from the decision of the Office of Workers' Compensation (Louisiana), which ordered he employer to provide disability benefits, medical expenses and rehabilitation services to plaintiff employee. Additionally, the employer appealed the adverse awards of attorney fees and penalties, and the employee appealed, seeking an increase in the amount of her penalty and wage determinations and additional attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The employer contended that claimant's medical benefits were timely paid, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201(F), because a statute extended the payment period from 14 to 60 days. On appeal, the court found that the statute was procedural, but concluded that it did not apply retroactively because retroactive application would have operated to unconstitutionally disturb the employee's vested rights to compensation of her medical bills within 14 days. The court found no merit to the employer's alternate theory that penalties could not be awarded for its failure to provide medical benefits, but only for its failure to pay wage benefits because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201 was amended to provide for a penalty on any unpaid medical benefits. The court further held that the employer waived its opportunity to protest its financial responsibility for the employee's rehabilitation efforts because the employer failed to comply with rehabilitation efforts set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1226. The court also concluded that the employee was allowed to have her fringe benefits included in her wage calculation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the hearing officer, reversing as to the wage computation and penalty assessment.

State v. Kennerson


NUMBER CR96-1518


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-1518 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/07/97); 695 So. 2d 1367; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1297



May 7, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Twelfth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana; the Honorables Angelo Piazza, III, and Michael J. Johnson, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 12th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana, which convicted him of with two counts of simple burglary, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplices entered two unlocked trucks in a driveway, removed various items, and left. They also stole frozen meat from another victim's home. Defendant was charged with and convicted of simple burglary, sentenced to 20 years on each count to run consecutively, and sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, vacated the sentences, and remanded for resentencing on the grounds that the trial court did not give defendant credit toward service of his sentence for time spent in actual custody before the imposition of sentence. The court rejected defendant's argument that his convictions were invalid because there was no physical evidence proving that he was present at the crime scenes due to there being no legal requirement that physical evidence had to be produced to support a conviction. The court held that even thought the State failed to properly produce and authentic, admissible documents in order to meet its burden to prove defendant a habitual offender the errors were harmless. The court found that the trial court could have multiple billed convictions rendered on the same day.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded the judgment that convicted defendant of simple burglary.

 

523 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simons


No. 29,544-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,544 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/07/97); 694 So. 2d 593; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1383



May 7, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 95-F0818. Honorable Charles E. Joiner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of possession of methamphetamine after entering a plea of guilty, sought review of a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), which imposed a sentence of five years at hard labor that defendant considered excessive.


OVERVIEW: The police discovered defendant sitting in a car with a loaded rifle. After he stepped out of the car and was given Miranda rights, the police noted a syringe on the car floor and found methamphetamine in his pocket. In exchange for pleading guilty to possession, a firearm charge was dropped and the state agreed not to prosecute him as a habitual offender, as he had a previous conviction. Upon being sentenced to five years at hard labor, defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court failed to adequately articulate reasons for the sentence, as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, and that it was excessive. The court disagreed, explaining that it would not set aside a sentence in the absence of an abuse of discretion. Applying a two-step analysis, the court ruled that the trial court considered the factors listed in the statute, namely, personal history, prior record, seriousness of the offense, and likelihood of rehabilitation, reviewed a presentence investigation report, found no mitigating factors, and considered as an aggravating factor defendant's serious drug problem. As there was an undue risk he would commit another offense, the sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence affirmed.

 

524 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Keys


Nos. 29,369-KA and 29,370-KA (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,369 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/07/97); 694 So. 2d 1107; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1385



May 7, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 32,412 and 32,412-A. Honorable Leon H. Whitten, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction, by the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jackson, Louisiana, for possession of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967 C, and his adjudication as a fourth felony offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 A(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of cocaine possession, adjudicated a fourth felony offender, and sentenced to mandatory life in prison. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. It held that sufficient evidence supported the conviction and that the trial court did not err in failing to grant a mistrial based on a testifying police officer's vague reference to defendant's prior bad acts. It further held that the application of the life imprisonment provision of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 A(1)(c)(ii) did not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws, and that because the offense with which defendant was initially charged was not punishable by life imprisonment, he need not have been indicted by a grand jury. The court also held that the fact that defendant's sentence for possession of cocaine apparently reflected his prior felony history did not exempt him from sentence as a multiple offender; that there was no error in regarding his guilty pleas to aggregate worthless check offenses as predicate offenses for the adjudication; that he was adequately identified as the person convicted of the prior felonies; and that the life sentence was not constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and adjudication as a fourth felony offender.

State v. Gibson


NUMBER CR97-108


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


97-0108 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/30/97); 693 So. 2d 286; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1186



April 30, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Aaron Frank McGee, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number 96-K-1253-B.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), which convicted her of vehicular homicide and sentenced to her to nine years hard labor.


OVERVIEW: A vehicle driven north on a highway by defendant crossed the grassy median separating the north and south lanes of the highway, became airborne, and collided with a southbound vehicle that was driven by a 20-year-old nursing student. The nursing student was pronounced dead at the scene. Defendant had been drinking heavily before the accident, and three hours after the accident her blood-alcohol concentration was 0.17 percent by weight based upon grams of alcohol per 100 cubic centimeters of blood. It was not disputed that defendant was under the influence of alcohol at the time of the accident. Defendant was found guilty of vehicular homicide and sentenced to nine years hard labor. On appeal defendant alleged that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that her blood-alcohol concentration, combined with her operation of the vehicle, caused the death of the nursing student. The court held that the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's intoxication or alcohol level was a contributing factor of the accident. The court agreed that there was no evidence of any other factor that would have been an intervening cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision which convicted defendant of vehicular homicide and sentenced to her to nine years hard labor.

Wilson v. City of New Orleans


No. 95-CA-2129


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-2129 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/30/97); 693 So. 2d 344; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1224



April 30, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 92-15606, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE YADA T. MAGEE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pedestrian appealed from the judgment of the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans, Division "F" (Louisiana), which dismissed his action against defendant city for damages resulting when he slipped and fell on a post used to close part of a city street.


OVERVIEW: The pedestrian was injured while walking in the French Quarter after he tripped on a cement post used to close the street to vehicular traffic. The posts were placed each day into holes in the pavement, were painted light green, and were 38 inches high. The pedestrian claimed to have walked past several sets of posts without event before tripping, but could not indicate exactly which bent post caused him to fall. The city claimed that the posts were not defective, that it had no notice that the post upon which the pedestrian tripped was bent, and that it had never received complaints regarding a pedestrian tripping on a post prior to the pedestrian's complaint. The trial court dismissed the pedestrian's action. The court held that the pedestrian failed to demonstrate that the city had constructive notice of the post, because the posts were placed not more than several hours prior to the accident, and were removed each day. The court held that the post was not defective, and affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the pedestrian's action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the pedestrian's action.

Department of Social Servs. v. McCorkle


No. 97-CA-13


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment from the Juvenile Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which found him to be the biological father of the minor child and ordered him to pay child support in an action brought by appellees, the mother and the department of social services.


OVERVIEW: Blood tests performed on the child and the father established paternity. The father filed requests for admissions, pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. The trial court found that paternity was properly established and ordered support. The court held that the trial court did not err in failing to consider the requests for admissions as facts admitted by the mother. The court also rejected the father's argument that the child support and that the enforcement of support for a child was not prohibited because the biological father did not agree, by consent or by contract, to become a father or to provide support for his child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that established paternity and ordered the father to pay child support.

Cressey v. Foster


96 CA 2716


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96-2716 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/25/97); 694 So. 2d 1016; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1263



April 25, 1997, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 431,846), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE A. FOSTER SANDERS, III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a private citizen and a children's and welfare rights advocacy organization, sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, which ruled against plaintiffs in their action for injunctive relief against defendants, the Governor of Louisiana, the Secretary of the Louisiana Department of Social Services, and the Louisiana Department of Social Services.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and stay to prevent irreparable injury from defendants' intended violation of public notice requirements. Specifically, it was a petition for injunctive relief to prevent defendants from causing irreparable injury by carrying out their stated intention to take certain voluntary actions which would have effectuated their own voluntary policy choices as to how and when to implement the new federal welfare reform law, without giving the public prior notice of their policy choices or an opportunity to comment. The lower court denied preliminary injunctive relief and later ruled against plaintiffs who sought review arguing that the lower court erred in finding that the challenged policies adopted by emergency rule were temporarily justified. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment on the grounds that the trial court was correct in finding that the emergency rulemaking undertaken by the department was authorized by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:953. The court found that it was evident that emergency rulemaking was not intended to take the place of regular rulemaking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied plaintiffs' injunctive relief.

Brown v. Louisiana Indem. Co.


No. 96-1393


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-1393 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/23/97); 693 So. 2d 270; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1110



April 23, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Thirty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen, State of Louisiana; the Honorable John P. Navarre, District Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: C-89-185.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Louisiana, Through the Department of Transportation and Development sought review of a judgment of the 33rd Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen, State of Louisiana, which assessed it to be 75 percent at fault in plaintiff passengers' negligence action.


OVERVIEW: A small vehicle being operated by a driver left the paved portion of a state highway and traveled on the shoulder portion of the road and then became air borne when the vehicle hit an abandoned driveway and then crashed into a tree. The vehicle was split into two pieces and the passengers were severely injured. The passengers filed actions against department seeking damages as a result of the accident. The lower court held against the department and it sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment on the grounds that there was no satisfactory explanation for the reason preventive maintenance work was not done because it was quite clear that the department had actual or constructive notice of the defect prior to the accident, and it had a reasonable opportunity to remedy the defect, yet it failed to do so. The court held that it was clearly the excessive cross-slope and the abandoned driveway which were responsible for propelling the vehicle toward the pine trees. The court further ruled that there was no question that the department's fault was more substantial for the resulting harm than the fault of the driver.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that held against the department.

State v. Jackson


No. 96-KA-661


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


96-661 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/09/97); 694 So. 2d 440; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 996



April 9, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 17, 1997.
Writ denied by State v. Jackson, 703 So. 2d 609, 1997 La. LEXIS 3209 (La., Oct. 13, 1997)
Writ denied by State v. Jackson, 703 So. 2d 612, 1997 La. LEXIS 3221 (La., Oct. 13, 1997)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Jackson v. State, 2005 La. LEXIS 711 (La., Mar. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 94-6931, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE SUSAN M. CHEHARDY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, No. 94-6931, Division "N," which imposed consecutive sentences of 40 years at hard labor for his aggravated kidnapping conviction and 198 years for armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant robbed restaurant employees of money and a police officer of his weapon at gunpoint, ran to a residence to hide, and locked the elderly residents in the bathroom. Defendant appealed his armed robbery and aggravated kidnapping convictions. The court affirmed because defendant failed to make a contemporaneous objections to a reasonable doubt instruction, the questioning of the co-defendant, and the trial court's failure to question jurors about a newspaper article and was not entitled to raise those issues on appeal. The employees' face-to-face identifications of defendant, which were made shortly after the crime and without police prompting, did not give rise to a substantial likelihood of misidentification. The court held that the kidnapping conviction was not double jeopardy because defendant used the residents as a shield to avoid capture, not to facilitate the armed robbery. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in overruling the Batson challenge and imposing the maximum and consecutive sentences because defendant placed the victims in fear of their lives, had prior felony convictions, and was a public risk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence for armed robbery and aggravated kidnapping. The court remanded with instructions to inform defendant of the prescriptive period for applying for post-conviction relief and amend the record to show that the trial court granted credit for time served with regard to the enhanced sentence.

Hebert v. Lafayette City Council


NUMBER 96-1341


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-1341 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/09/97); 692 So. 2d 750; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 917



April 9, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Allen M. Babineaux, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 961506.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a judgment from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which sustained the exception of prescription filed by defendants, presumably Lafayette City Council members in plaintiff's election contest.


OVERVIEW: About three years before plaintiff filed this action, the voters of Lafayette Parish passed a proposition to merge the Parish and City of Lafayette governments. About nine months after the new Parish-City Council regime took office, plaintiff filed this action to contest the election. In affirming the judgment that sustained the exception of prescription, the court dismissed plaintiff's contention that the 30-day prescription contained in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405(D) was not applicable to the action. The court held that an election contest was an election contest, whether the contestant decried the conduct of the election or claimed, as plaintiff did, that the election was a nullity. The court held that the short delay for filing an election contest, aside from being a prerogative of the legislature, was prudent given the importance of governance and the importance of certainty and stability of governments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that sustained the exception of prescription filed by defendants to plaintiff's election contest.

State v. Wade


No. 29,234-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


693 So. 2d 195; 29,234 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/02/97); 693 So. 2d 195; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 888



April 2, 1997, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 29, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 170,374B. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, which was entered upon a jury verdict finding her guilty of purse snatching and the sentence of three years imprisonment at hard labor that was imposed.


OVERVIEW: The victim was placing groceries in her car when defendant and another woman approached her from behind. The victim knew defendant because they were both in a relationship with the same man. Words were exchanged and the three women began fighting. During the melee, defendant took the victim's purse. Defendant was subsequently charged with purse snatching. A jury found defendant guilty and the trial court sentenced her to serve three years imprisonment at hard labor. Her timely motion for reconsideration of sentence was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The record supported defendant's conviction. Defendant denied taking the victim's purse, but eyewitnesses substantially corroborated the victim's testimony concerning the physical attack and theft. The jury heard conflicting testimony and chose to accept the version of events described by the State's witnesses. The jury's credibility determination was rational. The jury could reasonably conclude that defendant committed the offense charged. The sentence imposed was not constitutionally excessive. The sentence was neither grossly out of proportion to the seriousness of the offense nor did it shock the sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for purse snatching and the sentence that was imposed against her.

State v. Morris


NUMBER 96 KA 1008


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 1008 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/27/97); 691 So. 2d 792; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 865



March 27, 1997, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Morris, 703 So. 2d 609, 1997 La. LEXIS 3211 (La., Oct. 13, 1997)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Morris v. State, 731 So. 2d 279, 1998 La. LEXIS 3859 (La., Dec. 18, 1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Morris, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 2970 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 20, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Livingston. State of Louisiana. Suit No. 11230. Honorable Bruce Bennett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED. SENTENCE, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED. REMANDED, WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-First Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Livingston (Louisiana), which found him guilty of aggravated rape, claiming that his conviction and sentence were invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with and found guilty of rape. He appealed his conviction, arguing that his trial was invalid and the sentence was illegal. The court held that the evidence was legally sufficient for a jury to find him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also stated that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in limiting defendant's voir dire, and that defendant's challenge for cause as to jury members was correctly denied, as there was no evidence of bias. The court also determined that the prosecutor's failure to present a probable cause sheet in a timely manner did not cause undue prejudice and thus was not a reversible error. Finally, the court concluded that the trial court did not commit reversible error in admitting the victim's hearsay evidence, because the jury had an independent basis for finding that the rape occurred, and therefore the hearsay evidence was merely repetitive in nature. The court upheld defendant's conviction and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

State v. Bentley


No. 96-KA-795


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


96-795 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/25/97); 692 So. 2d 1207; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 588

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of false swearing, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:126.1. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the bill of information and in denying his motion to suppress his pretrial statement.


OVERVIEW: The case arose out of a murder investigation in which defendant had given a statement. After a retrial, defendant was convicted of false swearing. The court reversed his conviction and remanded the case. First the court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:126.1 was not unconstitutional because of vagueness. The court held that an ordinary person of reasonable intelligence was capable of discerning its meaning and conforming his conduct to it. The court held that the trial court should have suppressed the pretrial statement of defendant because he was not advised as required by Miranda v. Arizona. At the time that defendant made the second statement he had been picked up an officer and driven to the detective bureau. He was placed in an office and later interviewed by an officer. The court held that this was in custody interrogation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the trial court, which had convicted defendant of false swearing. The court held that the trial court should have suppressed defendant's pretrial statement. The case was remanded to the trial court.

State v. Styles


No. 96-KA-897


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


96-897 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/25/97); 692 So. 2d 1222; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 595



March 25, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, NO. 95-2328, DIVISION "N", HONORABLE SUSAN M. CHEHARDY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which found him guilty of one count of aggravated rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42 and two counts of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of one count of aggravated rape and two counts of armed robbery. The trial court's judgment was affirmed on appeal despite numerous assignments of error raised by defendant. Among the court's findings, the court found that defendant had waived his right to assert error in the admission of testimony by a witness, where the witness allegedly testified that defendant had robbed him in the past, because defendant failed to object to the witness's testimony at trial. The court found defendant's contention that the trial court improperly admitted hearsay testimony during the state's case to be without merit. In response to defendant's contention that the trial court erred in failing to charge the law applicable to the case, the court found that, based on the charges as a whole, that the jury was well aware that it should view the accomplice's testimony with great caution. Moreover, defendant's failure to object to a remark made by the trial judge to the jury waived defendant's right to argue that the trial court erred in commenting on the facts of the case. Finally, the court found that the verdict was not contrary to the law and evidence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of one count of aggravated rape and two counts of armed robbery, was affirmed.

 

536 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Verdin v. Louisiana Land & Exploration Co.


No. 96-CA-1815


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-1815 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/12/97); 693 So. 2d 162; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 551



March 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied of May 15, 1997, Reported at: 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1492. Rehearing Opinion of May 15, 1997, Reported at: 693 So. 2d 162 at 172.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 92-7633, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE RICHARD J. GARVEY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, injured husband and wife, sought review of a judgment from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which following a jury trial, dismissed their suit against appellee corporate landowner on a finding that the landowner was immune from liability under the Louisiana recreational use immunity statutes, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:2791, 9:2795.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs suffered serious injuries when their flat bottom skiff hit a concrete survey marker placed by the landowner at the corner of its property. Following a weeklong jury trial, the jury found that the landowner was totally at fault and that the plaintiffs were fishing for recreational purposes at the time of the accident. The trial court entered judgment for the landowner. On review, plaintiffs contended that the trial court erred in granting immunity to the landowner because (1) there was no evidence that the landowner had dedicated the bay for recreational purposes, (2) plaintiffs were not given permission to use the bay, and (3) the instrument was a man-made concrete post. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that it was not necessary for the landowner to have given permission to the plaintiffs for the immunity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2791. The court also held that the fact that the instrument that caused the accident was man-made did not of itself defeat the immunity. Because the record indicated that the bay was not used primarily for commercial recreational purposes, the court noted that § 9:2791 applied, not La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2795.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court that had dismissed plaintiffs' cause of action against the landowner.

Succession of Price


NUMBER 96-1330


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-1330 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/05/97); 692 So. 2d 1152; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 486



March 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Donald T. Johnson, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 29,390.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandchildren sought review of an order from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), granting defendant legatees' petition for possession of the decedent's estate in accordance with the terms of the decedent's will.


OVERVIEW: The grandchildren of a decedent who specifically disinherited them in her will challenged the trial court's order admitting the will to probate and granting possession of the decedent's estate to the legatees. On appeal, the court held that pursuant to a recently approved constitutional amendment, La. Const. art. XII, § 5(A), (B) (1995), the legislature passed La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493(A), (B) (1996) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2501(A), (B) (1996). Under those statutes, the trial court did not commit manifest error by interpreting the decedent's intent as a desire to disinherit her grandchildren, who were forced heirs. The decedent's intent was honored under the dictates of § 9:2501(B)(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting defendant legatees' petition.

Sudwischer v. Estate of Hoffpauir


No. 96-1312


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-1312 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/05/97); 692 So. 2d 590; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 499



March 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Acadia, Honorable Jules Edwards, Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 47,796.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an alleged daughter of the deceased, sought review of a decision of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Acadia, (Louisiana), which ruled that she was not the biological daughter of the deceased.


OVERVIEW: The alleged daughter brought an action for filiation after the death of the deceased. She claimed that the decedent was her biological father as the result of an adulterous affair with her mother. The decedent was survived by his wife. He was also survived by his two legitimate children that resulted from the marriage. To aid in proving the relationship between herself and the decedent, the alleged daughter compelled the decedent's legitimate daughter to submit blood for DNA comparison. The lower court characterized the evidence as ambiguous at best. The lower court ruled that the alleged daughter was not the biological child of the decedent. On appeal the alleged daughter asserted that the lower court erred when it applied the clear and convincing standard of proof to her action. The court affirmed. The court held that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 209(C), which was an amendment to the statute in which the alleged daughter filed her action, applied retroactively and hence the alleged daughter's burden was clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision, which ruled that the alleged daughter was not the biological daughter of the deceased.

 

539 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Conerly v. State


No. 29,236-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,236 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/03/97); 690 So. 2d 980; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 522



March 3, 1997, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 86-191. Honorable John R. Harrison, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED at defendants/appellants' cost.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a state government, a hospital, and two physicians, appealed the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana), which held that they were liable in malpractice to plaintiffs, parents of a newborn who died of asphyxia.


OVERVIEW: An infant died of asphyxia, after being delivered by two physicians. The parents of the infant sued the physicians, and brought a wrongful death lawsuit and a newborn's survival claim against the physicians, the hospital, and the state government. The trial court awarded the parents damages up to the amount of the statutory cap set by law, and both parties appealed the ruling. The court held that the evidence was sufficient for the jury to reasonably believe that the physicians committed malpractice by failing to diagnose the infant's distress during childbirth. The court also determined that the jury's findings that mother did not contribute to her child's death was not manifestly erroneous. In addition, the court stated that the hospital was correctly found liable under the doctrine of vicarious liability for the actions of its physicians. Finally, the court concluded that state law, which limited the amount of recovery, was constitutional, and the parents' wrongful death claim was separate and distinct from their newborn's survival claim. The court upheld the trial court's ruling and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court for the parents.

Wilson v. Louisiana Safety Ass'n


No. 29,263-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,263 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/28/97); 690 So. 2d 974; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 423



February 28, 1997, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana Trial Court. No. 55877. Honorable Elizabeth A. Pickett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an employee, sought review of a decision of the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of Desoto (Louisiana), which sustained the declaratory exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction of defendants, State and safety organizations, in a declaratory action.


OVERVIEW: The employee was employed on a unit basis as a pulpwood cutter and he was injured on the job. The safety organization paid the employee worker's compensation benefits according to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(10)(d). The employee alleged that under the formula of § 23:1021(10)(d) he was credited with only four days per week of earnings in the calculation of the average weekly wage, which he claimed reduced the wages of a unit worker who worked five days per week by 20 percent and the wages of a unit worker who worked six day per week by 33 and 1/3 percent. The employee brought an action for a declaratory judgment in the district court which sought to have § 23:1021 (10)(d) declared unconstitutional. The state brought a declinatory exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction on the ground that the Office of Worker's Compensation (OWC), was vested with exclusive jurisdiction to here the employee's action. The lower court sustained the declinatory exception. On appeal the court reversed. The court held that because the employee's action was not a claim or dispute for application of the worker's compensation act that it was outside the jurisdiction of the OWC.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision, which sustained the state's and the safety organizations' declaratory exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction in a declaratory action.

 

541 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Giovengo


No. CR96-1227


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-1227 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/26/97); 692 So. 2d 462; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 333



February 26, 1997, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Thirty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson Davis, State of Louisiana; the Honorable William N. Knight, District Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: CR-1604-96.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Thirty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson Davis (Louisiana), which denied defendant's motion to quash the bill of information filed against him on the basis that the statute under which he was charged, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:81(A), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulled over while driving for following another vehicle too closely in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:81(A). He was then arrested for possession of marijuana. Defendant pled guilty to possession of marijuana with intent to distribute and received a six-year sentence. Defendant then filed a motion to quash the bill of information because of the unconstitutionally vague language of the statute. The trial court denied that motion, and defendant appealed. The court held that words used in statutes did not have to have the same mathematical symbols. Due process required only that the language of the statute have generally accepted meaning so that a person of ordinary and reasonable intelligence was capable of discerning it proscriptions and was given fair notice of the conduct which was forbidden by its terms. Here, the statute at issue, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:81(A), provided that the driver of a motor vehicle could not follow another vehicle more closely than was reasonable and prudent, having due regard for the speed of such vehicle and the traffic upon the condition of the highway. As such, § 32:81 was constitutional, and the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed and the case was remanded so that the judgment could be amended to reflect that defendant was given credit for time served.

Lightell v. City of New Orleans


No. 96-CA-2013


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-2013 (La. App. 4 Cir. 02/19/97); 689 So. 2d 732; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 418



February 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION NO. 93-01763, DISTRICT 8. HONORABLE MARK ZIMMERMAN, HEARING OFFICER.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city appealed a judgment from the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 8 (Louisiana), that found that appellee worker at that time had a temporary total disability (TTD) because of a work-related accident and that awarded him attorney fees after finding that the city had arbitrarily and capriciously failed to promptly notify the office that it modified the worker's benefits from TTD benefits to supplemental-earnings benefits.


OVERVIEW: A hearing officer determined that the worker was entitled to temporary-total-disability (TTD) benefits, and the city appealed. On appeal, the court determined that the worker had not met the threshold burden of proving an entitlement to TTD benefits. According to the court, the only basis for finding that the worker continued to be temporarily and totally disabled was the worker's own testimony, and this testimony did not establish by clear and convincing evidence that the worker remained temporarily and totally disabled four years after the accident. The court accepted the city's argument that the hearing officer erred in awarding attorney fees to the worker for failure of the city to promptly notify the worker and the office of the change in the status of benefits per La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201(G) [changed to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201(H)]. Among the reasons the court gave were that § 23:1201(H) contained no penalty provision, and it did not pertain to a situation in which the amount of the worker's payments had not been altered.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the city and against the worker, the court reversed the office's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings. Costs of the appeal were assigned to the worker.

Holladay v. Louisiana State Bd. of Medical Examiners


No. 96-CA-1740


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-1740 (La. App. 4 Cir. 02/19/97); 689 So. 2d 718; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 324



February 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 95-17647, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE ROBERT A. KATZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Louisiana State Board of Medical Examiners, and defendant doctor appealed from a judgment of the Civil District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which affirmed in part, reversed in part and modified in part, the board's decision imposing disciplinary sanctions on the doctor.


OVERVIEW: The board found violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 37:1285 by the doctor, including: (1) the doctor's failure to advise the board on his Louisiana renewal application of an investigation undertaken by the Texas Board of Medical Examiners, (2) prescription of controlled substances in excess of any legitimate medically justifiable manner, and (3) failure to satisfy prevailing and generally accepted standards of medical practice. The board imposed a fine, suspended the doctor for three months, and ordered attendance at a pain management course. The trial court affirmed as to the first violation, reversed as to the second two, and modified the sanction to eliminate the suspension and the course. On appeal, the court reinstated the board's decision. The court noted the investigation and the lack of notice were undisputed, and supported affirmance as to the first violation, but that the trial court's reversals were manifestly erroneous. The court noted evidence that the doctor had prescribed controlled substances to patients without a treatment plan, and in some cases, for up to eight months with a medical exam. The court found the sanction within the board's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court partially reversed the district court judgment which affirmed in part, reversed in part, and modified the board's decision imposing disciplinary sanctions on the doctor, and reinstated the board's decision in its entirety.

Blackwell v. Louisiana Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corrections


No. 96 CA 0954 CONSOLIDATED WITH 96 CA 0955


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0954 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/97); 690 So. 2d 137; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 390



February 14, 1997, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 2, 1997. Released for Publication April 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 403,813 and No. 406,464. Honorable Joseph Keogh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, which dismissed his tort action against defendants, the Louisiana Department of Public Safety and Corrections and its Secretary and the warden of the Louisiana State Penitentiary, Angola.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed his tort suit after he was injured while operating an incinerator at the prison. Specifically, he averred that while he was raking ash inside the incinerator, an explosion occurred, causing a burning object to propel through the door. The burning object struck him resulting in burns. Even though he chose to invoke the administrative remedies available to him, he urged that the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure Act as it applied to inmate tort claims was unconstitutional, and therefore, he was entitled to bring his tort action directly in state court. He contended that because the Act was not constitutionally applied to his tort claim, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1177's 30 day time limitation had not applied to his action. The trial court dismissed his action and he sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment on the grounds that the Act was constitutional. The court held that the Act's peremptive time period for seeking judicial review of an adverse administrative decision could have been applied to an inmate's tort claim filed in state district court. The court found that all statutory enactments were presumed to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the inmate's action.

Liberty Mut. Ins. Co. v. Louisiana Ins. Rating Comm'n


96 CA 0793


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0793 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/97); 696 So. 2d 1021; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 392



February 14, 1997, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Applications for Rehearing Denied July 2, 1997, Reported at: 1997 La. App. LEXIS 1772.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NUMBER 418,660, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE FRANK J. SAIA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court REVERSED in its entirety. Matter REMANDED to trial court which is ordered to direct Liberty Mutual to apply to LIRC for reconsideration of validity of Bulletin LIRC 95-03 in light of views expressed herein. Total costs of appeal in amount of $ 886.06 assessed equally between Liberty Mutual and LIRC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Louisiana Insurance Rating Commission, Louisiana Commissioner of Insurance, and rating commissioners (LIRC), sought review of a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), in favor of appellee insurer, which declared invalid an LIRC rule prohibiting the issuance of "wrap-up insurance, " and enjoined enforcement against the insurer.


OVERVIEW: LIRC issued a bulletin to insurers requiring submission of any "wrap-up" insurance rules and rates to the LIRC for approval and commenced administrative proceedings against the insurer for failure to comply. The insurer commenced an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1871 et seq. The trial court declared the bulletin to be a "rule" subject to the Louisiana Administrative Procedure Act (LAPA), declared it invalid for noncompliance with LAPA rule-making requirements, and enjoined enforcement. On appeal, the court reversed. The court upheld the trial court's finding that the bulletin was a "rule," subject to LAPA. However, the court held that absent specific statutory provisions for review of LIRC rules, the requirements of the LAPA set forth in La. Stat. Ann. § 49:963(D), not the general Louisiana Code of Civil Procedure, applied to applications for declaratory relief. The court found that the insurer had not met the prerequisites under § 49:963(D), thus the trial court lacked authority to render declaratory, and in turn, injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment in favor of the insurer, which declared invalid an LIRC rule, and enjoined enforcement against the insurer. The court remanded to the trial court with the order to direct the insurer to apply to LIRC for reconsideration of validity of the rule in light of the court's opinion.

Allied Signal v. Jackson


96 CA 0138


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0138 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/97); 691 So. 2d 150; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 415



February 14, 1997, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd Judicial District Court Parish of Ascension, Louisiana. Docket No. 55,335, Division "C". Honorable Guy Holdridge, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and state officials, appealed a judgment from the 23rd Judicial District Court, Parish of Ascension, Louisiana, which declared that certain industrial areas in which plaintiffs, property owners, owned property could not be included in a proposed municipality, which defendants were attempting to have incorporated. The judgment also granted a permanent injunction of any further action to incorporate the proposed areas.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 51:1202 and 1203 were in abrogation of a municipality's power to levy an ad valorem tax. Recognizing that tax revenues enabled municipalities to provide services such as clean water and sewerage disposal, defendants contended that the proposed municipality could not exist without a sufficient tax base. In other words, it would be unable to provide such services to the people who lived within the municipality if the industrial areas were not included in its tax base. By not including these industrial areas in the proposed municipality, §§ 51:1202 and 1203 removed them from the proposed municipality's tax base. Therefore, defendants contended the legislature created an exemption from ad valorem taxation in derogation of La. Const. art. VI, § 27. Because they did not prove either that the legislature's enactment of §§ 51:1202 and 1203 was in contravention of a specific constitutional provision, or that there was a constitutional intention to limit the power of the legislature in the manner claimed, the court concluded that the trial court did not err in granting the injunction and denying the defendants' exception of no cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court denying defendants' exceptions raising the objections of prematurity, jurisdiction and no cause/no right of action, and affirmed the judgment granting declaratory and injunctive relief.

 

547 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Deumite v. State


No. 94 CA 1210R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94-1210 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/97); 692 So. 2d 1127; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 416



February 14, 1997, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Dissenting Opinion Dated April 23, 1997. Rehearing Denied April 24, 1997. Released for Publication April 24, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Pointe Coupee, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 23,268. Honorable Jack T. Marionneaux, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action against the state arising from a diving accident at a public lake, the Louisiana Supreme Court vacated the trial court's judgment for plaintiffs, an injured boy and his parents, and remanded to the court because the trial court erred in rejecting the state's immunity argument by declaring the Recreational Use Statute (RUS), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2795, unconstitutional, as that was unnecessary to decide the case.


OVERVIEW: The boy broke his neck when he dove into a shallow part of a recreational lake. The state admitted that it had knowledge of the depth at the site for years. The court reviewed the evidence de novo to determine whether the state was immune from liability under § 9:2795 and reversed the trial court, finding that it had made an error of law in its interpretation of the statute. Using a three-prong test, the court determined that the statutory immunity in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2795(E) applied in the instant case. Addressing the second prong first, the court found § 9:2795(E) relieved the state of proving the injury was the result of recreation that could be pursued in the true outdoors. Besides, there was no serious dispute about the issue of recreational use. The third prong was satisfied because the bottom of the lake was an instrumentality normally found in the "true outdoors." The first prong was satisfied because the development of the lake for recreation did not change the character of the area from semi-rural. Accordingly, the state and its agencies were entitled to the immunity granted in § 9:2795 and owed no duty to the boy to warn him of the shallow bottom.


OUTCOME: Having concluded that the state was not responsible for the boy's injuries, the court reversed the trial court judgment in his favor.

 

548 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Boswell


NUMBER 96-801


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-801 (La. App. 3 Cir. 02/12/97); 689 So. 2d 627; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 161



February 12, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana, the Honorable George Metoyer, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Judge Number: 240,546.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, Louisiana, which convicted him of two counts of distribution of cocaine. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to allow him to question a state witness regarding her prior arrests and any influence which her pending charges might have had on her testimony; as well as any arrangements she had with law enforcement officials.


OVERVIEW: The witness was a confidential informant who identified defendant as the individual who had distributed cocaine to her. She had entered into an agreement with the State wherein the charges pending against her would be dropped in exchange for providing information and working narcotics cases. Under cross-examination, when defendant attempted to impeach the informant with questions as to whether she had recently been arrested on drug charges, the State objected. The court found that the trial court erred in refusing to allow defendant to question the informant about her pending charge, but that such error was harmless. The court concluded that, although the informant's testimony was important to the State's case, it was cumulative and was corroborated on many material points by the testimony of the arresting officer. The informant was cross-examined extensively regarding her incentive for entering into an agreement with the police and about her prior conviction for distribution of cocaine. Finally, even without the informant's testimony, the arresting officer's testimony was sufficient to convict defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for distribution of cocaine. However, the court remanded the case to the trial court to amend the commitment and minute entry of defendant's sentence to reflect that he was given credit for time served.

Smith v. Brooks


NUMBER 96-1085


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-1085 (La. App. 3 Cir. 02/05/97); 689 So. 2d 544; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 115

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagees sought review of the judgment of the Thirty-Fifth Judicial District Court, Parish of Grant, State of Louisiana, in favor of defendant tax sale purchasers, in the mortgagees' suit to annul the tax sales of two tracts of real property.


OVERVIEW: After two tracts of real property were sold at tax sale, the mortgagees sought to annul the sales on the grounds that they had never been notified of the impending sales and that their constitutional due process right against deprivation of property without prior notice had thus been violated. The trial court denied the mortgagees' motion for summary judgment, and then entered judgment dismissing their action. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a trial on the merits, holding that the trial court was not authorized to render a judgment on the merits in favor of the purchasers upon denial of the mortgagees' motion for summary judgment.

Graham v. St. Landry Parish Sch. Bd.


NUMBER 96-904


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-904 (La. App. 3 Cir. 02/05/97); 689 So. 2d 595; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 133



February 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Robert Brinkman, presiding. Lower Court No. 94-C-2864-B.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher sought review of the judgment of the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana, dismissing his claim against defendant, a parish school board, for wrongful termination in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: After taking disability retirement, a certified teacher's application for rehire was rejected by the parish school board. He was employed by another school system and sued, alleging violations of La. Const. arts. 2, 3, and 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1981, 1983, in the board's employing of non-certified teachers in positions for which he was qualified. The trial court dismissed his suit. He appealed, and the court reversed the judgment. It held that because the parish school board retained, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:81, the authority to hire teachers, the decision not to hire the teacher was an action that could be considered a policy under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; the court also held that the board's refusal to rehire the teacher was arbitrary and without a rational basis. The court did not award damages. It reasoned that the teacher sustained no economic loss because he was making more money in his current position than he would have had he been re-hired; that he failed to claim punitive damages or to prove psychological pain; and that he was not entitled to attorney's fees, where he had failed to recover any other damages and where he had refused the remedy of reinstatement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the board but declined to award damages to the teacher.

 

552 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Manville v. Citizen


NUMBER 96-861


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-861 (La. App. 3 Cir. 02/05/97); 689 So. 2d 578; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 136



February 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Twenty-seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Alonzo Harris, presiding. Lower Court No. 94-C-2653-C.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the driver of a tractor-trailer, his employer, and their insurer, appealed from a judgment of the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), which overturned a jury verdict and found the driver was 100 percent at fault in an accident that injured plaintiffs, the driver of a pickup truck and her passengers. The trial court also increased the amount of damages that the jury awarded.


OVERVIEW: The jury found that the driver of the pickup truck was 20 percent at fault in an accident and awarded damages to her and her passengers. Following the jury verdict, the injured persons filed a successful motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict to increase the amount of damages and to find that the driver of the tractor-trailer was 100 percent at fault. The trial court sustained the motion. On review, the court determined that the facts and inferences pointed so strongly in favor of the trial court removing fault from the driver of the pickup truck, that reasonable men could not arrive at a contrary verdict. No evidence was presented to indicate that the driver of the pickup truck could have maneuvered her vehicle to avoid the accident, nor was there evidence indicating that she was traveling in excess of the posted speed limit. As for the judge's decision to increase the amount of the jury awards, the court held that the jury's verdicts were clearly wrong and contrary to the evidence. The jury failed to award damages for proven injuries. The amounts determined by the trial court were justifiable and within the range established by trial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which granted the motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict that the driver of the pickup truck and her passengers filed to change the jury's finding of fault and award of damages in the action they brought following an accident against the driver of a tractor-trailer, his employer, and their insurer.

State v. Boykin


No. 29,141-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,141 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/31/97); 688 So. 2d 1250; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 158



January 31, 1997, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 20, 1997. Released for Publication February 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 172096. Honorable Eugene W. Bryson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; HABITUAL OFFENDER ADJUDICATION AND SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction, by the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, for distribution of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40.967, as well as of his adjudication as a second felony offender and his sentence to 20 years imprisonment at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of cocaine distribution and was adjudicated a habitual offender. On appeal, the court affirmed his conviction, holding that the uncontradicted testimony of a police officer who purchased drugs from defendant was sufficient to support the conviction, and that the testimony of police officers and crime lab technicians established a chain of custody by a preponderance of the evidence. The court further held that there was neither error nor prejudice in the trial court's sustaining of the prosecutor's objection during defendant's closing argument on the issue of probable cause to make the arrest, and that the trial court's refusal to allow certain police reports into evidence as inadmissible hearsay was correct. The court held that defendant's adjudication as a habitual offender was not based on an unconstitutional application of an ex post facto cleansing period, but vacated the adjudication for an error patent, in that the state failed to introduce evidence to establish the date of defendant's discharge from prison for his prior felony conviction in order to prove that the "cleansing period" under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(c) had not expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on the cocaine charge, but vacated his habitual offender adjudication and sentence, and remanded the case.

 

554 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Reimer v. Medical Ctr.


No. 95-C-2799


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-2799 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/29/97); 688 So. 2d 165; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 102



January 29, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 95-8823, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GERALD P. FEDOROFF, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court, the court re-addressed its finding that the district court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over plaintiff state employee's lawsuit brought against defendant employer, which alleged retaliatory discharge in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1361 and discrimination based on his handicap or disability in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 46:2254 and 51:2242.


OVERVIEW: The employee was allegedly terminated from his probationary employment for failing to meet attendance standards. Instead of appealing to the Civil Service Commission (CSC), the employee brought an action alleging retaliatory discharge and discrimination. The court found that the district court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the claims. The employee's contention that application of the CSC's rules, enacted pursuant to La. Const. art. X, § 10. broadened definition of discrimination and expanded its jurisdiction beyond its constitutional bounds was without merit. The authority to review the basis for a termination of a civil servant's employment was expressly and unambiguously assigned to the CSC, subject to the right of judicial review, pursuant to La. Const. art. X, § 12(A). The court refused to find that there was concurrent jurisdiction over the employee's claims because that would result in unequal treatment of aggrieved civil service employees. Although the employee sought a money judgment rather than reinstatement, the district court still did not have jurisdiction. The application of the CSC rules was not in conflict with La. Const. art. X, § 8(B).


OUTCOME: The court found that the district court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the employee's claim and dismissed the action without prejudice.

 

555 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gant


No. 29,169-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,169 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/22/97); 687 So. 2d 660; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 58



January 22, 1997, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 11th Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 91903. Honorable Robert E. Burgess, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the 11th Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto (Louisiana), which had convicted her of forgery upon her plea of guilty, and sentenced her to the maximum 10 years at hard labor. Defendant argued that sentence was unconstitutionally excessive her sentence to the maximum 10 years at hard labor is constitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant plead guilty to one count of forgery and the trial court convicted defendant thereof. Defendant complained on appeal that her sentence to the maximum 10 years at hard labor was unconstitutionally excessive. On review, the court affirmed under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1. The court found that defendant's criminal conduct was not adequately defined by one count of forgery because her propensity to commit thefts and forgeries was evident in her brief, but prolific, criminal history for the two years surrounding her seventeenth birthday. The court found that while other trial courts might have sentenced a young and single pregnant substance abuser to a lesser term of years, the 10-year sentence, even though the maximum for one count of forgery, was not an abuse of the trial court's discretion in this case nor was it shocking to the court's sense of justice. The court could not say that defendant's criminal conduct was not serious or that the punishment imposed on defendant would not achieve the legitimately recognized purpose of generally deterring other young members of society who might be inclined to commit similar thefts and forgeries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and held against defendant.

State v. Bates


No. 29,252-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


29,252 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/22/97); 711 So. 2d 281; 1997 La. App. LEXIS 49



January 22, 1997, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 94-F1119. Honorable D. Milton Moore, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) of one count of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967, and one count of conspiracy to distribute cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:979, 40:967. Defendant also sought review of his concurrent sentences at hard labor, his probationary sentence, and his fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, conspiracy to distribute cocaine, and his sentences and fines related to his convictions. Defendant entered a plea agreement with the state that provided that he cooperate with both the state and federal governments in their efforts to indict and convict other drug dealers. The court affirmed and noted defendant's assertion that the trial court erred when it denied his motion to withdraw his guilty plea, and that his sentence was excessive. The court found that defendant's alleged violation of the plea agreement was based on the U.S. Attorney's failure to provide the trial court with a letter that attested to defendant's cooperation. Defendant also alleged that he pled to the charges in the indictment for purposes of cooperation but had no intention of being sentenced on those charges. The court held that defendant understood the terms and conditions of the plea agreement, and the U.S. Attorney's failure to provide the requisite letter because of the lack of defendant's total cooperation was not considered by the trial court. The court held that defendant received the benefit of his agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant of the charges of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, conspiracy to distribute cocaine, and the related sentences imposed for his convictions.

Hollingsworth v. Bowers


NUMBER 96-257


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-257 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/30/96); 690 So. 2d 825; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3201



December 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Ninth Judicial District, Parish of Rapides, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Donald T. Johnson, District Judge, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 171,198.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a physician and his insurer, appealed an order of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, a mother, individually, and on behalf of her son, and awarded general damages to the mother and son and future medical benefits to the son. The order imposed a statutory cap to each plaintiff under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40.1299.42(B).


OVERVIEW: The mother, a gestational diabetic, was a patient of the physician and was diagnosed with preeclampsia. When she was delivering her son, a complication known as shoulder dyscotia arose and the physician directed the nurses to perform a maneuver on the mother in order to push the baby through the birth canal. The son sustained permanent injury to his shoulder nerves and lost use his left arm and hand. The trial court awarded general damages to the son, damages for loss of future earnings, and future medical benefits, and damages to the mother for loss of consortium. The trial court imposed statutory caps on each plaintiff under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B)(1). The court affirmed because the finding that inappropriate fundal pressure was applied was not manifestly erroneous given the high likelihood of dystocia. The court affirmed the award for general damages and for future medical expenses to the son, but reversed the award of damages to the mother for loss of consortium. The mother's loss of consortium claim was a derivative claim of the son's injuries and therefore exceeded the statutory cap allowed for the child. The assessment of costs on defendants was not abusive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which found that the physician and his insurer were liable to plaintiffs in their medical malpractice action. The court affirmed the award of damages, but reversed the award to the mother for loss of consortium.
