Thompson v. La.


94 CA 2610 CONSOLIDATED WITH 94 CA 2611


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 2610 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/30/96); 688 So. 2d 9; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3266



December 30, 1996, RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 688 So. 2d 9 at 23.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of April 23, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. App. LEXIS 828.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorists alleged to have been injured by reason of acts or omissions on the part of appellees, the State of Louisiana as well as various political subdivisions and agencies thereof, in connection with the collision of a car with a tree branch that was overhanging a public road. After the trial court (Louisiana) held for the motorists and the state's initial appeal resulted in a reversal of the judgment, the motorists sought rehearing.


OVERVIEW: The motorists asserted that the state or various state instrumentalities were liable for injuries that resulted from a collision between their car and a low-hanging tree branch. After the motorists prevailed in the trial court, the state successfully appealed and obtained a reversal of the judgment. The motorists sought rehearing but the court reaffirmed. It rejected a claim that it erred by reviewing the lower court's findings de novo because it found legal errors that triggered de novo review. It confirmed its prior holding that a construction contract should not have been admitted into evidence because it related to a different part of the highway; rejected a claim that the state had general power to trim tree branches because that power only existed in the event of immediate danger; held that the state had no general duty to remove overhead objects that presented no danger to motorists; affirmed a ruling that evidence concerning other types of accidents on the same road was irrelevant; and held that La. Rev. Stat. § 48:220.1 did not apply, both because it was not retroactive and because the use by the state of the highway constituted an implied dedication.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motorists' request for rehearing but reaffirmed its prior ruling reversing the trial court's judgment in favor of the state and various state instrumentalities.

 

559 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Varnado v. Department of Empl. & Training, Office of Workers' Compensation


No. 95 CA 0787


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0787 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/30/96); 687 So. 2d 1013; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3267



December 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 687 So. 2d 1013 at 1038.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of June 28, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1405.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals filed an application for a partial rehearing and a clarification of the court's reversal of the judgment of the trial court (Louisiana), which held that defendants, a state worker's compensation office and its director, were liable for damages for the director's unconstitutional searches of their offices.


OVERVIEW: The individuals alleged that the director searched their offices in violation of their right to privacy under U.S. Const. amend. IV and La. Const. art. I, § 5. The trial court awarded damages to the individuals, finding that the searches were unconstitutional and in retaliation for the employee's action. The trial court failed to specify which constitutional provisions were violated. The court reversed, holding that the office was also liable under state law and granted the individuals' application for a rehearing and clarification. Defendants were liable for damages because the searches violated federal provisions and La. Const. art. I, § 5. The director was a state employee within the meaning of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:1441.1 and the office was vicariously liable under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2320. The director was not entitled to qualified immunity for violations of state constitutional rights because he did not show that he had no knowledge of the legal standard for unreasonable searches. Defendants were not entitled to immunity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 9:2798.1 because the director's acts were willful. The court reversed with respect to the grant of attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the order of the trial court, which awarded damages to the individuals and against defendants. The court reversed the portion of the order that awarded attorney's fees to the individuals.

State v. Woodberry


No. 95-KA-2402


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-2402 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/27/96); 686 So. 2d 984; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3146



December 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 14, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 371-742, SECTION "H". HONORABLE JAMES F. MCKAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Criminal District Court Orleans Parish Section H, where defendant had been sentenced to eight years at hard labor on a conviction for sexual battery, five years at hard labor on his conviction for crime against nature, 35 years at hard labor for second degree kidnapping, five years at hard labor on the conviction for simple robbery, and 10 years at hard labor for first degree robbery.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had convicted defendant on charges of sexual battery, crime against nature, second degree kidnapping, simple robbery, and first degree robbery. On review, the court affirmed. The court held that a witness was an unavailable witness under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 804(A)(5) and testimony from a suppression hearing was properly admitted where the witness was absent from the proceedings despite the state's good faith diligent effort to locate him, where the witness's prior testimony bore the requisite "indicia of reliability", and where defendant was represented by counsel at a suppression hearing and was cross-examined. The court held that it was not error for the state to have delayed in producing a witness's criminal record under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 609.1 where defendant could not have introduced evidence of, or questioned the witness about, a forcible rape charge against him. The court held that defendant's sentences were not excessive under La. Const. art. 1, § 20, and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 881.4(D), 894.1 where defendant's sentences were within the statutory ranges for all the convictions and are fully supported by the circumstances of the case.


OUTCOME: The court held against defendant, and affirmed the trial court's judgments of convictions and sentences.

Lewis v. State


No. 96 CA 1586


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 1586 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/20/96); 685 So. 2d 640; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3042



December 20, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 424,824. Honorable Bob Downing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Louisiana, challenged a judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana rendered in favor of appellee, a parent of a personal injury victim in a declaratory judgment action. The trial court's judgment permitted the parent to recover the entire damage award granted her in a prior personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The parent of the personal injury victim obtained a $ 3,16,604 verdict plus interest against the state. The state took the position that the award was capped at $ 500,000 and the prejudgment interest capped at six percent, pursuant to a constitutional amendment, and agreed to pay the parent the difference between the cap amount and the verdict. The parent accepted the settlement reserving his right to challenge the applicability of the cap. The parent brought a declaratory judgment action and the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the victim. On appeal, the court held that the constitutional caps on general damages and interest would not to be applied retroactively to this case, which was pending prior to the enactment of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the parent of the personal injury victim was entitled to the entire verdict award plus interest.

Banker's Ins. Co. v. Kemp


NUMBER 96 CA 0469


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0469 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/20/96); 686 So. 2d 111; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3134



December 20, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 95-02868. Honorable Robert H. Morrison, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant district attorney challenged an order of the 21st Judicial District Court for the Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), which granted a preliminary injunction in favor of appellee bail bond insurer and enjoined the district attorney from collecting bond forfeiture judgments against the insurer by the use of executory process, other than that provided for in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:85.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered four judgments of commercial bond forfeitures because certain principals failed to appear. Six months after the mailing of the notice of the signing of the judgments, writs of fieri facias were directed by the district attorney to the sheriff ordering the sheriff to seize the bonds of the bail bond insurer on deposit with the state in order to satisfy the judgments of the bond forfeitures. The insurer sought injunctive relief, which the trial court granted, enjoining the district attorney from collecting the bond forfeiture judgments in any other way other than through the requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:85, 22:658.1. The district attorney appealed and contended that although the statute required a filing to show cause with the Commissioner of Insurance, it did not restrict alternative methods of collection. The court affirmed and held that the statutes were clear in restricting the method of collection to the provisions of the statutes. The court held that the district attorney was not enjoined from collection if he proceeded pursuant to the statutes by filing a rule to show cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court which granted a preliminary injunction in favor of the bail bond insurer which enjoined the district attorney from collecting bond forfeiture judgments against the insurer by the use of executory process.

Rhodes v. State ex rel. DOT & Dev.


No. 94 CA 1758R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


94 1758 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/20/96); 684 So. 2d 1134; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3198



December 20, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court, the court was directed to consider whether plaintiff motorists proved negligence by the Department of Transportation and Development under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315 and, if so, what damages were due the motorists for their injuries sustained in their collision at a state highway intersection controlled by a malfunctioning traffic signal.


OVERVIEW: The motorists' vehicles collided at a state highway intersection controlled by a traffic signal that showed green to both cross roads. The trial court initially found negligence sufficient for the Department's strict liability but that the motorists had not met the burden of proof of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800 to show notice and an opportunity to repair. On appeal, the court ruled that § 9:2800 was unconstitutional, but the higher court remanded, holding that where negligence had been found by the trial court, it was unnecessary to address § 9:2800. In reversing the trial court on remand, the court ruled that it was required to sustain the trial court's finding of negligence in the absence of manifest error. The court applied the standard duty/risk negligence analysis in determining whether liability could be imposed under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315. The court found that the evidence established that the Department had a duty under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48:193 to maintain its traffic signals, that the Department breached that duty, that the breach was the cause-in-fact of the injuries, and the harm was within the scope of protection of the duty that was breached.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the Department and rendered judgment awarding damages to the motorists.

State v. Handley


No. 96 KA 0631


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0631 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/20/96); 686 So. 2d 149; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3200



December 20, 1996, DECISION RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 9, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. TRIAL COURT NO. 7-93-30. HONORABLE BONNIE P. JACKSON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which convicted him of aggravated rape, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42, armed robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, second degree kidnapping, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with raping a woman whom he was asked to assist after her car ran out of gas. On appeal of his conviction and sentence for the rape and associated offenses, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient, that the prosecutor referred to his failure to testify, that he was entitled to a new trial, and that his sentence was excessive. In affirming, the court analyzed the evidence in detail and found that, after viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, any rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of each of defendant's crimes beyond a reasonable doubt. The court ruled that the prosecutor's comments regarding the lack of rebuttal to the victim's testimony did not constitute indirect references to defendant's failure to take the stand because other witnesses were available for any possible rebuttal. The court found that the evidence failed to establish that a rape report, which referenced a previous rape by defendant, was examined by the jury before it was retrieved from the jury room and ruled that a new trial was not warranted. The court ruled that the sentences imposed were not constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentencing of the defendant.

 

565 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Whitt


No. 28,834-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,834 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/11/96); 684 So. 2d 1075; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2981



December 11, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 177077. Honorable Michael R. Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, which sentenced defendant to two concurrent sentences of 10 years imprisonment at hard labor after he pleaded guilty to two counts of aggravated incest in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78.1. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the bill of information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's victims were his 4-year-old daughter and his 16-year-old adopted sister. Defendant claimed that § 14:78.1 was unconstitutionally vague because it did not include the element of consanguinity contained in the incest statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:78. The court found that the aggravated incest statute was not an enhanced penalty for incest prohibited under § 14:78. Consanguinity was irrelevant to § 14:78.1. The two statutes were wholly self-contained, and they punished acts plainly defined against persons clearly enumerated in a manner that notified the public of what conduct was prohibited. Defendant's contention that § 14:78.1 was unconstitutionally vague and overly-broad because it failed to consider the offender's age and its relation to the victim's age was without merit because defendant failed to show how these factors were relevant to the prohibition of the conduct. The victim's age and the family relationship were the focus of § 14:78.1. Finally, § 14:78.1 was not shown to be overbroad because defendant did not assert a constitutionally protected right as a defense to the prosecution and because § 14:78.1 affected harmful, criminal conduct rather than speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying defendant's motion to quash. Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State v. Stepp


No. 28,868-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,868 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/11/96); 686 So. 2d 76; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3039



December 11, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 16, 1997. Released for Publication January 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 94-F0286. Honorable Robert W. Kostelka, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of his conviction and sentence of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) wherein a unanimous jury found defendant guilty as charged. He had been charged by bill of information with armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. He was sentenced as a habitual offender to 99 years at hard labor, without the benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove the getaway car for his girlfriend, who entered a convenience store with a gun and demanded the money from the cashier. After being pursued by police, defendant pulled over and surrendered. A holster was found on the car seat and a gun was recovered from the roadside. The state's evidence of defendant's prior armed robbery of another convenience store in Louisiana was admitted at trial. He urged that such evidence was admitted in error as it was not a "signature" type crime. In affirming defendant's conviction and sentence, the court concluded, inter alia, that the evidence of the prior armed robbery was properly admitted under La. Code Evid. 404B(1), as defendant's intent was at issue, the evidence of the prior crime was relevant to show intent, and the evidence of his identity in the prior crime was clear and convincing. Further, the prior armed robbery was sufficiently similar to the instant one. The two convenience store robberies were perpetrated within weeks of each other in locations adjacent to the same highway and were committed with a similar handgun. Thus, the probative value of the prior crime evidence outweighed the prejudice to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of defendant's conviction and sentence of armed robbery.

State v. Schexnayder


No. 96-KA-98


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


96-98 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/26/96); 685 So. 2d 357; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3020



November 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 17, 1997.
Writ denied by State v. Schexnayder, 693 So. 2d 796, 1997 La. LEXIS 1596 (La., May 16, 1997)
Writ of certiorari denied Schexnayder v. Louisiana, 522 U.S. 839, 118 S. Ct. 115, 139 L. Ed. 2d 67, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5023 (1997)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Schexnayder v. State, 706 So. 2d 973, 1998 La. LEXIS 71 (La., Jan. 16, 1998)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Schexnayder v. State, 869 So. 2d 843, 2004 La. LEXIS 879 (La., Mar. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 94-6099, DIVISION "N". THE HONORABLE SUSAN M. CHEHARDY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him for second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:30.1.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's first trial resulted in a mistrial, he was subsequently convicted in another trial for second-degree murder. The court affirmed his conviction. Defendant was not deprived of a fair trial and an impartial jury with respect to the trial court's failure to allow defendant to exercise a peremptory challenge during the selection of the jury with respect to a particular African American juror because the trial court established a prima facie case of purposeful discrimination. The trial court noted defendant's pattern of elimination of black jurors, excluding all but one from the panel. In addition, the trial court considered the relevant fact that the victim was black and defendant was white. Further, defendant's explanation for his peremptory challenge was not particularly persuasive, as there was nothing on the record to support the argument that the potential juror was objectionable. The state's destruction of certain evidence, defendant's car, did not deprive him of access to exculpatory evidence because defendant did not demonstrate that the state acted in bad faith in destroying the car and comparable evidence was reasonably available.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's second-degree murder conviction.

State v. Addison


No. 94-KA-1423


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


94-1423 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/13/96); 684 So. 2d 477; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2700



November 13, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 3, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT FOR ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 357-986, SECTION "I". HONORABLE JOSEPH MEYER, JR., JUDGE AD HOC. HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; MULTIPLE OFFENDER ADJUDICATIONS VACATED; MOTION TO WITHDRAW DENIED; MATTER REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brothers appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court for Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which, following a bench trial, convicted the first brother of attempted possession with intent to distribute cocaine and the second brother of possession with intent to distribute cocaine. The court also reviewed their adjudication upon guilty pleas under the multiple offender statute.


OVERVIEW: Police officers were on routine patrol in a marked a car when they observed the car that defendants were in disregard a stop sign. When they pulled the car over, they saw one defendant throw something onto the floor, which the officers subsequently recognized as a bag of rock cocaine. Both defendants testified that the cocaine all belonged to one, but not the other, and a third person who was in the vehicle. Defendants were represented by the same counsel. On review, the court affirmed the conviction and found, inter alia, that defendants were not prejudiced by being represented by the same attorney, the officers lawfully seized the cocaine pursuant to the "plain view" exception to the warrant requirement. However, the court held that the trial court erred because it did not fully advise defendants of their rights at the multiple bill hearing. The transcript of the multiple offender proceeding established that the trial court did not advise either defendant of the right to remain silent, and other than the guilty pleas, nothing was presented in to link either defendant to the convictions evidenced by the certified copies of convictions the prosecution provided to the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions that the trial court entered on the drug charges, but it vacated the multiple offender adjudications and remand for further proceedings.

State v. Berry


No. 95 KA 1610


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1610 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/08/96); 684 So. 2d 439; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2689



November 8, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 10, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Livingston, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 10651. Honorable Bruce Bennett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED, REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Twenty-First Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Livingston (Louisiana), which convicted him of the aggravated rape and the murder of his estranged wife. Defendant argued 51 assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly raped his wife at knifepoint and then killed her the next day. The court found no merit in defendant's assignments of error. In particular, the trial court did not err in refusing to allow defendant to exhume his wife's body because speculation that viewing her skull could help determine the caliber of bullet that passed through it was not a sufficient reason for such a drastic measure. Demonstrative evidence was sufficiently identified to be admitted at trial where the sheriff had told the wife to bring her clothes and the knife with her when she filed charges; a witness had helped the wife pack the items in a bag; and the bag was eventually turned over, unaltered, to the sheriff's office. The jury could infer that the knife was the one used in the rape. The court did not err in excluding the responsive verdicts of simple rape and attempted simple rape because there was no evidence of any of the special circumstances enumerated in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43A(1), (2), or (3). Further, sexual battery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.1 was properly excluded as a responsive verdict because it only applied to a victim who was not the spouse of the offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for murder and aggravated rape, but the case was remanded to allow the trial court to correct the minute entry to reflect that defendant was to be given credit for any time served.

State v. Goodman

State v. Demouchet


No. 95-1554


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-1554 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/06/96); 684 So. 2d 21; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2648



November 6, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 5, 1996.
Post-conviction relief dismissed at State ex rel. Demouchet v. State, 872 So. 2d 1076, 2004 La. LEXIS 1609 (La., May 7, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF IBERIA; THE HONORABLE ANNE L. SIMON, DISTRICT JUDGE, PRESIDING. Lower Court Number: 95-202.
State v. Demouchet, 677 So. 2d 465, 1996 La. App. LEXIS 889 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 24, 1996)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), which sentenced defendant to 15 years at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by bill of information as a habitual offender, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The trial court found that defendant was a second habitual offender and sentenced defendant to 15 years at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. After reviewing the record, the court found that there was one error patent concerning defendant's habitual offender hearing. At the hearing, defendant admitted to the two convictions without being advised of his right to remain silent. However, the trial court did not rely solely on defendant's admissions to the two convictions, but also provided the testimony of defendant's probation officer, and the trial records from defendant's prior convictions. The court therefore concluded that the trial court's failure to comply with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(D)(1) was a harmless error and did not require a remand of the case. The court also found that the sentence was not excessive where it was in the mid-range proscribed under the habitual offender statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which sentenced defendant as a habitual offender.

Henderson v. Colonial Sugar Refinery


96-CA-380


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


96-380 (La. App. 5 Cir. 10/29/96); 683 So. 2d 873; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2611



October 29, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SIXTH DISTRICT COURT FOR THE OFFICE OF WORKER'S COMPENSATION. NUMBER 94-07936, DISTRICT 6. HONORABLE DELOS JOHNSON, JUDGE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant, by his widow, appealed from the judgment of a hearing officer in the Sixth District Court for the Office of Worker's Compensation (Louisiana), which found in favor of defendant employer and dismissed a workmen's compensation suit at the claimant's cost. The widow claimed that the hearing officer erred in finding that the claimant did not meet the burden of proof set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1021(7)(e).


OVERVIEW: The claimant died from a heart attack while training for a new position. Under § 23:1021(7)(e), a heart-related death was not considered a personal injury arising out of and in the course of employment and was not compensable unless clear and convincing evidence showed that the physical work stress was extraordinary and unusual in comparison to the stress or exertion experienced by the average employee in that occupation and that the physical work stress or exertion was the predominant cause of the death and not some other source of stress or preexisting condition. The new job was physically similar to the former job with a similar location temperature. His widow testified that it caused him more mental and emotional stress, but § 23:1021(7)(e) required that the stress be physical. The claimant collapsed while performing a task that he had performed many times over the previous three days. Finally, the testimonies of a cardiologist who examined the medical records and a pathologist who performed the autopsy indicated that preexisting blockages caused the death. The court found no manifest error in the trial court's conclusion that the claimant had not met the burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the employer in the claimant's suit for worker's compensation benefits.

 

573 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Gegenheimer v. Cajun Painting


No. 96-452


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-452 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/09/96); 689 So. 2d 457; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2361



October 9, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 8, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Office of Workers' Compensation, Parish of Evangeline, Honorable Sharon McCauley, Administrative Hearing Officer, Presiding. Lower Court Number: 94-04471.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a claimant's former attorney, sought review of a decision from the Office of Workers' Compensation, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), which dismissed his action against appellees, the claimant, his new attorney, the employer, and the attorney of the employer and the insurer, to recover his attorney's fees in a workers' compensation case.


OVERVIEW: One year after the former attorney's fees were approved in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1141, appellees entered into a settlement judgment that deprived the former attorney of his attorney's fee privilege. The former attorney was not notified about the settlement proceedings and did not participate. Although the court found that the settlement judgment was a violation of the former attorney's due process rights, the court concluded that it could not grant the former attorney's request to declare the judgment a nullity. The former attorney could not raise nullity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1272(B) because he was not a party to the settlement, and he was also prohibited from seeking the nullity of the settlement by the jurisprudence based on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 37:218(A), which governed his attorney's privilege. The court, however, determined that the former attorney stated a cause of action for an unjust enrichment claim against the employer and its insurer. Additionally, the former attorney's entitlement to attorney's fees from the claimant sprang from their employment contract and was unaffected by the settlement agreement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that dismissed the former attorney's action to recover his attorney's fees. The court remanded the action for further proceedings and for entry of a judgment in favor of the former attorney and against the employer and its insurer in the amount of the former attorney's approved fee.

State v. Harris


NUMBER Cr96-205


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-0205 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/09/96); 684 So. 2d 1; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2378



October 9, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry, State of Louisiana, Honorable Aaron Frank McGee, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 93-K-0842-B.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and sentenced her to 30 years at hard labor, the maximum sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by bill of information with one count of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1). Defendant claimed that the evidence, when viewed in the light most favorable to the prosecution, was insufficient to sustain a guilty verdict. Defendant also contended that the imposition of the maximum sentence was unconstitutionally excessive and that the reasons given for such a sentence were inadequate. The court found that the only issue contested by defendant was whether or not she intended to distribute the cocaine. Shortly after her arrest, defendant gave a statement to police that she intended to sell the drugs. The statement made by defendant was direct proof that she intended to sell the cocaine. The court also found that the maximum sentence was appropriate only in a case that involved the most serious violations of the subject offense and the most egregious and blameworthy offenders within the class. Although the trial court's factors indicated that defendant was involved in the drug trade, the court did not find that they placed defendant in the class of the most egregious offenders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and vacated the sentence imposed.

Louisiana Farms v. Louisiana Dep't of Wildlife & Fisheries


NUMBER 95-845


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


95-845 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/09/96); 685 So. 2d 1086; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2392



October 9, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 27, 1997. Released for Publication January 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of Concordia, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Leo Boothe, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 30,698.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Louisiana Department of Wildlife and Fisheries (DWF) and its agents, sought review of the decision of the Seventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of Concordia (Louisiana), which awarded punitive damages and attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and compensatory damages, including lost profits and mental anguish, that resulted from the constructive seizure of the alligator and catfish farms of appellee farmers.


OVERVIEW: During a search, pursuant to warrant, DWF agents discovered untagged alligators skins, in violation of of the La. Alligator Regs. R. F(7), H(1). In order to preserve the untagged skins, the DWF constructively seized the farmers' alligator and catfish farms on the advice of its attorney. As a result of the constructive seizure, the farmers filed for bankruptcy and sought damages. The lower court awarded the farmers punitive and compensatory damages, as well as attorney's fees. The court reversed the award of punitive damages and attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because neither the DWF nor its agents, acting in their official capacity, were "persons" under § 1983. Further, the individual agents were entitled to qualified immunity under § 1983 and to good faith immunity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:65(A) because the agents' actions were reasonable and they did not violate any clearly established legal rule. Moreover, the award of future loss profits for the catfish operation was improper when the farmers could operate that farm. The court affirmed the remaining awards because the extent and duration of the initially valid seizure ultimately made it unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's award of punitive damages, attorney's fees, and compensatory damages against the agents. The court also reversed the award of future loss profits on the catfish operation. The judgment was reformed in order to enter a dollar amount of all costs. In all other aspects, the lower court's judgment was affirmed, in favor of the farmers.

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT

PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 0461164, DIVISION "P". THE HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED, ANNULLED & SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which, in an action filed by the property owner against appellees, a parish and the parish's department of inspection, requesting that a writ of mandamus be directed to the parish ordering it to rescind its dismissal of a neighbor's building code violation, granted appellees' exception of no cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The property owner filed an action against the parish and the parish's department of inspection and code enforcement, requesting that a writ of mandamus be directed to the parish ordering it to rescind its dismissal of a neighbor's building code violation. The parish and the department of inspection and code enforcement filed an exception of no cause of action based on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 4773(D) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment was vacated and remanded.

State v. Lassere

October 1, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 94-167, DIVISION "A". THE HONORABLE MADELINE JASMINE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Fortieth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. John the Baptist (Louisiana), which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute more than 200 and less than 400 grams of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A and sentenced him as a second felony offender to 20 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: When police officers informed defendant that he was wanted on outstanding warrants, he fled and was subdued by three officers. While handcuffing defendant, an officer saw cocaine clutched in his hand and felt a bulge in his sleeve from which money spilled out. On appeal, the court affirmed that defendant's conviction of possession of cocaine with the intent to distribute under § 40:967A was supported by sufficient evidence that he possessed a large amount of cash and over 200 grams of cocaine, an amount that was inconsistent with personal use and had a high street value, which were seized incident to his warrantless arrest. Defendant waived the irregularity in the arraignment and was not prejudiced by counsel's failure to object to a charge that instructed on all elements of the crime. The court held that the multiple bill conviction was valid because the state produced a perfect transcript of his prior guilty plea. The court was prevented from amending the illegally lenient sentence that should have been imposed without parole because the state did not appeal. The court directed the trial court to inform defendant of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence and conviction of possession of cocaine. The court remanded, with instructions to send appropriate written notice to defendant of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief within 10 days and to file written proof that defendant received the notice.

Fragala v. Dubea (Succession of Fragala)


No. 28,663-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,663 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/27/96); 680 So. 2d 1345; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2191



September 27, 1996, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana. Probate No. 8526. Honorable John R. Joyce, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executrix sought review of the judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse (Louisiana), which sustained defendant forced heirs' exception of no cause of action and the dismissal of her petition for the possession of the estate of her late husband. The executrix contended that the recitals in the will were sufficient to effect disinherison under La. Const. art. XII, § 5 and La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493.


OVERVIEW: The decedent executed a will that named his second wife as the executrix and the sole beneficiary of his estate. He provided that, if the law recognized his children as forced heirs, he specifically disinherited them because they were cruel and grievously injured him. The court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2501, which abolished the forced heirship of persons over the age of 23, did not apply retroactively because to the decedent's will because: (1) he died prior to the statute's effective date; (2) his will treated his children as not forced heirs under former La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1493, which was unconstitutional; (3) the change was substantive; (4) the legislature did not set an earlier date for its application under La. Const. art. III, § 19; and (5) it became operative upon ratification under La. Const. art. XIII, § 3. Reversing the trial court's dismissal of the executrix's petition for possession, the court held that there could be a reduction of the donation to the executrix under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1502, if she was unable to prove grounds for disinherance under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1621.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a determination of whether the decedent effectively disinherited the forced heirs, or whether the decedent's donation of his entire estate to the executrix was subject to a reduction.

Farley v. State ex rel. Dep't of Transp. & Dev.


No. 96 CA 0538 CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 96 CA 0539

September 27, 1996, Decision rendered

PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 394,157 and 395,159. Honorable Joseph Keogh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED IN PART, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the state department of transportation, sought review of a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which sought review of damages awarded to plaintiffs, an injured victim and her children, in an automotive negligence suit.


OVERVIEW: The victim was involved in an auto accident with another driver. The victim was severely and permanently injured and scarred. Both the driver and the victim filed suit against the state department of transportation and development (DOTD). After a trial on liability, the victim was found to be 25 percent negligent, and the DOTD was found to be 75 percent negligent. The trial court awarded the victim $ 725,000 and awarded her four adult children $ 25,000 consortium damages each. The DOTD sought review contending that the awards were excessive. The court affirmed the victim's award, but reduced the consortium awards to $ 5,000. The court held that a trier of fact had great discretion in awarding damages, which should only be changed if such discretion were abused. The evidence did not support a finding that the children experienced any extreme psychological or emotional damage or loss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the $ 725,000 award to the victim, but reduced the award to the victim's children in the automotive negligence suit.

Lee v. State


96 CA 0108


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0108 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/27/96); 681 So. 2d 1020; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2203



September 27, 1996, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 411,981), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE JOSEPH F. KEOGH, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Public Safety and Corrections (Department) sought review of a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which entered a judgment permanently enjoining the Department from requiring a convicted sex offender to register as and give notice of such under the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:542 and 15:574.4(H).


OVERVIEW: The felon was convicted of molestation of a juvenile. Due to a prior conviction of indecent behaviour with a juvenile, he was sentenced as a habitual offender. The felon was released due to a diminution of his sentence based upon good time credit pursuant to La Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.5, which, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:571.5(A), was as if released on parole. A condition of release was that he register as a sex offender pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542 and give notification of his status under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(H). The felon filed suit and the trial court granted a permanent injunction enjoining the Department from requiring the registration or notice. The court affirmed as to the prohibition against the imposition of the § 15:542 requirements finding that because the felon's failure to register would expose him to additional penalties than that authorized for the crime when it was committed. The court reversed as to the prohibition against the imposition of the § 15:574.4(H) requirements because even though the statute became effective after the offenses were committed, it did not create a new offense for a sex offender's failure to comply.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed insofar as it prohibited the imposition of the La. Rev. Stat. § 15:542 sex offender registration requirements upon the felon. The judgment was reversed insofar as it prohibited the imposition of the La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(H) sex offender notification requirements upon the felon.

State v. Steward


NUMBER KA 95 1693


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1693 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/27/96); 681 So. 2d 1007; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2221



September 27, 1996, Judgment Rendered Appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 224,522. Honorable Martin E. Coady, Judge Presiding.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 1996.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana, which imposed concurrent sentences of 5 years at hard labor upon his conviction for attempted forcible rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42.1 and 12 years at hard labor upon his conviction for second-degree kidnapping in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted forcible rape and second-degree kidnapping after the victim identified him as the man who grabbed, punched, and threatened her and dragged her to a dark parking lot. The court held that defendant's specific intent to commit rape under § 14:42.1 was proven by sufficient evidence that he did not rob the victim but brutally beat her on the roadside at night, removed her pants, and dragged her to a dark area. The doctor's testimony, that the victim's abrasions were consistent with being dragged, was sufficient to prove that she was forcibly seized and carried from one place to another to constitute kidnapping under § 14:44.1. The court found that the trial court did not err in allowing the jury, during deliberations, to view a photograph depicting the nature and extent of the victim's injuries; allowing the victim to testify, based on her perception, that the attacker intended to rape her; denying a motion for a new trial and mistrial; and deviating from the sentencing guidelines. The court held that the kidnapping statute was not unconstitutionally vague and found no double jeopardy violation under the same evidence and elements tests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentences and convictions for attempted forcible rape and second-degree kidnapping.

 

582 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Milstead


NUMBER 95 KA 1983


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 1983 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/27/96); 681 So. 2d 1274; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2230



September 27, 1996, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 1-95-2822. Honorable Bonnie P. Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which sentenced him to five years at hard labor after he pleaded guilty to sexual molestation of a juvenile, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §14:81.2. He complained that the trial court sentenced him on a defective presentence investigation (PSI) report.


OVERVIEW: Defense counsel obtained a copy of the PSI on the morning of sentencing and admitted to looking at it only briefly. The trial court sentenced defendant and later denied his motion for reconsideration. Defendant contended that the omission of statements from defendant's psychologist, his mother, and his employer rendered the PSI defective. In affirming the judgment, the court acknowledged that such statements were properly part of the social history elements of a PSI, which under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 875(A)(1) the trial court could consider in sentencing. The court held, however, that failure to consider these statements did not void the sentence. The court also held that defendant failed to preserve his claim that the failure to provide the PSI to him until the morning of the sentencing hearing was error, because defendant had not objected to this at or before the hearing. The court also held that defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, noting that it was only one-third of the maximum statutory sentence, and that defendant exercised control and authority over the victim, his daughter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that sentenced defendant to five years hard labor for molestation of a juvenile.

 

583 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. McMooain


No. 95 KA 2103


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 2103 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/27/96); 680 So. 2d 1370; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2231



September 27, 1996, DECISION RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY. STATE OF LOUISIANA. TRIAL COURT NO. 230814. HONORABLE HILLARY J. CRAIN, JUDGE AD HOC PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of possession of a controlled dangerous substance, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C), and subsequently convicted defendant of possession of drug paraphernalia, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1033(C), on the basis of the same evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for a traffic offense. After a search of his person, a crack cocaine pipe was found, and defendant was arrested. Analysis of the residue in the crack pipe revealed the presence of cocaine. Defendant was charged by the city with possession of drug paraphernalia, to which defendant pleaded guilty. The state then charged defendant with possession of a controlled dangerous substance, namely cocaine, based on the residue in the pipe. Defendant eventually pleaded guilty, and was sentenced. Defendant filed a motion to quash the prosecution for possession of cocaine based on double jeopardy grounds and argued that his plea of guilty to the charge for possession of drug paraphernalia precluded the state from prosecuting him for possession of cocaine. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant appealed. The court reversed the conviction and held that under the Louisiana "same evidence" test, the two offenses were the same under a plea of double jeopardy. The presence of the residual crack cocaine served to prove both that defendant intended to possess drug paraphernalia and that the pipe was actually drug paraphernalia.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the conviction and sentence of defendant for possession of cocaine.

 

584 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Morgan v. Leach


No. 96 CA 0173


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96-0173 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/27/96); 680 So. 2d 1381; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2238



September 27, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 9511505 c/w 9530099. Honorable A. Clayton James, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED IN PART, AND AS AMENDED AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged a decision of the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which recognized appellee children as forced heirs and awarded them full ownership of one-half of the decedent's estate. The husband alleged that the trial court erred in finding that he was not entitled to a life usufruct over the forced portion of the decedent's estate without the necessity of posting bond.


OVERVIEW: Decedent died testate survived by her husband and two children from a prior marriage. She bequeathed to her husband the entirety of her estate in full ownership and named him testamentary executor. Decedent wrote her testament after the abolishment of forced heirship for all competent children over the age of 23. She failed to change her will after the law was declared unconstitutional and died before forced heirship was abolished. The children filed a petition to annul the probated testament. The trial court recognized them as forced heirs and awarded them full ownership of one-half of the estate. The court amended and affirmed, finding that it was decedent's intent that the husband be given the maximum permitted under the law. The court held that the maximum she could give under the law at the time without impinging on her children's legitime was a life usufruct over community and separate property. The court found that La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1502 only required a reduction to the point where the bequest no longer impinged upon the legitime; thus, the best way to effectuate the decedent's intent was to hold that the husband was entitled to a life usufruct over the forced portion.


OUTCOME: The part of the trial court's judgment awarding the children their forced portion in full ownership was amended to award them the naked ownership of their forced portion. The judgment was further amended to award the husband, in addition to the disposable portion in full ownership, an usufruct of the forced portion for life. The court remanded for a determination of the appropriate security required.

 

585 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Palmer v. Louisiana Forestry Comm'n


NUMBER 96 CA 0008


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


96 0008 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/27/96); 683 So. 2d 739; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2223



September 27, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Amended October 11, 1996. Rehearing Denied December 23, 1996. Released for Publication December 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 402,619. Honorable Bob D. Downing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state agencies and companies, filed an appeal from the decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which determined the action of the forestry and tax commissions exceeded their authority.


OVERVIEW: At issue in the severance tax case was whether a timber product known as "chip and saw" should be classified as "trees and timber" or "pulpwood" for purposes of assessing the proper state severance tax. The agencies changed the classification of chip and saw from pulpwood to trees and timber, effective January 1, 1994. Appellee taxpayer sought to have the reclassification overturned. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the taxpayer. Appellants challenged the decision. The court agreed with the trial court. The court found that the language in the original statute recognizing the distinction between pulpwood and timber by the measurements used, by the cord for pulpwood and by the 1,000 feet log scale for trees and timber, was applicable to the current statute. The general rule of interpretation was that provisions of an original act which were repeated in the body of an amendatory act, either in the same or equivalent words, were considered to be a continuation without change of the original law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which determined the action of the forestry and tax commissions exceeded their authority.

State v. Henton


No. 28,576-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,576 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/25/96); 682 So. 2d 777; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 2170



September 25, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Madison, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 68642. Honorable Charles R. Brackin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AFFIRMED AS AMENDED. REMANDED WITH ORDER. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the from the Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Madison (Louisiana), which convicted him of distribution of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A(1). Defendant attacked the sufficiency of the evidence to support the conviction and claimed that his sentence was unconstitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold crack cocaine to undercover officers who videotaped the transaction from a surveillance camera in their vehicle. In addition to playing the videotape for the jury the officers identified defendant in court. In affirming the conviction, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to convince a rational factfinder of defendant's guilt. The court found that the chain of custody of the rock of crack that defendant sold to the officers was proved beyond a reasonable doubt from the testimony of the officers regarding the safekeeping of the evidence and the limited access to it. The court also held that defendant had failed to preserve his claim that his sentence was excessive, because he had not filed a motion with the trial court for reconsideration of his sentence as required by La. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for distribution of cocaine and the sentence imposed for the offense.

 

587 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gonzales


No. 95-KA-0860


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0860 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/18/96); 680 So. 2d 1253; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1983



September 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 293-358, SECTION "A". HONORABLE MIRIAM G. WALTZER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of her conviction and sentence from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana). She was granted an appeal in 1983 after her conviction of simple possession of pentazocine and subsequently was adjudicated and sentenced as a multiple offender, but she escaped and was absent from Louisiana until 1993. She was returned to custody and filed a motion for the lodging of her appeal record, which was lost.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's appeal from her conviction was granted prior to her illegal escape from custody, whereby she was absent from Louisiana for 10 years. When she returned she sought to lodge her appeal, but her conviction was so old that the trial records, including the trial transcript, had been lost. Therefore the facts of the case were unknown to the court. Defendant urged that her constitutional right to appeal had been denied because the trial transcript was unavailable. She argued that, because she did not specifically waive her right of appeal, her appeal should have proceeded in her absence after it was granted. The court affirmed the judgment of her conviction and her adjudication and sentencing as a habitual offender, as her 10-year absence after her illegal escape constituted a waiver of her right of appeal. Also, the court opined that her prolonged absence after her escape made it impossible for the district court to notify her during the time that her appeal could not be lodged due to lost records, and thus she had waived such notice. The court declined to dismiss the appeal, although it viewed dismissal as a justifiable option.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of defendant's conviction for simple possession of pentazocine, and her adjudication and sentencing as a multiple offender.

 

588 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tucker


No. 95-KA-0030


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0030 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/18/96); 682 So. 2d 261; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1986



September 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused November 22, 1996. Released for Publication November 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH NO. 269-183, SECTION "D". HONORABLE FRANK A. MARULLO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section D (Louisiana). The trial court convicted defendant of two counts of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. On remand from the state supreme court, the trial court resentenced defendant on count one to 60 years at hard labor and sentenced defendant on count two as a multiple offender to 60 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: A jury found that defendant was guilty of two counts of armed robbery. The trial court resentenced defendant on remand from the state supreme court. The court affirmed. Because the full transcript of the evidentiary portion of the trial was made part of the appellate record, the absence of the jury instruction transcript did not deny defendant full appellate review. Defendant's claim that counsel was ineffective for failing to raise the issue of identification lacked merit; even if the issue had been raised, defendant's convictions would not have been reversed. The jury was well aware of the discrepancy in a victim's identifications at a photographic lineup and at a physical lineup, and the reliability of her positive identification of defendant at the physical lineup and at trial was for the jury to decide. The trial court's reimposition of a 60-year sentence was not excessive in light of defendant's conviction for another armed robbery committed in the same area and in a similar fashion. Because less than five years had elapsed between defendant's conviction for simple burglary and the present offenses, the state was not required to prove discharge from the prior offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for two counts of armed robbery.

 

589 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bastian


No. 96-K-0997


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0997 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/11/96); 681 So. 2d 420; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1948



September 11, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 31, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPLICATION FOR WRIT OF CERTIORARI AND PROHIBITION. CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. NO. 382-225, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED, MULTIPLE BILL SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought a writ of certiorari and prohibition requesting review of a decision of the Criminal District Court (Louisiana), which deviated from imposing a mandatory sentence of life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence on defendant who was a multiple offender and instead imposed a six year sentence at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: The State invoked the court's supervisory jurisdiction to review a multiple offender sentence. Specifically, the State argued that the trial court failed to state adequate reasons to support imposition of a six year sentence at hard labor for defendant who was convicted of a third felony offense, rather than the mandatory sentence of life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The defendant was convicted of forgery, and had previous convictions for unauthorized use of a movable and a simple robbery. The State argued that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:529.1 (A)(2)(b)(ii), 14:2(13)(y), and 14:72, the mandatory sentence was appropriate. Upon review, the court held that the district court properly justified the lower sentence by noting the nature of the past felony offenses. The court noted that the district court held that a sentence of life imprisonment would constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application for a writ of certiorari and prohibition, and affirmed the sentence given to defendant by the criminal district court.

 

590 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Haspel & Davis Milling & Planting Co. v. Board of Levee Comm'rs


No. 95-CA-0233


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0233 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/04/96); 680 So. 2d 159; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1936



September 4, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM 25th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PLAQUEMINES PARISH. NO. 31-357, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE MICHAEL E. KIRBY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: BREVERSED; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners appealed a judgment of the 25th Judicial District Court, Plaquemines Parish, No. 31-357, Division "A" (Louisiana), which maintained the exception of no cause of action filed by defendant Orleans Parish Levee Board (board), denied the owners' motion for a new trial, and dismissed their class action to require the return of royalties earned on the owners' expropriated property after the effective date of 1984 La. Acts 233 (act).


OVERVIEW: The board expropriated the owners' property as part of a spillway. Because the board obtained a restraining order against the enforcement of the act, which required it to return the property to the owners, applications for the transfer of title were not made available until 1987. The court held that the trial court erred in maintaining the board's exception of no cause of action to the owners' claim for monies representing revenues generated from their property after the effective date of the act and before the 1992 transfer of title and by denying their motion for a new trial. The court held that equity dictated that the board, whose attack on the constitutionality of the act delayed the availability of applications for years, should not have been allowed to benefit in revenues from its decision not to follow the legislative mandate. The court held that, under La. Const. art. VII, § 14(B)(4), the board had no right to the expropriated property and revenues generated during the application process after the effective date of the act, which was not repealed by its amendments and which declared that a public and necessary purpose for the expropriation no longer existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment maintaining the board's exception of no cause of action to the owners' action for royalties recovered by the board on their expropriated property.

State v. Page


No. 95-KA-2401


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-2401 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/21/96); 680 So. 2d 700; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1628



August 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 4, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 371-678, SECTION "J". HONORABLE LEON A. CANNIZZARO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which found him guilty of possession with intent to distribute marijuana and attempted possession of more than 200 but less than 400 grams of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and found guilty of possession with intent to distribute marijuana and attempted possession of more than 200 but less than 400 grams of cocaine. Defendant appealed both his conviction and his sentence. The court held that defendant was properly brought to trial on a valid bill of information. The court also determined that the police had reasonable suspicion to search defendant for an investigatory stop based upon the totality of the circumstances and that a magistrate correctly issued a search warrant after finding probable cause. In addition, the court stated that a police officer's testimony discussing defendant's alias was not an unambiguous reference to other crimes, and defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated because any delays in the trial was brought by the defense and the prosecution. Finally, the court concluded that defendant's sentence was not illegal or was cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which convicted defendant.

 

592 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Short v. Giffin


No. 96-CA-0361


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-0361 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/21/96); 682 So. 2d 249; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1629



August 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Refused November 22, 1996. Released for Publication November 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 90-19179, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GERALD P. FEDOROFF, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff clients filed suit against defendants, accountants, their firm, its insurer, and a partnership's sales representative, alleging several causes of action including accounting malpractice, violations of the Louisiana Blue Sky Laws, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:701 et seq., and breach of fiduciary duty. The clients appealed the decisions of the District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) granting summary judgment for the defendants.


OVERVIEW: An accountant of the firm recommended that the clients invest in a partnership to receive tax benefits after preparing their tax returns. The clients purchased an interest in the proposed partnership from the sales representative. Several years later, the Internal Revenue Service notified the clients that it was investigating the investment and then disallowed the tax benefits they claimed in connection with the partnership. The clients sought recovery after they were required to pay back taxes, plus penalties and interest. The defendants were awarded summary judgment based upon their argument that the claims were prescribed. Although both parties based their arguments regarding the malpractice claim on La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5604, the court held that the statute did not apply to the claim because the malpractice claim had prescribed prior to the enactment of the statute. The court held that the claims under the Louisiana Blue Sky Laws were also prescribed because it was filed more than two years after the sale of the partnership interest. The court found that there was no basis for suspending or interrupting the prescriptive periods and that there was no breach of fiduciary duty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court decisions finding that the clients failed to filed their times within the applicable prescriptive periods. Therefore, the court found that the grants of summary judgments in favor of the defendants were appropriate.

 

593 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


o. 28,516-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,516 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/21/96); 679 So. 2d 491; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1635



August 21, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 71,808. Honorable Cecil P. Campbell, II, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, which entered judgment on a jury verdict convicting him of unauthorized entry of a business in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.4 and sentenced him to six years at hard labor. The court granted defendant an out of time appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with simple burglary but a jury found him guilty of unauthorized entry of a business in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.4, a lesser included offense. On appeal, defendant claimed that the jury instruction providing that § 14:62.4 was a lesser included offense of simple burglary was error on the facts of the case and that his sentence was excessive. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence. Defendant's conviction was based on a break-in at a church, and he claimed that a church was not a business as contemplated in § 14:62.4. Under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 814(44), unauthorized entry of a place of business was a responsive verdict to simple burglary. The court held that a church was a place of business as contemplated in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.4, noting that churches had employees, offered services, paid bills, and sometimes sold products. The court further held that the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. It was within the range for second felony offenders pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and defendant had a long history of prior and pending offenses and a history of substance abuse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unauthorized entry of a business and the sentence of six years at hard labor.

 

594 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


State v. Douglas


No. 28,518-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


28,518 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/21/96); 679 So. 2d 469; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1642



August 21, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 168,012. Honorable Monty M. Wyche, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, claiming that the sentence of three years at hard labor for the offense of indecent behavior with a juvenile was excessive and showed little regard for the Louisiana Sentencing Guidelines.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with molestation of a juvenile arising from having sexual intercourse with his minor step-daughter on numerous occasions. He entered a plea of guilty to the offense of indecent behavior with a juvenile, a lesser included offense, and was sentenced to three years at hard labor, with credit for time served. On appeal, defendant claimed that the sentence was excessive and showed no regard for the Louisiana Sentencing Guidelines. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence. The record showed that the trial court properly considered the Louisiana Sentencing Guidelines but was within its discretion in rejecting them. The trial court determined that an upward deviation was warranted in light of defendant's position of authority over the victim and the numerous occurrences of the offense. The court also held that the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. Defendant had abused a position of trust and responsibility, repeatedly committed the criminal actions, was sentenced to less than half of the maximum sentence for the crime originally charged, and was not ordered to pay a fine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for indecent behavior with a juvenile and the sentence imposed as a result.
