Davis v. Carter


No. 96-CA-1706


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


96-1706 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/26/96); 677 So. 2d 1147; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1484



July 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 26, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. NO. 96-10868, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GERALD P. FEDOROFF, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, registered voters domiciled in the city of New Orleans, appealed an order of the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which maintained an exception of no cause of action filed by defendants, the members of the City Council of New Orleans, in the voters' action to force the Council to consider supplemental petitions for amendment of the city charter.


OVERVIEW: The voters were among the signatories to a petition which was submitted to the City Council calling for an amendment to the Home Rule Charter of the City of New Orleans. The voters submitted the petition for verification of the number of signatures. The voters then submitted two supplemental petitions to the Council, which refused to accept or consider the two supplemental petitions. The voters filed a petition seeking to compel the Council to consider the supplemental petitions as part of the original petition and further, to compel the registrar to inspect the signatures on the supplemental petitions for the purpose of verifying the number of registered voters. In response, the Council filed an exception of no cause of action on the grounds that plaintiffs were seeking the enforcement of an action that was purely discretionary. The trial court maintained the exception. On appeal the court held that for the purpose of amending the Charter, the City Council was not required to call an election in accordance with the procedure outlined La. Home Rule Charter §§ 9-201, 9-202 unless the registrar had certified the required number of signatures from a single petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that maintained the council members' exception of no cause of action.

State v. Cooper


NUMBER 96-119


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


96-119 (La.App. 3 Cir. 07/17/96); 678 So. 2d 59; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1380



July 17, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana, the Honorable Michael J. Johnson, District Judge, presiding. Lower Court Number: 95-73-765/95-75-578.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the 12th Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles, State of Louisiana, which convicted him of one count of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:64 and sentenced him as a fourth felony habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that, taking all of the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, a rational trier of fact could have found that the elements of the crime, including identity, were proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective. The court found that the State met its burden of proof regarding defendant's adjudication as a fourth habitual offender and that defendant did not present any affirmative evidence of a procedural irregularity or infringement of his rights at any of the prior guilty plea proceedings. The court also concluded that it could not say the sentence imposed on defendant was excessive based on the circumstances of the offense, defendant's prior record, and the likelihood of recidivism. The court found that the trial court erred in failing to give defendant credit for time served prior to the execution of the sentence, pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 882A. The case was remanded for amendment of the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and remanded to the trial court to amend the commitment and minute entry of the sentence to given defendant credit for time served.

State v. Bowman


No. 95-KA-0667


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


95-0667 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/10/96); 677 So. 2d 1094; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1378



July 10, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 367-198, SECTION "C". HONORABLE JEROME M. WINSBERG, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant minor sought review of a decision from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "C" (Louisiana), convicting him of manslaughter as the driver of a getaway car involved in a drive-by shooting and sentencing him to 33 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 16-year-old boy, contested his manslaughter conviction by a jury and the 33-year sentence imposed by the trial court. Defendant was driving a car whose passenger, his co-defendant, fatally shot the occupant of another car. On appeal, the court held that defendant acted as a principal in the crime, even though he was acquitted of a charge of second-degree murder and convicted of manslaughter instead. The prosecutor did not directly comment on defendant's failure to testify in contravention of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 770 by stating in closing arguments that defendant had been afforded "the right to take the stand." Any indirect reference to the defendant's failure to testify was harmless. The state was merely required to prove that defendant intended to frighten the victim rather than kill him in order to convict of manslaughter under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31. Although the maximum sentence imposed was harsh, the trial court weighed both aggravating and mitigating factors and did not abuse its discretion in holding that defendant was a "menace to society." The sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

598 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Varnado v. Department of Empl. & Training, Office of Workers' Compensation


No. 95 CA 0787


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 0787 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/28/96); 687 So. 2d 1013; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1405



June 28, 1996, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Rehearing Granted in Part and Denied in Part December 30, 1996, Reported at: 1996 La. App. LEXIS 3267. Released for Publication January 6, 1997. Rehearing of December 30, 1996, Reported at: 687 So. 2d 1013 at 1038.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 388,795. Honorable Robert Downing, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AND AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, employer and its director, sought review of the decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found in favor of plaintiff employees in their action for damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 stemming from their discharges from employment.


OVERVIEW: The employees brought several claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against the employer and its director based on their discharge of employment as the result of the director's search of their offices. The trial court found in favor of employees and awarded them damages but refused to reinstate them or to award them punitive damages. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the trial court erred in holding the employer liable for damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, but that the director met the "state action" requirement and was liable for damages. The court held that the record supported the trial court's conclusions that the director conducted an unlawful search of the employees' offices, desks, and filing cabinets. The court affirmed the trial court's decision that the director was not entitled to qualified immunity. The court held that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in its awards of damages to the employees for their lost wages, pain, and suffering, emotional and mental distress, attorneys' fees, and costs. The court held that the trial court properly refused to award punitive damages or to reinstate the employees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that employer was liable but affirmed in all other respects.

 

599 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


McKenzie v. Thomas


No. 95 CA 2226


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 2226 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/28/96); 678 So. 2d 42; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1442



June 28, 1996, JUDGMENT RENDERED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FAMILY COURT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 102,059. HONORABLE JENNIFER LUSE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Family Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which established his paternity and support obligation and awarded appellee mother attorney's fees. On appeal, he contended that the trial court erred in not finding La. Child. Code art. 240 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:399 unconstitutional, that mother failed to carry her burden of proof, and other errors.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a petition to establish defendant as the father of her minor child. Defendant admitted a sexual encounter with the mother, but denied paternity. After a trial, the trial court rendered a judgment declaring defendant as the father and ordered child support payments. The court affirmed. The court held that La. Child. Code art. 240 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:399 were constitutional. The court noted that while defendant objected to the blood testing procedure, he did not offer any evidence to support the alleged basis of any improper procedures used in the testing. The test results were admitted by certification. The court found no error in their admission. The court also found that the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's determination that defendant was the father of the minor child. The court also held that the trial court had the authority to make the support award retroactive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court and held that defendant was established as the father of the minor child. The court approved the retroactive child support award and the award of attorney's fees against defendant.

 

600 of 1113 DOCUMENTS


Kansas City S. Ry. v. Louisiana Tax Comm'n


No. 95 CA 2319


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


95 2319 (La. App. 1 Cir. 06/28/96); 676 So. 2d 812; 1996 La. App. LEXIS 1439



June 28, 1996, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 1996. Rehearing Denied August 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 402-730. Honorable Janice Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a decision from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), affirming the 1993 ad valorem property tax assessment of its Class II railroad by defendant Louisiana Tax Commission at $ 200,000,000.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a Class II railroad, contested the state tax commission's method of valuating ad valorem taxes on its operations, arguing that the valuation method unfairly penalized Class II railroads as opposed to Class I railroads. On appeal, the court held that the methods the commission used to determine the fair market value of the taxpayer's property violated the uniformity requirements of La. Const. art. VII, § 18, because the classifications "Class I" and "Class II" railroads were arbitrary and discriminatory. The classifications also violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The commission's method of valuation also impermissibly included intangible assets specifically exempted from ad valorem taxation by La. Const. Art. VII, §§ 18, 21, and the Railroad Revitalization and Regulatory Reform Act of 1976. Finally, the court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1709, the intangible property exemption statute, conflicted with La Const. art. VII, § 21, and was therefore invalid. However, the commission was not obliged to adopt the accounting methods or capitalization rate proposed by the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the commission's tax assessment of the taxpayer railroad and remanded for reassessment of ad valorem taxes for the year 1993.
